Miracles
intermediate
7 min
Could Miracles Be Trickery? A Classic Objection
A skeptic objects that miracles might be tricks, undermining their proof of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational objection that miracles could be achieved by trickery and why this challenge must be answered to establish prophethood.

Core Idea
Miracles are only proofs if they are beyond all human trickery.

This lesson presents a classic objection to the evidential value of miracles. If miracles could be the result of magic, juggling, or talismans, then they would not distinguish a true prophet from a fraudulent one. Imam Nasafi is citing this objection to show the importance of the challenge (tahaddi) that accompanies a true miracle.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that this is a hypothetical question from a skeptic.
The passage is a continuous objection, so take it in one go.
2
Identify the core doubt
The objector argues that miracles might be achieved by tricks (hiyal), magic, or natural abilities. Find the specific examples given.
Examples: pulling heavy object with silk, talismans, etc.
3
Understand the challenge it poses
This objection forces us to define what makes a miracle different from a trick. The answer requires that the miracle be accompanied by a challenge (tahaddi) and be beyond human capacity.
This lesson only covers the objection; the refutation is in later lessons.
4
Relate to the source context
Notice the reference to al-Mughni by Qadi Abd al-Jabbar. This shows that Nasafi is engaging with Mu'tazilite arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن سأل سائل فقال : إنما يتم جميع ما ذكرتموه في المعجزات متى بينتم أنه لا سبيل إلى الوصول إليها بحيل المحتالين، فأما إذا قيل إنها واقعة ممن ظهرت على يده كوقوع الجبل من المحتالين فمن أين أنها أدلة ؟ وكيف يصح لكم ذلك ؟ وقد رأيتم الحيل تظهر على وجه يختص بها قوم على قوم، كما يفعله المشعوذ والمُمَخرق.. وذلك مثل ما يفعله المحتال من جر الثقيل بالقز ومثل الآثار المعمولة بالطلسم، فما الأمان أن تكون المعجزات جارية هذا المجرى لكنها أبعد عن الأفهام؟.. ثم يجوز أن من ظهرت عليه معجزة اختص بلطيفة أو طبيعة أو ضرب من المعرفة والقدرة والآلة فتمكن من ذلك. راجع المغني لعبد الجبار جـ 15 ص 261.
If a questioner asks and says: All that you have mentioned regarding miracles is complete only when you show that there is no way to achieve them by the tricks of tricksters. But if it is said that they occur from the one on whose hand they appear, just as the mountain occurs from tricksters, then how are they proofs? And how is that correct for you? For you have seen tricks appear in a way that some people specialize in over others, like what the magician and the juggler do... And that is like what the trickster does in pulling a heavy object with silk, and like effects made by talismans. So what assurance is there that miracles are not of this kind, but are harder to understand?.. Furthermore, it is possible that the one upon whom a miracle appears is specialized in a subtlety, nature, or type of knowledge, power, and instrument, and so is able to do that. See al-Mughni by Abd al-Jabbar, vol. 15, p. 261.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a cited objection, likely from a Mu'tazili source (al-Mughni). It challenges the reliability of miracles as proofs of prophethood. The objector argues that miracles might be achieved through tricks (hiyal) like magic, juggling, or talismans. If so, they would not distinguish a true prophet from a pretender. The objector further suggests that the miracle worker might possess a special subtlety (latifa) or natural ability that enables the feat. The passage ends with a reference to Qadi Abd al-Jabbar's al-Mughni. This is a common objection in kalam, and Nasafi would need to respond that true miracles are beyond human capacity and come with a challenge (tahaddi).

Key Terms
معجزة
حيلة
محتال
مشعوذ
طلسم
دليل
تحدي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any impressive event can be a miracle that proves prophethood.
Correction: Miracles must be beyond all human capacity and accompanied by a challenge (tahaddi) to distinguish them from trickery.

Checkpoint
What is the main doubt raised in this objection about miracles?
A) That miracles are impossible.
B) That miracles might be achieved by trickery and thus not be reliable proofs.
C) That prophets cannot perform miracles.
D) That miracles are only for ancient times.

Key Takeaway
This objection shows why miracles must be clearly distinguished from trickery to serve as proofs of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the skeptic's claim that miracles could be mere tricks, does any doubt stir in your heart about the authenticity of the Prophet's miracles? What would it take for you to be utterly certain?
?
The objector suggests that a miracle worker might possess a hidden 'subtlety' or skill. Have you ever allowed yourself to think that perhaps the miracles of the prophets were just extraordinary human abilities? If so, what truth in your faith stands against that thought?
?
If you had to defend the proof of prophethood from miracles to a skeptic tomorrow, would you be able to refute this objection with conviction? If not, what do you need to learn or internalize to remove that hesitation?

Miracles
beginner
4 min
Two Types of Miracles
Divides miracles into two categories: unusual act and disabling from usual act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two categories of miracles as defined in Islamic theology: an unusual act and a disabling from a usual act, and why both are considered violations of custom.

Core Idea
Miracles are either an unusual act or a disabling from a usual act.

This short passage from Imam al-Nasafi classifies miracles into two distinct types. Understanding this division is fundamental to grasping how theologians define prophetic miracles as divine interventions that break the normal course of events. Let's see how the author explains each type and why both are considered violations of custom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then its literal translation. Notice the concise style and the two parts introduced by 'One of them...' and 'And the second...'.
The square brackets indicate a heading in the original text.
2
Identify the two types
Find the first type: 'an unusual act' (fiʿl ghayr muʿtād). Then find the second type: 'a disabling from the usual act' (taʿjīz ʿan al-fiʿl al-muʿtād). Write them down.
These two categories cover all miracles.
3
Understand the second type as violation
The passage explicitly states that the second type is also a violation of custom (naqḍ al-ʿāda). Reflect on why preventing a normal action is considered breaking the usual course of events.
Both types are therefore 'kharq al-ʿāda' (breaking of custom).
4
Apply the classification
Think of examples: bringing the dead to life is an unusual act; preventing a hand from harming is a disabling from a usual act. Which type would you classify each as?
This helps solidify the concept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[المعجز ينقسم إلى قسمين:] أحدهما: فعل غير معتاد. والثاني: تعجيز عن الفعل المعتاد، وهذا أيضا في الحقيقة نقض العادة إذ المنع عن المعتاد نقض للعادة وخروج عنها.
[The miracle is divided into two types:] One of them: an unusual act. And the second: a disabling from the usual act, and this also is in reality a violation of custom, for prevention from the customary is a violation of custom and a departure from it.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage classifies miracles into two types. The first is a 'non-customary act' (fiʿl ghayr muʿtād)—something that does not normally occur, such as bringing a dead person back to life. The second is a 'disabling from the customary act' (taʿjīz ʿan al-fiʿl al-muʿtād)—the prevention of a normally possible action, such as making a hand unable to grasp or a tongue unable to speak. The author notes that this second type is also truly a violation of custom (naqḍ al-ʿāda), because preventing what normally occurs is itself a departure from the usual course of events. Thus both types fall under the general category of 'violation of custom' (kharq al-ʿāda).

Key Terms
فعل غير معتاد (fiʿl ghayr muʿtād)
تعجيز (taʿjīz)
نقض العادة (naqḍ al-ʿāda)
قسم (qism)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think only the first type (unusual act) is a violation of custom, while the second type is just a normal prevention.
Correction: The passage clarifies that preventing a habitual act is equally a violation of custom, because the usual course of nature is thus interrupted.

Checkpoint
According to this classification, what is the second type of miracle?
A) An act that is impossible for God
B) A disabling from performing a usual act
C) A purely imaginary event
D) An act that violates logical necessity

Key Takeaway
Miracles are either an extraordinary act or an extraordinary prevention, and both are violations of the natural custom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think about a time in your life when you were prevented from doing something that would have led to harm. Before this lesson, did you see that as a miracle? Now that you know that disabling from a usual act is a type of miracle, how does that change your view of Allah’s protection in your daily life? Will you start recognizing these 'preventive miracles' and increase your gratitude?
?
If miracles are violations of the normal custom, what does that imply about your reliance on natural causes? Are you more focused on the means—like your health, wealth, or abilities—than on the One who upholds or suspends them? How can this lesson shift your trust from created causes to the Creator?

Miracles
intermediate
5 min
The Miracle Must Demonstrate Truthfulness, Not Falsehood
Nasafi explains two conditions for a valid miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that a miracle must manifest the truthfulness of its claimant; if it shows falsehood or is matched by an opponent, it ceases to be a proof of prophethood.

Core Idea
A miracle is defined by confirming truth, not by being supernatural.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla establishes a key condition for miracles: they must demonstrate the truthfulness of the prophet. The author argues that if a claimed miracle actually shows falsehood, it is not a miracle but a proof of lying. He also explains why the inability of the opponent to produce a similar act is essential for the miracle to retain its indicative force.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Notice how Nasafi presents two distinct conditions for a valid miracle.
The passage is dense; read slowly to grasp the logical flow.
2
Identify the two conditions
Find where Nasafi states that a miracle must show truthfulness (first condition) and that the opponent must be unable to produce a similar act (second condition).
The example of the tree illustrates the first condition.
3
Reflect on the logic
Consider why a miracle that shows falsehood cannot be a proof, and why a matched miracle loses its indicative power. This understanding is foundational for later discussions on prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما قدمنا بقولنا : لإظهار الصدق، فإنه لو ظهر لإظهار كذبه لا يكون معجزة. كما لو ادعى المتنبئ أن معجزته نطق هذه الشجرة فأنطق الله تعالى تلك بتكذيبه، لا يكون ذلك معجزة له ودليلاً لصدقه، بل يكون دليلاً على كذبه. وإنما قلنا مع نكول من يتحدى به عن معارضته بمثله، لأنه لو ظهر الناقض للمادة على يدي مدعي النبوة ثم ظهر مثله على يدي المتحدى به، لخرج عند المعارضة عن الدلالة إذ ذاك كذبه في دعواه وظهر له مثل دليله فصار دليلاً يدل على الشيء وضده، وما هذا سبيله لا يكون دليلاً.
And we introduced [the condition] with our statement: for the manifestation of truthfulness. For if it appears to manifest his falsehood, it would not be a miracle. Just as if the pretended prophet claims that his miracle is the speaking of this tree, and God makes it speak to deny him, that is not a miracle for him nor a proof of his truthfulness, but rather a proof of his falsehood. And we said [this] with the inability of the one challenged to oppose it with its like, because if the breaker of custom appears at the hand of the claimant of prophethood, and then its like appears at the hand of the one challenged, then upon opposition it would lose its indication, because then his falsehood in his claim would appear and his proof would be matched, so it becomes a proof that indicates both the thing and its opposite, and what is like this is not a proof.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage clarifies a condition of the miracle: it must manifest the truthfulness of the claimant. The author first states that if a miracle appears to manifest falsehood, it is not a miracle. He gives the example of a false prophet who claims that his miracle is that a tree will speak; if God makes the tree speak to deny him, that speech is not a miracle for him but rather evidence of his lie. The author then explains that we also require that the challenged opponent cannot produce something similar. If a similar act appears at the hand of the opponent, it would cancel the miracle's indicative force, because it would then point to both the truth and falsehood of the claim, which is not a valid proof.

Key Terms
معجزة
صدق
كذب
نكول
معارضة
الناقض للمادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any supernatural event qualifies as a miracle, regardless of its context or the truthfulness of the claimant.
Correction: A miracle is only valid if it demonstrates the truthfulness of the claimant. If it shows falsehood, it is not a miracle but a proof of lying.

Checkpoint
What happens if God creates an act that shows the falsehood of the claimant?
A) It is still a miracle.
B) It is not a miracle but a proof of falsehood.
C) It is a miracle but for the challenger.
D) It indicates nothing.

Key Takeaway
A miracle is only valid if it demonstrates the truthfulness of the claimant and the opponent cannot produce its like.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a sign or event as proof of someone's righteousness without checking if it truly confirms truth or could be matched? How does this lesson make you reconsider your criteria for spiritual proof?
?
When you present evidence for your faith, are you sure it is unique and undeniable, or do you rely on arguments that an opponent could easily match? What would it mean for your conviction if your proof were matched?
?
Think of a time you were convinced by a supernatural claim. Did you ask: 'Does this event truly manifest truthfulness, or could it be used to deceive?' How will you change your approach to testing claims of divine support after this lesson?

Miracles

The Two Types of Miracle
Classifies the miracle into two types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Islamic theology classifies miracles into two types: an unprecedented act (fi‘l ghayr mu‘tād) and incapacitation from a customary act (ta‘jīz ‘an al-fi‘l al-mu‘tād), and that both involve a breaking of custom.

Core Idea
Miracles break custom in two ways: doing the impossible or stopping the usual.

This short passage from Imam al-Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla establishes a key classification in the theology of miracles. Before we can discuss the purpose or conditions of miracles, we need to understand what a miracle is. The author gives a precise twofold definition that covers both extraordinary acts and extraordinary prevention.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two parts
Read the Arabic passage once through. Then read the translation. Notice that the author explicitly divides the miracle into two parts (qismayn).
2
Understand each type
The first type is 'a non-customary act' – something that never occurs in the normal course of events. The second type is 'incapacitation from the customary act' – preventing someone from performing an act that is normally within human power. Reflect on how these are different.
Both violate the customary order of nature.
3
Reflect on the common element
The author emphasizes that both types are in reality a breaking of custom ('naqd al-‘ādah'). Ask yourself: why is prevention also a breaking of custom?
This connects to the broader theological principle that miracles are divine interventions that suspend the usual laws.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المعجز ينقسم إلى قسمين: أحدهما: فعل غير معتاد. والثاني: تعجيز عن الفعل المعتاد، وهذا أيضا في الحقيقة نقض العادة إذ المنع عن المعتاد نقض للعادة وخروج عنها.
The miracle is divided into two parts: one of them: a non-customary act. And the second: incapacitation from the customary act, and this too in reality is a breaking of custom, because prevention from the customary is a breaking of custom and a departure from it.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage classifies the miracle. The author states that the miracle divides into two types. The first type is a 'non-customary act' (fi‘l ghayr mu‘tād) – something that never occurs in the normal course of events. The second type is 'incapacitation from the customary act' (ta‘jīz ‘an al-fi‘l al-mu‘tād), meaning that someone is prevented from performing an act that is normally within human power. The author emphasizes that this second type is also a breaking of custom, because preventing what is usual is itself a violation of the customary order.

Key Terms
معجز
فعل غير معتاد
تعجيز عن الفعل المعتاد
نقض العادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles only involve extraordinary acts like splitting the moon, not prevention of ordinary acts.
Correction: The text defines miracles to include both the performance of extraordinary acts and the prevention of ordinary acts, both of which break the customary order.

Checkpoint
How many types of miracle are there according to this passage?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The miracle (mu‘jizah) is defined in Islamic theology as either an unprecedented act or an incapacitation from a customary act, both of which constitute a breaking of God's customary order.

Miracles

5 min
How the Miracle Confirms the Prophet
Explains the mechanism and gives analogies showing miracle as divine confirmation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a miracle serves as divine confirmation of a prophet's truthfulness, through the mechanism of breaking customs and two illustrative analogies.

Core Idea
A miracle is God's unambiguous act confirming a prophet's claim.

The author explains the logical mechanism by which a miracle indicates the truthfulness of a prophet. He compares it to a human messenger proving his credentials through shared secret knowledge, and to a depositor proving his claim by handing over a ring. These analogies illustrate that the miracle is a direct, non-verbal confirmation from God, stronger than any speech.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the basic mechanism
Read how God hears the claimant, the miracle exceeds all human power, and when the prophet requests a sign and God performs it, that acts as divine confirmation.
Notice that it equates to God saying 'You have spoken the truth.'
2
Examine the first analogy
Consider the analogy of a human messenger who asks the sender to write a secret; the receiver knows only the sender could know it, thus confirming the messenger's truth.
This shows how a unique sign from the sender confirms the messenger.
3
Examine the second analogy
Reflect on the depositor asking for the ring; the act of handing it over is stronger than speech because speech can be deceptive but actions are unambiguous.
This underscores why the miracle is more powerful than verbal testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما وجه كيفية دلالتها على صدق الآتي بها، فإنا نعلم أن الله تعالى سامع لما يقوله هذا المدعي، وأن ما يظهر على يده خارج عن مقدور البشر بل عن مقدور جميع الخلق ولا قدرة عليه إلا الله تعالى، فإذا ادعى الرسالة، ثم قال آية صدق دعواي أن الله أرسلني أن يفعل الله كذا ففعل الله تعالى ذلك كان تصديقا من الله تعالى له فيما يدعي من الرسالة بما فعل من نقض المادة، فيكون ذلك كقوله عقيب دعواه هذه صدقت نظيره. وأن من أرسله غيره من البشر إلى آخر فقال الرسول للمرسل، اكتب لي شيئًا من الأسرار التي كانت بينك وبينه فكتب له، وعلم المرسل إليه أن لا إطلاع على تلك الأسرار لغير المرسل كان ذلك دلالة صادقة على صدق مدعي الرسالة. وكذا لو قال رجل لصاحب الوديعة بين يدي المودع، إن كنت صادقا فيما أدعى من أمرك إياي بأخذ وديعتك منك فناولني خاتمك فناوله كان ذلك دليلاً على صدقه، كما لو قال صدقت بل أبلغ إذ القول به يحتمل الاستهزاء وهذا مما لا احتمال فيه بوجه من الوجوه.
As for the manner of its indication of the truthfulness of the one who brings it, we know that God hears what this claimant says, and that what appears at his hand is beyond human capability, indeed beyond the capability of all creatures, and none has power over it except God. So when he claims prophethood, and then says, 'The sign of the truth of my claim that God has sent me is that God does such-and-such,' and God does that, then it is a confirmation from God of what he claims of prophethood, by what He did of breaking the custom. So that is like His saying after his claim, 'You have spoken the truth,' its analogy. And that if someone else sent him from among humans to another, and the messenger said to the sender, 'Write for me something of the secrets that were between you and him,' and he wrote for him, and the one sent to knew that there is no access to those secrets for other than the sender, that would be a truthful indication of the truthfulness of the claimant of the message. And likewise, if a man said to the owner of a deposit in the presence of the depositor, 'If you are truthful in what I claim of your order to me to take your deposit from you, then give me your ring,' and he gave it to him, that would be a proof of his truthfulness, just as if he had said, 'You have spoken the truth,' but rather more effectively, because speech can be subject to mockery, and this has no possibility of that in any way.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage explains the manner in which a miracle indicates the truthfulness of the prophet. The author begins by establishing that God hears the claimant and that the miracle is beyond all human power. When the prophet says, 'If I am truthful, let God do X,' and God does X, that is a divine confirmation, equivalent to God saying 'You have spoken the truth.' The first analogy is that of a human messenger who asks the sender to write a secret, and the receiver knows only the sender could know that secret, thus confirming the messenger's truth. The second analogy involves a depositor: if a man asks the owner to hand over a ring as proof of his claim, the act of handing over is stronger than words because words can be deceiving. Thus, the miracle is an unambiguous act from God that serves as clear testimony.

Key Terms
معجزة
دلالة
تصديق
نقض المادة
آية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the miracle itself is the proof, independent of God's action.
Correction: The text clarifies that the miracle indicates truthfulness because it is God's action of breaking custom, serving as His direct confirmation, not merely the event itself.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what makes the miracle a stronger proof than verbal confirmation?
A) It is more dramatic.
B) It cannot be subject to mockery or deception unlike speech.
C) It is performed by a human.
D) It is predictable.

Key Takeaway
A miracle is God's direct, unambiguous confirmation of a prophet's truthfulness, conveyed through an action that breaks custom and cannot be imitated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that a miracle is God's unambiguous confirmation of a prophet. If you were to face a situation where you desperately wanted a sign from God to guide you, would you recognize His action as a clear confirmation, or would you rationalize it away? What does that say about your faith?
?
The passage argues that God's action is stronger than words because words can be mocked. Are there areas in your life where you have settled for verbal assurances from God—like hearing a sermon or reading a verse—without letting them change your actions? How can you move from hearing to acting on God's confirmation?
?
If a miracle leaves no room for doubt, what does your doubt about the truth of Islam say about you? Is it because you haven't seen a miracle, or because you haven't truly accepted the miracle that is the Qur'an or the example of the Prophet? Commit to one concrete step to strengthen your certainty today.

The Moving Tree: How Miracles Confirm Prophethood
Nasafi compares a miracle to an angelic testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi uses the analogy of a moving tree to explain that miracles serve as direct divine confirmation of a prophet's truthfulness, equivalent to hearing an angel's testimony.

Core Idea
A miracle is like a visible angelic statement confirming the prophet's truth.

Imam Nasafi presents a powerful analogy to clarify how miracles function as objective evidence for prophethood. Just as a tree moving in response to a prophet's challenge convinces onlookers, a miracle is equivalent to hearing an angel directly affirm the prophet's message. This lesson unpacks the analogy and its theological significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp the narrative and analogy.
Notice the conditional structure: 'if the tree moves, then it is evidence.'
2
Identify the analogy's components
Break down the analogy: the prophet's claim, the challenge (moving tree as sign), the actual movement, and the comparison to angelic testimony.
3
Reflect on why the analogy is effective
Consider how the analogy elevates a miracle from a mere sign to an objective divine declaration, similar to a direct statement from an angel.
This connects to the broader concept of miracles as proof of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قصرك ليكون تحركها آية صدقي فتحركت الشجرة بمرأى من أهل البلدة عقيب هذا النداء، كان ذلك دليلاً على صدق مقالة الرسول، وكان بمنزلة ما لو سمعوا من الملك أن قال للرسول: صدقت فيما أدعيت من رسالتي، أو قال لأهل البلدة: إنه صادق فيما بلغ إليكم من رسالتي، فكذا هذا.
Your palace, so that its movement would be a sign of my truthfulness. Then the tree moved in the sight of the people of the town after this call. That was evidence for the truthfulness of the messenger's statement, and it was analogous to if they heard from the angel that he said to the messenger: 'You have spoken the truth in what you claimed of your message,' or said to the people of the town: 'He is truthful in what he conveyed to you of my message.' So this is like that.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage presents an analogy to explain how a miracle serves as divine confirmation of a prophet's truthfulness. The scenario: a person claims prophethood and says, 'Your palace, so that its movement would be a sign of my truthfulness.' Then the tree moves visibly before the townspeople. This movement is evidence of the truth of the messenger's claim. It is equivalent to the people directly hearing an angel say to the messenger, 'You have spoken the truth,' or say to the people, 'He is truthful.' Thus, the miracle functions as a direct divine testimony.

Misconception: Some might think the analogy implies the miracle is merely a subjective sign.
Correction: The author insists it is objective evidence like a direct angelic statement.

Checkpoint
What does the movement of the tree in the analogy represent?
A) A natural occurrence
B) A sign of the person's power
C) A divine confirmation of the prophet's truthfulness
D) A trick by the townspeople

Key Takeaway
The moving tree analogy teaches that a miracle is as clear a proof of prophethood as hearing an angel directly confirm the messenger.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The townspeople in the analogy saw the tree move and had no excuse. You have the Quran, the final miracle, as your evidence. Have you treated it with the same certainty as if you heard an angel speak? Or has familiarity dulled your conviction?

What is one specific action you will take to respond to that truth?

The Maturidi Argument Against Miracles for False Prophets
Nasafi states a general principle and expounds the Maturidi rational proof for the impossibility of miracles for false prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the general epistemological principle about miracles after a claim of prophethood and the specific Maturidi rational argument for why such miracles are impossible for false prophets.

Core Idea
Miracles are God's stamp of approval; allowing them on a liar would destroy the distinction between truth and falsehood.

Imam Nasafi begins by establishing a foundational principle: when a miracle occurs after someone claims prophethood, we know with certainty that God is the agent because no one else can produce it. This miracle is God's affirmation of the claimant's truthfulness. Consequently, it is impossible for such a miracle to occur at the hands of a false prophet. However, the theologians disagreed on the precise reason for this impossibility. Nasafi then presents the Maturidi explanation, which focuses on the devastating consequences that would follow if miracles were not exclusive to true prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the flow from the general principle to the specific argument.
The passage has two clear sections: the principle and the Maturidi argument.
2
Identify the two main parts
Mark where the shift occurs: from 'ثم ظهور' to 'ممتنع' is the principle, and from 'واختلف' to the end is the Maturidi argument.
3
Grasp the key concept of 'equivalence'
The Maturidi argument hinges on the idea that a miracle on a false prophet would create equivalence (تسوية) between truth and falsehood. Understand why that would block the path to truth.
This is central to the proof.
4
Contrast with the religious pretender
Notice the contrast between a false prophet (متنبئ) and a religious pretender (متأله) who does not claim prophethood. Why is a miracle possible for the latter?
This contrast clarifies the argument.
5
Reflect on the rational basis
Ask yourself: Why does the Maturidi view rely on reason alone to derive ethical categories (حكمة, قبيح, etc.)? How does that connect to the argument?
This ties into broader Maturidi epistemology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ظهور الناقض للعادة عقيب دعوى الملك للرسالة، يوجب العلم يقينا أن الله تعالى هو الذي فعل ذلك إذ لا قدرة لغيره على مثل ذلك الفعل، ثم ذلك منه تصديق له فيدل ذلك على صدقه لا محالة، ثم ظهور مثله على يدي الكاذب في دعوى الرسالة ممتنع. واختلف المتكلمون في وجه امتناعه فقال من قال من أصحابنا باستدراك الحكمة والسفه والقبيح والحسن بمجرد العقول أن جهة امتناعه أنه لو ظهر ذلك على يد المتنبي، ولا دليل على صدق النبي إلا هذا لكان فيه التسوية بين الصادق والكاذب والحق والباطل، وسد طريق الوصول إلى الحق أصلا وذا خارج من الحكمة، حتى إن ظهور ناقض العادة على يدي المتأله لما لم يكن سادًا طريق الوصول إلى الحق، ولا موجبًا التسوية بين الحق والباطل والمحق والمبطل لما في شخصه عن أمارات الحدوث، ودلائل كونه كاذبا في دعواه كان ذلك ممكنا ممتنع بخلاف المتنبئ فإنه ليس في ذاته ما يدل على كذبه إذ هو من جوهر صادق في الدعوى لا فرق بينهما من حيث الذات فلا فرقان بينهما إلا من جهة المعجزة الناقضة للعادة فكان في ظهورها على يدي الكاذب ما مر من التسوية بين الحق والباطل وسد طريق الوصول إلى الحق.
Then the appearance of the contravention of custom after the claim of the angel (or king) for prophethood necessitates certain knowledge that God Almighty is the one who did that, since no one else has power over such an action. Then that from Him is an affirmation of him, so it indicates his truthfulness without doubt. Then the appearance of the like of it at the hands of a liar in his claim of prophethood is impossible. And the mutakallimun differed about the reason for its impossibility. Those among our companions who derive wisdom and foolishness and evil and good solely from reason said: the reason for its impossibility is that if it appeared at the hands of the false prophet, and there is no evidence for the truthfulness of the prophet except this, then there would be in it equivalence between the truthful and the liar, and between truth and falsehood, and blocking of the path to reaching truth entirely, and that is outside of wisdom. So much so that the appearance of a contravention of custom at the hands of a religious pretender (mutā'allih) – since it was not blocking the path to reaching truth, nor causing equivalence between truth and falsehood and the righteous and the false, because in his person there are signs of temporality and proofs that he is a liar in his claim – that was possible, not impossible, unlike the false prophet, for in his essence there is nothing that indicates his falsehood, since he is of the same substance as the truthful in the claim, with no difference between them in terms of essence. So there is no distinction between them except by way of the miracle that contravenes custom. Thus, in its appearance at the hands of the liar there is what was mentioned of equivalence between truth and falsehood and blocking of the path to reaching truth.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage first establishes a general principle: a miracle occurring after a claim of prophethood necessitates certain knowledge that God is its agent, because no one else can produce such an act. This miracle is God's affirmation of the claimant, proving his truthfulness. Therefore, its appearance at the hands of a liar is impossible. Then the author mentions that the mutakallimun disagreed on the precise reason (wajh al-Imtinā‘) for this impossibility. The Maturidi view (from those among ‘our companions’ who derive ethical categories like wisdom, foolishness, good, and evil from reason alone) is: if a miracle appeared at the hands of a false prophet (al-mutanabbī), and there were no other evidence for the truthfulness of the true prophet, this would create equivalence between truth and falsehood and block the path to truth, which is contrary to divine wisdom. The argument is clarified by contrast with a religious pretender (al-mutā‘allih) – someone who makes claims of piety but not prophethood. For such a person, his own signs of contingent existence and other indicators show his falsehood, so a miracle at his hands does not cause the same problem. But a claimant to prophethood has no inherent sign of falsehood, since his essence is the same as a true prophet. Thus, without a miracle, there would be no distinction, so a miracle on a false prophet would destroy the very purpose of miracles, leading to an absurd consequence that is outside wisdom.

Key Terms
ناقض العادة
دعوى الرسالة
تصديق
حكمة
سفه
قبيح
حسن
متنبئ
متأله
امتناع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The impossibility of a miracle for a false prophet is because a miracle is inherently incompatible with falsehood by its nature.
Correction: The Maturidi argument does not rely on an inherent incompatibility; rather, it argues that if a miracle appeared on a false prophet, it would cause equivalence between truth and falsehood and block the path to truth, which is contrary to divine wisdom. Thus, the impossibility is based on rational necessity (consequence), not on the nature of the miracle itself.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidi view, what would be the consequence if a miracle appeared at the hands of a false prophet?
A) People would embrace the false prophet
B) It would create equivalence between truth and falsehood and block access to truth
C) The miracle would be less powerful
D) God would be proven unjust

Key Takeaway
Miracles are God's exclusive endorsement of true prophets; allowing them for false claimants would nullify the very purpose of divine guidance by making truth and falsehood indistinguishable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that God blocks any equivalence between truth and falsehood. In what areas of your life have you allowed a comfortable equivalence between the two, and what specific step will you take today to remove it?
?
The passage says a false prophet has no inherent sign of falsehood—only the miracle distinguishes him. If you were to be tested by a charismatic teacher who performs extraordinary acts, what criteria from this lesson would you use to judge his truthfulness? Write down one concrete action you will take this week to verify that your spiritual guides are backed by God's clear signs.
?
When the mutā'allih mistakes the scholar for a prophet, his claims collapse because of inherent signs. Examine your own heart: Are there any claims you make about your faith or piety that collapse under the weight of your own actions? Commit to one small change that brings your outward claim into alignment with your inward reality.

The Ash'ari Argument on Miracles for False Prophets
Imam Nasafi presents the Ash'ari view on miracles for false prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash‘ari argument for why miracles cannot appear on false prophets and how it differs from other views.

Core Idea
A miracle on a liar would make God unable to prove truth, so it's impossible.

Imam Nasafi presents a distinct Ash‘ari argument for the impossibility of miracles at the hands of false prophets. Unlike other schools that base this on divine wisdom, the Ash‘arites ground it on the consequence of incapacitating God. This passage explains their reasoning and a notable exception. Let’s examine the text.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the dense phrasing and the key terms listed.
Pay attention to the definition of 'foolishness' and the structure of the argument.
2
Identify the core consequence
The argument hinges on the consequence that a miracle on a liar would necessitate God's inability (ta'jiz) to establish proofs for the truthful prophet. Understand why this consequence is deemed impossible.
3
Contrast with the exception
The passage ends with the case of a mutā'allih (religious pretender). See why the same impossibility does not apply here due to inherent signs of falsehood.
This exception reinforces the logic of the main argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذهب جمهور الأشعرية ومن قال من متكلمي أهل الحديث : إنه لا سفه إلا ما ورد عنه النهي، إلى أن جهة امتناع ظهور الناقض للعادة على يدي مدعي الرسالة كاذبًا ، أن ظهوره على يديه يوجب تعجيز الباري جلا وعلا عن إقامة الدلائل على صدق الصادق في دعوى الرسالة، وإثبات التفرقة بين الحق والباطل، وتعجيز الباري جل وعلا محال، حتى إن إظهار ذلك على يدي المتأله لما لم يكن موجبًا تعجيزه جل وعلا عن ذلك لما في شخص المدعي ما يدل على كذبه لم يكن ذلك ممتنعا.
And the majority of the Ash‘arites and those who said among the mutakallimun of the people of hadith – that there is no foolishness except what prohibition came concerning it – went to the view that the reason for the impossibility of the appearance of the contravention of custom at the hands of a claimant of prophethood who is a liar is that its appearance at his hands necessitates incapacitating the Creator, majestic and exalted, from establishing proofs for the truthfulness of the truthful one in his claim of prophethood, and establishing the distinction between truth and falsehood; and incapacitating the Creator, majestic and exalted, is impossible. So much so that the manifestation of that at the hands of a religious pretender – since it was not necessitating His incapacitation, majestic and exalted, from that, because in the person of the claimant there is something that indicates his falsehood – that was not impossible.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage presents the Ash‘ari argument for the impossibility of miracles at the hands of false prophets. The Ash‘arites, along with some mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith, hold that there is no ethical category of 'foolishness' except what is prohibited by revelation (i.e., ethics are revealed, not rational). Their argument: if a miracle appeared at the hands of a liar claiming prophethood, this would necessitate that God is unable to establish proofs for the truthful prophet and to differentiate between truth and falsehood. But incapacitating God is impossible. Therefore, such a miracle cannot occur. The argument is contrasted with the case of a 'mutā'allih' (a religious pretender not claiming prophethood). Since there are inherent signs in the pretender's person that indicate his falsehood (e.g., he does not bring miracles, or his claims are inconsistent), a miracle at his hands does not imply God's inability, so it is not impossible.

Key Terms
جمهور الأشعرية
سفه
تعجيز الباري
إقامة الدلائل
تفرقة بين الحق والباطل
متأله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ash‘ari argument is identical to the Maturidi argument.
Correction: The Ash‘ari argument focuses on divine power (incapacitation), while the Maturidi focuses on divine wisdom and ethical categories (foolishness).

Checkpoint
According to the Ash‘ari argument, why is a miracle impossible on a false prophet?
A) Because it would be contrary to wisdom
B) Because it would imply God's inability to distinguish truth from falsehood
C) Because miracles are intrinsically tied to truth
D) Because people would not believe

Key Takeaway
The Ash‘arites argue that a miracle on a false prophet would imply God's inability to distinguish truth from falsehood, which is impossible, so such a miracle cannot occur; however, this does not apply to a pretender with inherent signs of falsehood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Have you ever been in a situation where you doubted whether something was a sign of truth or just coincidence? How does this lesson's emphasis on God's power to distinguish truth from falsehood challenge your tendency to rely on your own judgment? What would it look like to actively seek God's clarity instead?
?
This lesson teaches that God cannot be incapacitated. How does the absolute assurance of God's power affect your trust in His guidance? Are you living as if God is able to make truth clear to you? What step can you take this week to rely more on His proofs than on your own logic?
?
The Ash'aris argue that miracles on false prophets are impossible because they would blur truth and falsehood. How does this deepen your certainty about the finality of prophethood in Islam? Does it compel you to examine how you treat the clear proofs of the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ? What is one practical way you will honor that clarity today?

Miracle as Intrinsic Sign of Truth
Nasafi presents the Ahl al-Hadith view on miracle as intrinsic sign of truth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument from some Ahl al-Hadith that a miracle is intrinsically a sign of truth and cannot accompany falsehood, using the analogy of a perfectly crafted action as a sign of knowledge.

Core Idea
A miracle is intrinsically a sign of truth; it cannot be paired with falsehood.

This argument from some mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith offers a straightforward view: miracles are not just signs, but they are essentially signs of truth. The author uses a clear analogy to explain why a miracle cannot appear from a false prophet. As you read, consider how this reasoning differs from other arguments about miracles.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to get a sense of its structure and key terms. Note that it begins with 'وقال بعض متكلمي أهل الحديث'.
The passage is concise; savor each word.
2
Identify the core claim
After reading the translation, identify the main claim: a miracle is intrinsically a sign of truth. Notice the phrase 'لعينها' (by its very essence).
This is the key premise.
3
Analyze the analogy
Examine the analogy: a perfectly crafted action (الفعل المحكم) is intrinsically a sign of knowledge, so it cannot be paired with ignorance. Similarly, a miracle cannot be paired with falsehood. Consider why this analogy is apt.
4
Consider potential objections
Think about possible objections: Is this argument circular? Does it assume what it tries to prove? Reflecting on this will deepen your understanding.
Objections are not in the passage, but thinking critically helps.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال بعض متكلمي أهل الحديث : أن جهة امتناع ذلك أن المعجزة دلالة الصدق لعينها ، فلا يجوز وجودها مع غير الصدق كالفعل المحكم دلالة العلم لعينه فلم يجز اقترانه بالجهل فكذا هذا.
And some mutakallimun of the people of hadith said: the reason for its impossibility is that the miracle is an indication of truth by its very essence, so its existence with other than truth is not permissible, just as the perfectly crafted action is an indication of knowledge by its very essence, so its association with ignorance is not permissible. So this is like that.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage presents a third argument from some mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith. Their view is simpler: a miracle (mu‘jizah) is intrinsically (li-‘aynihā) a sign of truth; therefore, it cannot be found together with falsehood. They draw an analogy with a perfectly crafted action (al-fi‘l al-muḥkam): such an action is intrinsically evidence of knowledge (since only a knowledgeable agent could produce it), so it cannot be associated with ignorance. Likewise, a miracle is intrinsically evidence of truth, so it cannot accompany falsehood. Thus, a miracle cannot appear at the hands of a liar claiming prophethood.

Key Terms
معجزة
دلالة الصدق
فعل محكم
علم
جهل
اقتران

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A miracle is like a word that cannot be both true and false
B) A perfectly crafted action is evidence of knowledge and cannot be associated with ignorance
C) A miracle is like a lion that cannot be both alive and dead
D) A false prophet cannot speak Arabic

Key Takeaway
A miracle is intrinsically a sign of truth and cannot be associated with falsehood, just as a perfectly crafted action is intrinsically a sign of knowledge and cannot be associated with ignorance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to love truth, but when was the last time you chose falsehood to protect your reputation or avoid conflict? If a miracle cannot exist with falsehood, what does that say about the truthfulness of your own actions? Where in your life today will you make a concrete commitment to truth, even if it costs you?
?
The analogy compares a perfectly crafted action to a miracle as signs of knowledge and truth respectively. Look at your own daily actions—prayer, speech, work. Are they 'perfectly crafted' in the sense of reflecting true inner faith, or are they just outward shows? Will you ask Allah to purify your intentions so your actions become true signs of the knowledge you profess?
?
Allah has given you countless signs of His truth—Qur'an, creation, your own existence. Yet how often do you treat these signs as just background noise? If a miracle is intrinsically a sign of truth, then every blessing is a call to recognize that truth. What sign have you ignored today, and what is your repentance for that neglect? Name one blessing you will actively try to see as a sign of truth starting tomorrow.

Why Miracles Cannot Appear on False Prophets: Two Scholarly Views
Imam Nasafi reports two views on why miracles cannot appear on false claimants and states the verified position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main theological arguments for why miracles cannot accompany false claimants of prophethood, and which view is considered verified among the scholars.

Core Idea
Miracles cannot appear on false prophets because that would undermine God's ability to distinguish truth from falsehood.

This passage from Imam Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla presents a critical debate in Islamic theology: how do we know that miracles only occur at the hands of true prophets? Two distinct arguments are given, one based on God's wisdom and the impossibility of attributing incapacity to Him, the other on the inherent nature of miracles as signs of truth. We will explore both and see which view the verified scholars uphold.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the author's own words set the stage.
Notice the technical terms: الناقض للعادة, تعجيز, دلالة الصدق.
2
Identify the two views
The passage presents two distinct groups with different arguments. Locate where each view begins and ends.
The first view is introduced by 'وذهب جمهور الأشعرية...', the second by 'وقال بعض متكلمي أهل الحديث...'.
3
Understand the first view: the consequence argument
The first view argues that a miracle on a false prophet would necessitate attributing incapacity (ta'jiz) to God in establishing evidence for truth. Reflect on why that would be impossible.
This view also discusses a hypothetical case of a claimant to divinity, where the appearance of a miracle is not impossible because the claimant's claim indicates falsehood.
4
Understand the second view: the essence argument
The second view argues that a miracle is inherently a sign of truthfulness, so it cannot coexist with falsehood, just as a perfect act cannot coexist with ignorance.
This is a more direct, self-evident argument based on the definition of a miracle.
5
Note the author's conclusion
Imam Nasafi states that the verified scholars (al-muhaqqiqun) adopt the first view. Consider the implications for theological reasoning.
The author does not elaborate on why the first view is preferred, but the lesson invites reflection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذهب جمهور الأشعرية ومن قال من متكلمي أهل الحديث : إنه لا سفه إلا ما ورد عنه النهي، إلى أن جهة امتناع ظهور الناقض للعادة على يدي مدعي الرسالة كاذبًا، أن ظهوره على يديه يوجب تعجيز الباري جلا وعلا عن إقامة الدلائل على صدق الصادق في دعوى الرسالة، وإثبات التفرقة بين الحق والباطل، وتعجيز الباري جل وعلا محال، حتى إن إظهار ذلك على يدي المتأله لما لم يكن موجبًا تعجيزه جل وعلا عن ذلك لما في شخص المدعي ما يدل على كذبه لم يكن ذلك ممتنعا. وقال بعض متكلمي أهل الحديث : أن جهة امتناع ذلك أن المعجزة دلالة الصدق لعينها ، فلا يجوز وجودها مع غير الصدق كالفعل المحكم دلالة العلم لعينه فلم يجز اقترانه بالجهل فكذا هذا. والمحققون منهم على الوجه الأول، والله الموفق.
And the majority of the Ash'aris and those who said from the mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith: 'There is no foolishness except what the prohibition came about,' that the aspect of the impossibility of the appearance of the breaker of custom at the hands of a false claimant of prophethood is that its appearance at his hands would necessitate attributing incapacity to Allah, Majestic and Exalted, to establish evidences for the truthfulness of the truthful in the claim of prophethood, and to establish distinction between truth and falsehood. And attributing incapacity to Allah, Majestic and Exalted, is impossible. However, if the appearance of that at the hands of the one who claims divinity did not necessitate attributing incapacity to Him, Majestic and Exalted, because of what is in the person of the claimant that indicates his lie, then it is not impossible. And some mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith said: 'The aspect of its impossibility is that the miracle is a sign of truthfulness in its essence, so its existence with other than truthfulness is not permissible, just as the perfect act is a sign of knowledge in its essence, so its conjunction with ignorance is not permissible; thus this is similar.' And the verified scholars among them are upon the first view, and Allah is the Granter of success.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage reports two views on why it is impossible for a miracle (the breaking of customary laws) to appear at the hands of a false claimant to prophethood. It then states the view preferred by the verified scholars. The first view, held by the majority of Ash'aris and some mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith, argues that the impossibility stems from the fact that if such a miracle appeared on a false claimant, it would necessitate attributing incapacity (ta'jiz) to Allah, because Allah would then fail to provide clear distinguishing evidence between truth and falsehood. However, if the false claimant bears some indicator of his lie (e.g., open contradiction or known falsehood), then the miracle is not impossible — it is the absence of such an indicator that ensures the miracle only accompanies truth. The second view, held by some mutakallimun of Ahl al-Hadith, argues that the miracle is in its very essence a sign of truthfulness, so it cannot coexist with falsehood any more than perfect skillful action can coexist with ignorance. This is a self-evident impossibility, not dependent on consequences. The author then notes that the verified scholars (al-muhaqqiqun) among them adopt the first view, and Allah is the Granter of success.

Key Terms
المعجزة
الناقض للعادة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The impossibility of miracles on false prophets is solely due to the inherent nature of miracles as signs of truth.
Correction: While the second view argues that, the first view (adopted by verified scholars) emphasizes that the impossibility also preserves God's ability to provide clear evidence distinguishing truth from falsehood.

Checkpoint

A) Because miracles are inherently signs of truth and cannot coexist with falsehood.
B) Because it would necessitate attributing incapacity to God to provide evidence for the truthful.
C) Because false claimants are always known to be liars by their character.
D) Because miracles only appear at the hands of prophets by consensus.

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of miracles on false prophets is primarily based on the need to preserve God's ability to provide clear evidence distinguishing truth from falsehood, as upheld by the verified scholars.

Miracles as Proof of Prophethood
The author defines miracles as evidence for prophethood and lists prophetic miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that miracles (mu'jizat) that break natural habits serve as the definitive proof of a prophet's truthfulness, and you will be able to identify several examples from various prophets.

Core Idea
Miracles that break natural laws are the primary evidence for prophethood.

In this passage, the author establishes the central proof for the authenticity of a prophet's claim: the performance of miracles that defy the normal course of nature. These miracles are not just extraordinary events; they are specifically designated as 'nawāqid al-ʻādāt' — that which breaks customary occurrences. The author then provides a rich list of examples from the lives of major prophets, illustrating how each miracle served as a sign of their prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author first states the general principle, then provides a list of examples.
2
Identify the key term
Identify the key term 'المعجزات الناقضات للعادات' and understand its meaning: miracles that break customary habits.
3
Reflect on the examples
Go through each example in the list. Ask yourself how each miracle breaks a natural law and which prophet it is associated with.
The examples span from Prophet Salih to Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon them).
4
Consider the logical implication
These miracles are not merely wonders; they are proofs of truthfulness. Understand how they serve as evidence for the claim of prophethood.
The author mentions that this is based on the previously explained manner of implication.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to see if you grasped the main point of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الدليل على ثبوت الرسالة لبعض الرسل على التعيين ظهور المعجزات الناقضات للعادات على أيدي كثير منهم كخروج الناقة من الصخر، وصيرورة النار بردًا وسلامًا على إبراهيم، وقلب العصا حية، وتسخير الريح والجن والشياطين وتسبيح الجبال، وإلانة الحديد، وإحياء الموتى، وحنين الأسطوانة وشكاية الناقة، وكلام الجمل المسموم، ونبع الماء من بين الأصابع وغير ذلك مما هي أدلة صدق ادعاء هم الرسالة على ما بينا من كيفية وجه الدلالة.
Then the proof for the establishment of prophethood for some messengers specifically is the appearance of miracles that break customary occurrences at the hands of many of them, such as the emergence of the she-camel from the rock, the fire becoming cool and safe for Abraham, the turning of the staff into a serpent, the subjugation of the wind, jinn, and devils, the glorification of the mountains, the softening of iron, the resurrection of the dead, the yearning of the pillar and the complaint of the she-camel, the speech of the poisoned camel, the gushing of water from between the fingers, and other things that are proofs of the truth of their claim to prophethood, according to what we have explained concerning the manner of the implication.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage defines the proof of prophethood: the manifestation of miracles that break natural habits (nawāqid al-ʻādāt) at the hands of the prophets. The author lists various miracles from different prophets — from Prophet Salih's camel coming out of rock, to Prophet Ibrahim's fire, to Prophet Musa's staff, to Prophet Sulayman's control over wind and jinn, to Prophet Dawud's softening of iron, to Prophet Isa's raising of the dead, and to Prophet Muhammad's miracles like the yearning pillar, the camel complaint, the poisoned camel speaking, and water flowing from his fingers. These are all evidence of their truthful claim to prophethood, as explained previously.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are merely extraordinary events and can be performed by anyone.
Correction: Miracles (mu'jizat) are specifically defined as events that break natural habits and are performed by prophets as proofs of their truthfulness. They are not just wonders but are tied to the claim of prophethood.

Checkpoint

B) The appearance of miracles that break customary norms
C) Their ability to predict the future
D) The number of followers they have

Key Takeaway
Miracles that break natural laws are the definitive proof of prophethood, and they have been granted to many prophets as signs of their truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Take a moment: what is the one piece of evidence that makes you certain that Muhammad (ﷺ) is a true prophet? If you cannot name it, are you truly convinced?
?
You have just read that miracles break 'customary occurrences'—they are unmistakable signs from Allah. But in your daily life, do you look for His signs in the ordinary, or do you only recognize Him when He breaks the pattern? What small miracle today are you ignoring because it seems 'customary'?

The Dilemma of Miracles: Refuting a Doubt
Presents a doubt and partial refutation concerning miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand a classical doubt against miracles and how Maturidi scholars begin to refute it by appealing to widespread testimony.

Core Idea
Miracles are proven by widespread witness, not by fitting natural categories.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents a doubt that attempts to undermine the evidential value of miracles. The doubter argues that miracles cannot serve as proof because they either follow nature (and thus are not special) or violate nature (which is deemed impossible). The author begins his refutation by dismissing this as weak and pointing to the fact that miracles are witnessed by multitudes. However, the full refutation is cut off in this excerpt.

Guided Path
1
Read the doubt carefully
Understand the dilemma presented: either the miracle conforms to nature (no evidence) or violates nature (impossible). Note the two horns.
This is a classic 'damned if you do, damned if you don't' argument.
2
Identify the author's response
See how the author dismisses the doubt as flimsy and introduces the idea of widespread witnessing as the basis for accepting miracles.
The response is only partially given; the full argument continues.
3
Consider the incompleteness
Recognize that the refutation is only partial; the full argument would likely elaborate on the reliability of testimony.
4
Reflect on the significance
Why does appealing to testimony matter in establishing prophetic miracles? How does this connect to the broader kalam approach of using tawatur?
This connects to the concept of 'mutawatir' reports.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما شبهة من زعم أن لا ثبوت للرسالة إلا بالدليل ولا ثبوت للدليل، فإنه لو كان خارجًا على ما عليه العادة ومجرى الطبيعة فلا دليل فيه، وإن خرج عن العادة ومجرى الطبيعة فهو محال إذ لا تغير للطبائع. فكلام واه لو تفوه به مجنون لتعجب منه، وذلك لما مر أن كل ذلك معاينه من لا يجوز خفاء أمره عليهم لكثرتهم، فكان ما أنكروه من الخروج عن الطبيعة بلا
As for the doubt of one who claims that there is no establishment of prophethood except by evidence, and there is no establishment of the evidence — for if it (the miracle) occurs in accordance with custom and the course of nature, then there is no evidence in it; and if it departs from custom and the course of nature, then it is impossible because natures do not change. This is flimsy speech; if a madman uttered it, he would be wondered at. And that is because, as we have mentioned, all of that is witnessed by those whose matter cannot be hidden from them due to their multitude. So what they denied of departure from nature is...
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage presents a doubt (shubha) against miracles as proof. The doubter argues a dilemma: if a miracle follows natural laws, it is not a proof; if it violates nature, it is impossible because natures are immutable. The author refutes this by calling it 'flimsy speech' and stating that miracles are witnessed by many people, so their occurrence is established regardless of natural laws. The refutation is incomplete in this excerpt, but the author indicates that the widespread witnessing eliminates the possibility of denial. The key point is that the objection is invalid because the fact of the miracle is established through multiple witnesses, not by fitting into natural categories.

Key Terms

عادة
طبيعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles cannot be evidence because they either fit nature or are impossible.
Correction: Miracles are established through widespread testimony (tawatur), not by fitting into natural categories. The multitude of witnesses makes denial impossible.

Checkpoint
What is the core claim of the doubt that the author refutes?
A) That miracles are impossible because natures are immutable
B) That miracles cannot serve as evidence because they either fit nature or are impossible
C) That miracles are only possible if they break nature
D) That miracles are not witnessed

Key Takeaway
The doubt against miracles is refuted by the fact that miracles are witnessed by multitudes, establishing their occurrence beyond doubt.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Distinguishing Miracles from Sorcery
Nasafi refutes that sorcerers can produce miracles, listing distinctions and divine protection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key distinctions between miracles and sorcery as argued by Imam Nasafi, and why sorcerers cannot produce genuine miracles.

Core Idea
Miracles endure under scrutiny; sorcery dissolves. God protects His proofs from imitation.

Imam Nasafi addresses a critical objection: if changing natural laws is possible, why couldn't sorcerers also perform miracles? He dismantles this claim by showing that miracles and sorcery are fundamentally different in their nature, effects, and divine backing. This passage not only refutes the sorcerers' pretense but also reinforces the distinct role of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the confident tone of refutation. Then read the commentary to understand the flow of arguments.
The passage ends abruptly; we only have the beginning of the lodestone example.
2
Identify the differences listed
Nasafi gives several distinctions: effect under scrutiny, moral/spiritual context, practitioners' states, and divine intervention. List each one as you find it.
These are the core of the argument.
3
Analyze the logical structure
The passage moves from refuting a claim, to listing differences, to explaining why God prevents sorcerers from producing miracles. See the guided breakdown to follow the structure.
4
Reflect on the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding: if miracles are possible, why can't sorcerers do them? Nasafi's answer shows that miracles are divinely guarded and contextually distinct.
This is the key takeaway.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما من يزعم أن قلب العادة والطبيعة جائز، غير أن ذلك أيضا في مقدور السحرة والمشعبذة. فكلام فاسد، إذ المشعبذة والمخرفة يزداد ضعفًا واضمحلالاً لدى البحث عنهما والتأمل فيهما، إذ المخرفة تمويه محض، والشعبذة مبنية على سفل أعين الناظرين بشيء ثم إخراج غيره وعلى المهارة في خفة اليد. والمعجزة تزداد عند البحث والتأمل وكادة () وعلى مر الأيام ثباتاً ودواما. والسحر من علائق الكلمات المؤلفة من الشرك الخالص والكفر المحض والتعمد لتفخيم الشياطين. ثم في الأعم الأغلب يظهر على أيدي الحيض من النساء وذوي القذارة والنجاسة من الرجال، في أوقات ومواضع لا يجري فيها ذكر الله تعالى، وإذا وافقه شيء من ذكر الله تعالى ينمحق ويضمحل. ولهذا يكون نفوذه في بلاد الشرك وعبادة الأصنام أشد وأبلغ، وهذا لأن ذلك يظهر بمعونة الشياطين والأرواح الخبيثة فلابد من تقرب ممن يطلب منهم العناية إليهم بما ذكرنا من التباعد عن ذكر الله تعالى وطاعته ومباشرة الأعمال الخبيثة وملامسة الأشياء المستقذرة، وحال الأنبياء عليهم السلام كانت في نهاية المخالفة من هذه الأحوال، إذ هم المواظبون على ذكر الله تعالى المداومون على جميع أنواع القرب، والموصوفون بالتطهر عن النجاسات والأقذار. فتمتاز المعجز عن السحر بأحوال الآتي بهما المكتسب لهما، على أنا بينا أن الله تعالى هو الذي يظهر المعجزة عقيب الدعوى على يد مدعي النبوة تأكيدًا لدعوته وتصديقًا له في دعواه الرسالة، فلو ادعى أحد من المشعبذة والسحرة النبوة، وأراد إيجاد ما هو ناقض العادة ليكون دلالة له على صدق مقالته لأعجزه الله تعالى عن إظهار ناقض للعادة وأبطل سحره وكيده في هذه الحالة، صيانة لحججه عن أن يعارضها باطل أو يقاومها فاسد، وهذا لما مر أن لابد في حق الحكمة من إثبات تفرقة الحق والباطل، ودفع ما يوجب التسوية بينهما، وإثبات القدرة للصانع على ذلك، وامتناع تعجيزه ذلك على نحو ما قررنا، والله ولي التوفيق. ولهذا قال مشايخنا إن من ظفر بحجر المغناطيس ثم أتى ناحية من آفاق الأرض، لم يعلم أهلها بما هو من خاصية المغناطيس من جذب الفولاذ ثم ادعى الرسالة، وجعل حجة دعواه وآية صدقه القدرة على جذب الحديد، أبطل الله
As for the one who claims that the changing of custom and nature is possible, but that also is within the power of sorcerers and jugglers, it is corrupt speech. For jugglers and deceivers increase in weakness and dissolution upon investigation and reflection about them. For deception is pure illusion, and juggling is based on diverting the eyes of the beholders with something then bringing out something else, and on skill in lightness of hand. But the miracle increases upon investigation and reflection in strength and over the passage of days in constancy and permanence. And sorcery is from the attachments of words composed of pure polytheism and sheer disbelief and intent to glorify devils. Then in the majority of cases it appears at the hands of menstruating women and those of filth and impurity from men, in times and places where the remembrance of God does not occur, and if any remembrance of God coincides with it, it vanishes and dissolves. For this reason, its influence in lands of polytheism and idol worship is more intense and stronger. This is because it appears with the help of devils and evil spirits, so it is necessary to draw near to those from whom one seeks their assistance by what we mentioned of distancing from the remembrance of God and His obedience, and engaging in evil deeds and touching impure things. And the state of the prophets, peace be upon them, was in extreme opposition to these states, for they are the ones who persist in the remembrance of God, who are constant in all types of acts of obedience, and are described as purified from impurities and filth. Thus the miracle is distinguished from sorcery by the states of the one who brings them and acquires them. Moreover, we have shown that God Almighty is the one who causes the miracle to appear after the claim at the hand of the claimant of prophethood, as a confirmation of his call and a verification of his claim of messengership. So if a juggler or sorcerer claimed prophethood and wished to produce something that breaks custom to be a proof for the truth of his statement, God would incapacitate him from showing a custom-breaker and would nullify his sorcery and cunning in that situation, as protection for His proofs from being opposed by falsehood or resisted by corruption. This is because, as has passed, it is necessary in respect of wisdom to establish a distinction between truth and falsehood, and to repel what necessitates equality between them, and to establish the power of the Creator over that, and the impossibility of His being incapacitated from that, as we have established. And God is the Granter of success. For this reason, our mashā'ikh said: If someone obtains a lodestone and goes to a region of the earth whose inhabitants do not know about the property of the magnet of attracting iron, and then claims prophethood, and makes the proof of his claim and the sign of his truthfulness the power to attract iron, God would nullify
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection: if changing natures is possible, why cannot sorcerers also produce miracles? Nasafi first declares this claim corrupt. He then lists several differences: (1) Juggling and deception grow weak under scrutiny, while miracles grow stronger and enduring. (2) Sorcery involves polytheism, disbelief, and glorification of devils, and it usually appears in impure states and times devoid of God's remembrance. (3) Prophets are the opposite: they are constant in worship, pure, and far from such states. (4) Ultimately, God Himself produces the miracle at the hand of a true prophet after his claim. If a sorcerer claimed prophethood, God would prevent him from producing a genuine miracle, thus protecting His proofs from being confused with falsehood. Nasafi then gives an example from the mashā'ikh: if someone obtained a lodestone and used its property of attracting iron as a claimed miracle in a place ignorant of that property, God would nullify that claim. The passage ends abruptly, but the point is that God protects the distinction between truth and falsehood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that sorcerers can perform similar feats to prophets, making prophethood indistinguishable.
Correction: Nasafi shows that miracles and sorcery differ in their nature, conditions, and divine backing. God actively prevents sorcerers from producing genuine miracles.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what happens to a miracle upon investigation compared to sorcery?
A) Both weaken.
B) The miracle weakens, sorcery strengthens.
C) The miracle strengthens and endures, sorcery weakens.
D) Both remain unchanged.

Key Takeaway
Miracles are divinely guarded and distinct from sorcery; God ensures that no impostor can replicate the sign of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been impressed by an outwardly spiritual act or 'miracle' and immediately trusted the person, without examining their character and consistency in obedience to God? How can you apply the lesson's test of 'investigation and reflection' to avoid being deceived?
?
The source shows that sorcery thrives in environments far from God's remembrance. Where in your daily life have you allowed distance from God—through neglect of prayer, impure environments, or tolerance of sin—that may be opening space for spiritual deception? What specific step will you take today to close that gap?
?
The prophets were described as constant in remembrance and purified from filth. If your life were measured by these same standards—your constancy in dhikr and purity—would the state of the one performing signs (you) align more with a prophet or a sorcerer? What change must happen this week to shift that balance?
