The Distinction Between Miracles and Sorcery
Distinguishes miracle from sorcery via the condition of the doer and Allah's protection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key distinctions between miracles and sorcery based on the state of the doer and divine protection.

Core Idea
Miracles are distinguished by the purity of the prophet and Allah's protection, unlike sorcery.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi clarifies why miracles cannot be mistaken for sorcery. It explains that sorcery thrives on impurity and association with devils, while prophets are characterized by constant remembrance of Allah and purity. Moreover, Allah actively prevents sorcerers from producing genuine miracles if they claim prophethood, preserving the integrity of divine proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own argument come through.
Notice that the passage has two main sections: the nature of sorcery and the nature of prophethood.
2
Contrast sorcery and prophecy
Identify how the author contrasts the conditions of sorcerers (impurity, reliance on devils) with those of prophets (remembrance of Allah, purity). This is the first distinction.
The key phrase is 'falamtāz al-muʿjiz ʿan al-siḥr bi-aḥwāl al-ātī bihimā'.
3
Understand divine safeguarding
The author then explains that Allah Himself prevents sorcerers from producing a miracle when they claim prophethood. This is the second and more fundamental distinction.
Look for 'fa-law iddaʿā aḥad...' to see the hypothetical example.
4
Reflect on the wisdom behind it
Consider why Allah would do this: to maintain the distinction between truth and falsehood. The author ties it back to divine wisdom.
This connects to the broader purpose of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شيء من ذكر الله تعالى ينمحق ويضمحل. ولهذا يكون نفوذه في بلاد الشرك وعبادة الأصنام أشد وأبلغ، وهذا لأن ذلك يظهر بمعونة الشياطين والأرواح الخبيثة فلابد من تقرب ممن يطلب منهم العناية إليهم بما ذكرنا من التباعد عن ذكر الله تعالى وطاعته ومباشرة الأعمال الخبيثة وملامسة الأشياء المستقذرة، وحال الأنبياء عليهم السلام كانت في نهاية المخالفة من هذه الأحوال، إذ هم المواظبون على ذكر الله تعالى المداومون على جميع أنواع القرب، والموصوفون بالتطهر عن النجاسات والأقذار. فتمتاز المعجز عن السحر بأحوال الآتي بهما المكتسب لهما، على أنا بينا أن الله تعالى هو الذي يظهر المعجزة عقيب الدعوى على يد مدعي النبوة تأكيدًا لدعوته وتصديقًا له في دعواه الرسالة، فلو ادعى أحد من المشعبذة والسحرة النبوة، وأراد إيجاد ما هو ناقض العادة ليكون دلالة له على صدق مقالته لأعجزه الله تعالى عن إظهار ناقض للعادة وأبطل سحره وكيده في هذه الحالة، صيانة لحججه عن أن يعارضها باطل أو يقاومها فاسد، وهذا لما مر أن لابد في حق الحكمة من إثبات تفرقة الحق والباطل، ودفع ما يوجب التسوية بينهما، وإثبات القدرة للصانع على ذلك، وامتناع تعجيزه ذلك على نحو ما قررنا، والله ولي التوفيق.
Something of the remembrance of Allah Most High vanishes and decays. Hence, its influence in the lands of polytheism and idol worship is stronger and more pervasive. This is because that appears with the aid of devils and evil spirits. So one must draw close to those from whom they seek assistance by what we mentioned of distancing from the remembrance of Allah Most High and His obedience, and engaging in evil deeds and touching impure things. The state of the prophets, peace be upon them, was utterly contrary to these conditions, for they are those who constantly remember Allah Most High, persistently perform all types of acts of drawing near [to Him], and are described as purified from impurities and filth. So the miracle is distinguished from sorcery by the states of the one who brings them and acquires them, given that we have explained that Allah Most High is the one who brings forth the miracle following the claim at the hand of the claimant of prophethood as an affirmation of his call and a confirmation of his claim of messengership. So if any of the jugglers and sorcerers were to claim prophethood and intend to produce something breaking custom to be a proof for the truth of his statement, Allah Most High would disable him from manifesting a breaker of custom, and would nullify his sorcery and trickery in that situation, safeguarding His proofs from being opposed by falsehood or resisted by corruption. This is because it is necessary in consideration of wisdom to establish the distinction between truth and falsehood, to repel that which necessitates equivalence between them, to establish the power of the Maker over that, and to prevent His being disabled in that, as we have established. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage defines the distinction between miracles (mu'jizat) and sorcery (sihr). It begins by noting that sorcery thrives in environments distant from the remembrance of Allah, as it relies on the assistance of devils. In contrast, prophets are constantly engaged in divine remembrance and purity. The key point is that miracles are distinguished by the state of the person: a prophet is inherently contrary to sorcerers. Moreover, Allah Himself produces the miracle after the prophetic claim, and if a sorcerer claims prophethood and attempts a miracle, Allah disables him from breaking custom, thus protecting divine proofs from being challenged. This is necessary for wisdom to maintain the distinction between truth and falsehood.

Key Terms
المعجز
السحر
ذكر الله
الشياطين
ناقض العادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles and sorcery are similar in kind and cannot be distinguished except by external factors.
Correction: This passage shows they differ fundamentally by the state of the doer (purity vs impurity) and by Allah's direct intervention to prevent sorcerers from mimicking miracles when they claim prophethood.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why would Allah disable a sorcerer who claims prophethood?
A) Because sorcerers are inherently evil.
B) To safeguard His proofs from being opposed by falsehood.
C) Because sorcerers lack proper training.
D) To test the faith of the community.

Key Takeaway
Miracles are distinct from sorcery because prophets are pure and Allah actively prevents sorcerers from producing miracles, preserving the truth of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you seek to influence others or succeed in life, are your methods closer to those of the prophets (through remembrance and purity) or to those of sorcerers (through manipulation and impurity)? What does your current approach say about the state of your heart?
?
If Allah were to test you by enabling you to perform a supernatural act, would your life and character align more with the prophets or with sorcerers? What specific habits of devotion or impurity do you need to change to be worthy of divine support?
?
The passage says Allah disables sorcerers who claim prophethood. Has there been an area in your life where you claimed authority or power without the purity to back it? Will you repent and realign with the way of the prophets today?

The Magnetic Stone Example of Divine Protection
Example of divine protection by nullifying a natural property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Allah can disable natural properties to protect His proofs from being challenged.

Core Idea
Allah can nullify natural properties to safeguard His true religion.

Our masters (mashayikh) gave a vivid example of divine protection: if someone uses a magnetic stone's iron-attracting property as a proof of prophethood where that property is unknown, Allah would simply nullify that property. This illustrates that natural laws are subject to Allah's will and that He protects His proofs from imitation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the example come through clearly.
Pay attention to the sequence: obtaining the stone, going to a region, claiming prophethood, and the divine response.
2
Understand the scenario
The scenario involves a person who acquires a magnetic stone and travels to a place where its property is unknown. He then claims prophethood and uses the stone's attraction as a proof.
This sets up a challenge to true prophethood.
3
Identify the divine response
Allah nullifies the magnetic property from the stone. This is the key action that safeguards His proofs.
This shows that Allah can override natural causes at will.
4
Reflect on the principle
The example illustrates that Allah protects the distinctiveness of miracles by disabling any natural explanation that could be used to imitate them.
This reinforces the uniqueness of prophetic miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا قال مشايخنا إن من ظفر بحجر المغناطيس ثم أتى ناحية من آفاق الأرض، لم يعلم أهلها بما هو من خاصية المغناطيس من جذب الفولاذ ثم ادعى الرسالة، وجعل حجة دعواه وآية صدقه القدرة على جذب الحديد، أبطل الله تلك الخاصية عن المغناطيس، صيانة لحججه عن المعارضة، وحفظًا لدينه الحق عن أن يقاومه باطل، وبالله التوفيق.

And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage presents a concrete example to illustrate the principle established earlier. The 'masters' (mashayikh) state that if someone acquires a magnetic stone, goes to a place where its property is unknown, and uses its iron-attracting ability as a proof of prophethood, Allah would simply nullify that property from the stone. This divine intervention protects divine proofs from being matched and preserves the true religion from being challenged by false claims.

Certain Miracles Beyond Human Power
Lists sensory miracles beyond human capacity, arguing against opposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why certain sensory miracles cannot be opposed because they are beyond any human capacity.

Core Idea
Some miracles are intrinsically beyond any human ability, making imitation impossible.

This passage from Imam Nasafi lists specific prophetic miracles and argues that a sane person cannot even conceive of them being performed by anyone other than Allah. This removes any possibility of opposition or imitation, strengthening the case for prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once, then the literal translation. Notice the force of the language: 'no doubt for anyone not given to obstinacy.'
The passage is concise but definitive.
2
Identify the listed miracles
The passage mentions five specific miracles: staff turning into a snake, splitting the sea, reviving the dead, splitting the moon, and water from fingers. Recognize that each is drawn from prophetic traditions.
These are well-known miracles in Islamic tradition.
3
Understand the rational argument
The passage asserts that these acts are not within the capability of anyone other than Allah. Moreover, a sane person would never even imagine such acts from another. This is the key logical move.
It appeals to common sense and rational intuition.
4
Reflect on the implication for prophethood
If such miracles cannot be imitated, then when a prophet performs them, it is a clear sign from Allah. Opposition is futile because no one can produce a similar act.
This strengthens the proof of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And the possibility of that from other than Allah Most High would never occur to the mind of a sane person at all. So opposition is not possible in it.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage makes an additional argument for the impossibility of opposing certain miracles. It lists specific miracles from prophetic traditions (staff turning into a snake, splitting the sea, reviving the dead, splitting the moon, and water from fingers) and asserts that no one other than Allah can perform them. Therefore, a sane person cannot even imagine such acts from anyone else, and thus there is no possibility of opposition or imitation.

Correction: This passage shows that some sensory miracles are intrinsically beyond any human capacity, and a sane person cannot even conceive of them being performed by another. Thus, opposition is impossible.

Certain sensory miracles are so far beyond human power that no sane person can imagine them from anyone but Allah, making opposition impossible.

?

?

Refuting the Acquirability of Miracles
Refutes the objection that breaking custom can be achieved through effort and practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi scholars refute the objection that prophetic miracles could be the result of acquired skill rather than divine intervention.

Core Idea
A true miracle is marked by the absence of prior training in the miracle-worker.

This passage presents the response to a skeptical objection: that what appears to be a miracle could actually be the product of strenuous effort and practice. The author, Imam al-Nasafi, argues that such a possibility is ruled out by the public knowledge of the prophet's life before his claim. The community that knew him best can testify that he never engaged in any such training, making his act a clear breach of normal patterns.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the first part of the passage where the objector claims that breaking custom could be acquired through exertion and that not everyone has been tested.
Notice the objector's attempt to undermine miracle uniqueness.
2
Understand the author's concession
See how the author says 'Even if we agreed with you' – this is a rhetorical strategy to strengthen the refutation.
Concession does not mean acceptance; it prepares the ground for a stronger argument.
3
Grasp the decisive refutation
The author points to the public testimony of the prophet's community, who observed him from birth and can confirm his lack of training in such acts.
Community knowledge makes the act a clear breaking of custom, thus a miracle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبهذا كله يبطل قول من يقول: إن قلب العادة الذي أتى به مدعي الرسالة مما يمكن تحصيله لمن له في نوعه تكلف واجتهاد والمدعون ما امتحنوا قوى الجميع. على أنا نقول لهم: لو ساعدناكم لكان وجوده مما لم يكن له بذلك اجتهاد وتدرب واعتياد نقضا للمادة، فيكون دليلاً لصحة دعواهم، والمدعون للرسالة له لم يكن لهم بذلك اجتهاد ولا اعتياد عرف ذلك منهم قومهم الذين نشأوا هم بين أظهرهم، إذ عاينوا أحوالهم وشاهدوا منذ ولدوا إلى أن كبروا وادعوا ما ادعوا من الرسالة، فلم يروهم اشتغلوا بشيء من ذلك، ولا اعتادوا تعاطيه، ولا صحبوا من له بذلك علم واعتياد، وخروج ذلك على أيدي مثلهم ناقض للعادة، فكان معجزة كافية والله الموفق.
And by all this is invalidated the statement of the one who says: Indeed, the breaking of custom which the claimant of messengership brought is among the things that can be acquired by anyone who has exertion and striving in its type, and the claimants have not tested the powers of everyone. However, we say to them: Even if we agreed with you, its existence as something for which he had no exertion, training, and habituation would be a breach of the matter, so it would be a proof for the truth of their claim. And the claimants of messengership had no exertion or habituation in that; their people among whom they grew up knew that, for they witnessed their states and observed them from the time they were born until they grew up and claimed what they claimed of messengership, and they did not see them engaged in any of that, nor did they accustom themselves to practicing it, nor did they accompany anyone who had knowledge and habituation of it. The occurrence of that at the hands of such people is a breaking of custom, thus it was a sufficient miracle. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector claims that breaking custom (kharq al-ada) performed by a prophetic claimant could theoretically be acquired by anyone who exerts effort in that field, and since not everyone has been tested, the claimant's act might not be unique. The author refutes this by even granting the premise. He argues that even if it were acquirable, the fact that the claimant had no prior training, habituation, or association with practitioners makes his act a breach of normal patterns, thus a miracle. Moreover, the claimant's people, who knew him from birth, can testify that he never engaged in such things. Therefore, his act remains a valid miracle.

Key Terms
قلب العادة
تكلف واجتهاد
تدرب واعتياد
نقضا للمادة
خروج على عادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles might be secretly acquired skills.
Correction: The public knowledge of the prophet's upbringing and lack of training rules out such acquisition, as his entire community can testify.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the author's response to the objection?
A) The claimant's act is beyond any human capability.
B) The claimant's lack of prior training makes his act a breaking of custom.
C) The objector has no proof.
D) Miracles can only be done by prophets.

Key Takeaway
The absence of prior training and the community's testimony conclusively establish that a prophetic miracle is a genuine breach of custom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever brushed aside a clear sign from Allah because you could imagine a natural explanation, just as the objector imagines miracles could be acquired by effort? What would it take for you to recognize a true miracle?
?
If your own life were scrutinized from birth by those around you, would they see consistency between your claims of faith and your actions? The prophet's community knew his entire history. Does your community see evidence of prophethood's truth in your character?
?
The objector's argument is really a way to avoid submission. Are you harboring any similar intellectual excuses to keep distance from the full demands of Islam? What would change if you truly accepted that the Prophet's miracles were undeniable?

Refuting the Objection of Zoroaster's Wonders
Refutes the objection that Zoroaster's acts were like miracles but he was not a prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the example of Zoroaster does not undermine the argument that genuine miracles are signs of prophethood.

Core Idea
Extraordinary acts alone don't prove prophethood; only divine miracles do.

This passage addresses a common objection: if Zoroaster performed wonders without being a prophet, why should we accept miracles as proof? The author provides a sharp rebuttal by distinguishing between true signs and counterfeit wonders. Let's see how the argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The objector points to Zoroaster's actions that break custom, arguing they were not proof of his claim. Recognize that this is a challenge to the reliability of miracles.
This objection assumes that all extraordinary events are equal.
2
Examine the author's rebuttal
The author responds by stating that Zoroaster's acts were not a sign of truth. Therefore, the objector's example actually supports the original position.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The key is that not every wonder is a miracle; a true miracle must be a sign from Allah confirming a prophet. Counterfeit wonders prove nothing.
This distinction is crucial in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قابلوا ذلك بما ظهر من الناقض للعادة على يدي زرادشت ولم يكن ذلك علمًا لصحة دعواه فكذا ما أنتم تدعونه.
And if they counter that with what appeared of breaking custom at the hands of Zoroaster, and that was not a sign of the truth of his claim, then likewise what you claim [is false/not a sign].
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage presents a second objection-and-answer. The objector brings up Zoroaster, who allegedly performed acts of breaking custom but was not a prophet, to argue that such acts are not reliable proofs. The author's rebuttal is concise: since Zoroaster's acts were not true signs of prophethood, the same applies to the objector's examples—they are not valid. In other words, the objector's own example actually disproves their argument because Zoroaster's acts were not genuine miracles from Allah but mere sorcery or deception.

Key Terms

ناقض العادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any extraordinary event can be considered a miracle and proof of prophethood.
Correction: Genuine miracles are divine signs given to prophets as validation; false claimants may also produce wonders, but they lack the divine endorsement and challenge (tahaddi). Zoroaster's acts were not true miracles.

Checkpoint

A) Zoroaster was actually a prophet.
B) Zoroaster's acts were not true signs of truth.
C) The objection is irrelevant.
D) Miracles are not needed for prophethood.

Key Takeaway
The example of Zoroaster does not refute the role of miracles because his wonders were not genuine divine signs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If someone today performed wonders but lacked divine endorsement, how would you test whether it is a true sign or mere deception? Translate the criterion of this lesson into a concrete principle for your own discernment.

The Irrefutable Nature of Prophetic Miracles
Nasafi argues prophetic miracles are exclusively divine and thus undeniable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets' miracles cannot be opposed because they are exclusively acts of Allah beyond human capability.

Core Idea
Prophets' miracles are divine acts, not human feats—making them irrefutable.

Imam Nasafi presents a crisp argument for the uniqueness of prophetic miracles. He lists familiar examples to show they are not within human power. This passage establishes a foundational principle in proving prophethood: miracles are the strongest proof because they cannot be matched.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Let the author's rhythm come through before interpreting.
Notice that Nasafi uses a very direct and definitive tone.
2
Identify the overall claim
Nasafi states that for a rational person free from obstinacy, there is no doubt about the miracles mentioned.
3
Examine the list of miracles
Find the five specific miracles given (staff, sea, dead, moon, water). Note that they are all sensory and extraordinary.
These are well-known miracles from various prophets.
4
Understand the reason for irrefutability
Nasafi argues that these miracles are not within anyone's power except Allah, and a rational mind never even considers them possible from anyone else.
Thus, no one can produce a similar miracle to oppose the prophet.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Since opposition is impossible, these miracles serve as conclusive proof of prophethood.
This strengthens the case for accepting the prophet's message.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أنه لا ريب لأحد (١) لم يكن من شأنه العناد والمكابرة أن قلب العصا حية، وفلق البحر، وإحياء الموتى، وشق القمر، ونبع الماء من بين الأصابع، وغير ذلك من هذه المعجزات الحسية، ليست من أنواع ما يدخل تحت مقدور أحد غير الله تعالى، وقد لا يخطر جواز ذلك من غير الله تعالى على قلب عاقل البتة، فلا يتمكن إذا فيه المعارضة.
Indeed, there is no doubt for anyone who is not habitually obstinate and contentious that the turning of the staff into a snake, the splitting of the sea, the reviving of the dead, the splitting of the moon, the gushing of water from between the fingers, and other such sensory miracles, are not among the types of things that enter under anyone's power other than Allah the Exalted, and indeed the permissibility of that from other than Allah the Exalted never crosses the mind of a rational person at all, so opposition to them is not possible.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a concise argument establishing the irrefutable nature of the prophets' miracles. Imam Nasafi begins by stating that there is no doubt for anyone not given to obstinacy and contention (العناد والمكابرة) that specific miracles—such as the staff turning into a snake, the parting of the sea, reviving the dead, splitting the moon, and water flowing from between the fingers—are not among the types of actions that lie within anyone's power except Allah. He then emphasizes that the very thought of such things being possible from other than Allah never occurs to a rational person. Consequently, these miracles cannot be opposed or challenged by any counter-miracle or human effort. The structure is: a statement of certainty, a list of undeniable examples, a claim of exclusivity to divine power, and a conclusion of impossibility of opposition.

Key Terms
المعجزات الحسية
مقدور
المعارضة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People may think prophets' miracles are just extraordinary human feats or magic.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that these miracles are exclusively divine acts, beyond any human or jinn capability, making them true signs from Allah.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Nasafi, why is opposition to prophets' miracles impossible?
A) Because the prophets were powerful.
B) Because these miracles are beyond human power and only from Allah.
C) Because the miracles were witnessed by many.
D) Because the prophets were not challenged.

Key Takeaway
Prophetic miracles are not extraordinary human acts but exclusive divine acts, making them impossible to challenge and thus definitive proof of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Reflect on your own life: When you hear about these miracles, is your first reaction awe and submission, or do you find yourself mentally rationalizing them away? What does your response reveal about your heart's posture toward Allah's power?
?
If you truly believed that every miracle of the prophets is a direct act of Allah with no human involvement, how would that change the way you rely on Him in your daily struggles—especially when you feel powerless?
?
The lesson states that only the obstinate and contentious deny these signs. Is there any area of your faith where you are being stubborn—holding onto doubt because it feels comfortable? Will you sincerely ask Allah to remove that obstinacy today?

Nasafi's Refutation: Miracles Beyond Effort
Nasafi refutes the objection that breaking custom can be achieved by effort.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes the objection that miracles can be achieved by human effort and why the absence of prior training in prophets proves their miracles are genuine.

Core Idea
Prophets' miracles are unique because they happened without prior practice or training.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi addresses a common objection against the miraculous nature of prophethood. Some argue that if breaking custom can be achieved through effort, then miracles are not special. Nasafi refutes this by accepting the premise for argument's sake and then pointing out that the prophets themselves never engaged in such training, as attested by their communities.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the first part of the passage where the objection is stated: that breaking custom can be attained by anyone with effort and diligence.
Notice the phrase 'لمن له في نوعه تكلف واجتهاد'.
2
Follow the conditional argument
Nasafi says 'لو ساعدناكم' – even if we agree with you, the absence of effort in the prophets makes their acts a breaking of custom.
This is a dialectical technique: granting the opponent's premise for the sake of argument.
3
Recognize the historical evidence
Nasafi points out that the prophets' own people knew them from birth and never saw them train or practice for these acts.
This empirical observation seals the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبهة والرد عليها ] وبهذا كله يبطل قول من يقول: إن قلب العادة الذي أتى به مدعي الرسالة مما يمكن تحصيله لمن له في نوعه تكلف واجتهاد والمدعون ما امتحنوا قوى الجميع. على أنا نقول لهم: لو ساعدناكم لكان وجوده مما لم يكن له بذلك اجتهاد وتدرب واعتياد نقضا للمادة، فيكون دليلاً لصحة دعواهم، والمدعون للرسالة له لم يكن لهم بذلك اجتهاد ولا اعتياد عرف ذلك منهم قومهم الذين نشأوا هم بين أظهرهم، إذ عاينوا أحوالهم وشاهدوا منذ ولدوا إلى أن كبروا وادعوا ما ادعوا من الرسالة، فلم يروهم اشتغلوا بشيء من ذلك، ولا اعتادوا تعاطيه، ولا صحبوا من له بذلك علم واعتياد، وخروج ذلك على أيدي مثلهم ناقض للعادة، فكان معجزة كافية والله الموفق.
(Objection and refutation) And with all this, the statement of one who says is invalidated: 'Indeed, the breaking of custom that the claimant of prophethood brings is something that can be attained by one who has, in its kind, effort and diligence, and the claimants did not test the powers of all people.' Then we say to them: Even if we agreed with you, its occurrence without him having effort, training, and habituation in it would be a breaking of matter, so it would be a proof for the validity of their claim. And the claimants of prophethood had no effort or habituation in that, as their people who grew up among them knew, for they observed their conditions and witnessed them from birth until they grew up and claimed what they claimed of prophethood, and they did not see them occupied with any of that, nor did they practice it, nor did they accompany anyone who had knowledge and practice of it. And the appearance of that at the hands of people like them is a breaking of custom, so it is a sufficient miracle. And Allah is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is an objection and refutation. First, the objection is stated: someone might say that the breaking of custom (قلب العادة) performed by a claimant to prophethood could be achieved by anyone who makes an effort and practices in that field, and that the claimants did not test everyone's powers. Then Nasafi gives the refutation: Even if we concede that such things can be achieved by effort, the fact remains that the prophets performed these acts without prior effort, training, or habituation. Their people knew them from birth and never saw them engage in such practices. Therefore, the occurrence of these acts at their hands constitutes a genuine breaking of custom and thus a sufficient miracle. The argument proceeds by granting the opponent's premise for the sake of argument (لو ساعدناكم) and then showing that the key point is the absence of training, which is historically attested.

Key Terms
قلب العادة
تكلف واجتهاد
نقضا للعادة
معجزة كافية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If breaking custom can be achieved by effort, then miracles are not unique and cannot prove prophethood.
Correction: The uniqueness lies in the fact that prophets performed miracles without any prior effort or training, as witnessed by their communities.

Checkpoint
How does Nasafi refute the objection that prophets' miracles could be achieved by effort?
A) He says miracles are impossible anyway.
B) He says the prophets had training but hid it.
C) He says even if effort could achieve it, the prophets had no prior training or habituation.
D) He says only prophets can do magic.

Key Takeaway
Even if breaking custom were possible by effort, the prophets' lack of training proves their miracles are genuine divine signs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you accomplish something impressive, do you tend to attribute it to your own effort and skill? How does the lesson's point that the prophets performed acts without any prior training challenge your tendency to rely on yourself rather than acknowledging divine assistance? Will you today recognize one achievement where God's help was greater than your effort?
?
Think of a time when you dismissed a possible sign from God because you thought it could be explained by natural causes or human ability. After reading this passage, what would it take for you to accept that something is a genuine miracle? Are you willing to examine the background of the person or event more closely, as the community did with the prophets?
?
If you had been a contemporary of a prophet, would you have honestly testified that they never trained for their miracles? What might prevent you from admitting a miracle even when the evidence is clear? Examine your heart: is there pride or skepticism that blocks you from seeing God's signs in your life today? Ask Allah for sincerity.

The Zoroastrian Objection Answered: Tawatur and Miracles
Nasafi answers an objection by distinguishing reliable (prophetic) from unreliable (Zoroastrian) miracle reports.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi argues that reports of Zoroaster's miracles lack tawatur, while prophetic miracles are transmitted with certainty, and therefore the objection fails.

Core Idea
The certainty of a miracle depends on the reliability of its transmission.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi addresses a common objection: if we accept Zoroaster's miracles as breaking the custom, why do we not accept his prophethood? Nasafi's answer focuses on the mode of transmission. He argues that reports of Zoroaster's miracles are not mass-transmitted and thus do not produce certain knowledge, unlike the miracles of the prophets which are conveyed through unimpeachable chains. This lesson unpacks that critical distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage slowly, then read the literal translation. Notice how the objection is set up and then refuted.
2
Identify the two criteria Nasafi uses
Nasafi gives two reasons: (1) the reports of Zoroaster's miracles are not mutawatir, and (2) they were performed in private, allowing collusion. Underline these points.
Look for the words 'لم يثبت بالتواتر' and 'ليس عند ملأ'.
3
Contrast with prophetic miracles
Note how Nasafi describes prophetic miracles: transmitted in a way that precludes falsehood and collusion. Why does this make them certain?
The phrase 'لا احتمال فيه للكذب' indicates absolute certainty.
4
Reflect on necessary knowledge
Nasafi ends by saying such reports produce necessary knowledge. Consider how tawatur leads to certainty that is immediate and undeniable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قابلوا ذلك بما ظهر من الناقض للعادة على يدي زرادشت ولم يكن ذلك علمًا لصحة دعواه فكذا ما أنتم تدعونه. قلنا (۱): لم يثبت شيء من ذلك بالتواتر بل (۲) المذكور أنه أدخل قوائم فرسه في بطنه في دار الملك بين يدي الملك وخواصه وكذا وضع طشت فيه نار على صدره فلم يضره ولم يكن عند ملأ من الناس. ومثل هذا الخبر لا يجب العلم بمخبره، لجواز التواطؤ على الكذب عليهم، بل الغالب من حال الملوك وأتباعهم، توليد أخبار لا صحة لها لما في ذلك من تمكين رعيتهم وتسوية أمور مملكتهم. فأما ما نقل من أعلام الرسل عليهم السلام فقد نقل على طريق لا احتمال فيه للكذب، ولا يتصور التواطؤ على النقلة، وما هذا سبيله من الأخبار فهو موجب للعلم الضروري على ما قررنا والله الموفق.
And if they oppose that with what appeared of the breaking of custom at the hands of Zoroaster, and that was not knowledge for the validity of his claim, then so is what you claim. We say: None of that is established by mass transmission (tawatur). Rather, what is mentioned is that he inserted his horse's legs into its belly in the king's palace before the king and his retinue, and likewise he placed a basin containing fire on his chest and it did not harm him, and that was not in the presence of a multitude of people. And reports like this do not necessitate knowledge of their content, because collusion upon lying is possible. Rather, the usual state of kings and their followers is the generation of baseless reports for the sake of controlling their subjects and settling their kingdom's affairs. As for what is transmitted from the signs of the messengers (peace be upon them), it has been transmitted in a way that admits no possibility of falsehood, and collusion by the transmitters is inconceivable. And reports of this kind produce necessary knowledge (al-ʿilm al-ḍarūrī) as we have established. And Allah is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is an answer to an objection: opponents might cite Zoroaster's miracle as a breaking of custom that did not prove his claim, so why should prophets' miracles be proof? Nasafi responds with two points. First, the reports about Zoroaster are not mutawatir (mass-transmitted), so they do not constitute certain knowledge. Specifically, the reported acts were performed in private before the king and his close associates, not in front of a large public assembly. Such reports are susceptible to collusion and fabrication, especially since kings often propagate false stories to maintain control. Second, the miracles of the prophets are transmitted through a way that has no possibility of falsehood, and collusion among all transmitters is inconceivable. Thus, these reports produce necessary knowledge (العلم الضروري). The argument differentiates the reliability of transmission between the two cases.

Key Terms
تواتر
العلم الضروري
التواطؤ على الكذب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All miracle reports are equally valid and should be accepted as proof of prophethood.
Correction: Nasafi shows that the mode of transmission (tawatur) is crucial. Without mass transmission, certainty is not achieved.

Checkpoint
Why does Nasafi consider the reports of Zoroaster's miracles unreliable?
A) Because they are impossible.
B) Because they were not witnessed by a large public and are not mutawatir.
C) Because Zoroaster was a magician.
D) Because the prophets denied them.

Key Takeaway
Prophetic miracles are transmitted through mass-transmission (tawatur), which produces necessary certainty, unlike isolated miracle reports.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a religious story or miracle you accept as true. Have you ever investigated its chain of transmission? Does this passage make you question any story you believe based solely on the authority of a speaker? How can you verify it?
?
The passage warns that rulers fabricate miracles for political control. Have you ever uncritically accepted a 'miracle' story because it came from a respected leader? How will you guard against being deceived by authority?
?
Necessary knowledge comes from mass transmission that leaves no room for collusion. Consider your own faith: are there core beliefs you hold that rest on isolated reports or personal experiences rather than on tawatur? What is one step you can take today to ground your belief on a firmer transmission?

Miracles Only Confirm the Possible, Not the Impossible
Rule: miracles indicate possible, not impossible; applied to Zoroaster.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a miracle cannot validate a claim that is logically impossible, and how this principle was applied to Zoroaster's dualistic claim.

Core Idea
Miracles confirm possible claims; impossible claims remain impossible.

Some scholars of kalam argued that a miracle (breaking of custom) does not automatically prove any claim; rather, it only establishes the possibility of that claim. If a claim is inherently impossible, like Zoroaster's description of a weak and ignorant Creator, a miracle cannot support it. This lesson explores that crucial distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main argument
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the flow: the rule is stated, then applied to Zoroaster, then verified.
The last sentence is incomplete; the argument is cut off.
2
Understand the rule: miracles indicate the possible, not the impossible
The passage states that breaking custom (miracle) indicates the establishment of the possible (al-mumkin), not the impossible (al-mumtani'). This is a foundational principle.
This rule limits the scope of what a miracle can prove.
3
See how Zoroaster's claim is classified as impossible
Zoroaster's claim implies a weak, ignorant Creator who produces an adversary. Such a description is self-evidently impossible. List the attributes mentioned: weak, ignorant, subject to accidents, etc.
The impossibility is not just theological but logical.
4
Reflect on the implication: miracles cannot support false prophets
The passage concludes that a miracle cannot occur at the hand of a false prophet because it would lead to... (text cuts off). Think about why allowing miracles for impossible claims would undermine the purpose of miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذهب إلى هذا الجواب جميع متكلمي أهل الإسلام وأجاب بعض المحققين من علماء الأمة عن هذا فقال: إن الناقض للعادة يدل على ثبوت الممكن لا على ثبوت ما هو من الممتنع، ولهذا لا يكون دليلاً على صحة دعوى التأله، ودعوى زرادشت دعوى ممتنعة لما فيها من القول بصانع عاجز جاهل، تولد من فكرته الردية من يعاديه ويزاحمه في ملكه وينازعه في سلطانه وهو غير عالم بعاقبة فكره، عاجز عن قهر عدوه وغلبته، وهو مع هذا محل للحوادث، إذ حدثت فيه فكرته الرديئة، وكل ذلك دعوى ممتنعة ظاهر عوارها بإفسادها، ومثل هذا لا يصح بالدليل - ألا يرى أن دعوى المتأله لا تصح بمثل هذا لما فيها من الامتناع. يحققه أن قيام المعجزة على يدي المتنبئ إنما لا يجوز لئلا يؤدي إلى
All the mutakallimun of Ahl al-Islam agreed on this answer, and some verifiers from the scholars of the community answered this by saying: Indeed, the breaking of custom indicates the establishment of the possible, not the establishment of what is impossible. For this reason, it is not a proof for the validity of the claim of divinity. And the claim of Zoroaster is an impossible claim because it contains the statement of a weak, ignorant Creator, from whose evil thought generated one who opposes him, vies with him in his kingdom, and contends with him in his authority, while he (the Creator) is unaware of the consequence of his thought, incapable of subduing his enemy and overcoming him, and moreover he is subject to accidents, since his evil thought occurred in him. All of that is an impossible claim, whose defect is apparent in its corruptness. And such a claim is not validated by evidence. Do you not see that the claim of a self-deifier is not valid by such because of its impossibility? He verifies that the occurrence of a miracle at the hand of a false prophet is not permissible because it would lead to...
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage presents a second answer given by some accomplished scholars (بعض المحققين) beyond the standard mutakallimun response. The argument is that a miracle (breaking of custom) only confirms the possibility of a claim, not its impossibility. Zoroaster's claim is inherently impossible because it implies a deity who is weak and ignorant, who through his evil thought generates an adversary that opposes him, while he is unaware of the outcome and unable to defeat his enemy. Moreover, this deity is subject to temporal events (محل للحوادث). Such a claim is self-evidently impossible, and a miracle cannot support it. The passage concludes that a miracle cannot occur at the hand of a false prophet (متنبئ) because it would lead to... (the text cuts off). The structure is: statement of the rule, application to Zoroaster's claim, and a final verification.

Key Terms
الممكن (the possible)
الممتنع (the impossible)
دعوى ممتنعة (impossible claim)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any miracle proves that the claim made is true.
Correction: Miracles only support claims that are logically possible; they cannot make an impossible claim true.

Checkpoint
According to some scholars, why did Zoroaster's miracle not prove his claim?
A) Because it was not a real miracle.
B) Because his claim was logically impossible, and miracles only support possible claims.
C) Because the miracle was weak.
D) Because he was not a prophet.

Key Takeaway
A miracle cannot validate a logically impossible claim; it only confirms the possibility of a claim.

The Problem of Transmission: Why Zoroaster's Miracles Lack Certainty
The author argues that Zoroaster's miracles lack tawatur and thus do not produce necessary knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the lack of tawatur (mass transmission) in reports of Zoroaster's alleged miracles undermines their evidentiary value compared to the miracles of true prophets.

Core Idea
Without mass transmission, reports of miracles cannot yield certain knowledge.

In this passage, the author tackles the first line of refutation: the reports of Zoroaster's miracles are not transmitted by tawatur. He contrasts them with the transmission of the prophets' miracles, which are so widely and reliably transmitted that falsehood is impossible. This lesson examines the criterion of tawatur and why it is essential for establishing miraculous claims.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the author's contrast between the reports of Zoroaster's deeds and those of the prophets.
Pay attention to the terms 'tawatur' and 'al-ilm al-daruri'.
2
Identify the two types of reports
The author distinguishes between reports that lack tawatur (like Zoroaster's) and those that are mass-transmitted (like the prophets' miracles). Understand why the former cannot produce certainty.
The 'usual state of kings' is given as a reason for fabrication.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why the author places such importance on tawatur. How does this criterion protect the integrity of prophetic miracles?
This connects to the broader epistemology of kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قلنا (١): لم يثبت شيء من ذلك بالتواتر بل (۲) المذكور أنه أدخل قوائم فرسه في بطنه في دار الملك بين يدي الملك وخواصه وكذا وضع طشت فيه نار على صدره فلم يضره ولم يكن عند ملأ من الناس. ومثل هذا الخبر لا يجب العلم بمخبره، لجواز التواطؤ على الكذب عليهم، بل الغالب من حال الملوك وأتباعهم، توليد أخبار لا صحة لها لما في ذلك من تمكين رعيتهم وتسوية أمور مملكتهم. فأما ما نقل من أعلام الرسل عليهم السلام فقد نقل على طريق لا احتمال فيه للكذب، ولا يتصور التواطؤ على النقلة ، وما هذا سبيله من الأخبار فهو موجب للعلم الضروري على ما قررنا والله الموفق. ذهب إلى هذا الجواب(۳) جميع متكلمي أهل الإسلام وأجاب بعض المحققين من علماء الأمة عن هذا فقال: إن الناقض للعادة يدل على ثبوت الممكن لا على ثبوت (٤) ما هو من الممتنع ()، ولهذا لا يكون دليلاً على صحة دعوى التأله، ودعوى زرادشت دعوى ممتنعة لما فيها من القول بصانع عاجز جاهل، تولد من فكرته الردية من (٦) يعاديه ويزاحمه في ملكه وينازعه في سلطانه وهو غير عالم بعاقبة فكره، عاجز عن قهر عدوه وغلبته، وهو مع هذا محل للحوادث، إذ حدثت فيه فكرته الرديئة ، وكل ذلك دعوى ممتنعة ظاهر عوارها بإفسادها، ومثل هذا لا بالدليل - ألا يرى أن دعوى المتأله لا تصح بمثل هذا لما فيها من الامتناع. يحققه أن قيام المعجزة على يدي المتنبئ إنما لا (۷) يجوز لئلا يؤدي إلى التسوية بين (۱) الحق والباطل أو إلى تعجيز الباري عن إقامة الدليل على ما من الدعاوي والتفرقة بين الحق منها والباطل، وإنما تثبت التسوية أو العجز عن التفرقة إذا كانت الدعوى في نفسها ممكنة غير ممتنعة، فأما عند امتناعها (۲) فلا يؤدي إلى ذلك، ولهذا كان قيام الناقض للعادة على يدي المتأله ممكنا غير ممتنع، والله الموفق.
We say: None of that has been established by tawātur (mass transmission). Rather, what is mentioned is that he inserted the legs of his horse into his belly in the royal court before the king and his retinue, and likewise he placed a basin containing fire on his chest and it did not harm him, and this was not before a multitude of people. Such a report does not necessitate certain knowledge of its content, because it is possible for them to conspire upon falsehood; indeed, the usual state of kings and their followers is to generate reports that have no truth, because of what is in that of subjugating their subjects and managing the affairs of their kingdom. As for what is transmitted from the signs of the messengers, peace be upon them, it is transmitted in a way that allows no possibility of falsehood, and collusion upon the transmitters is inconceivable. And what is of this nature among reports, it necessitates necessary knowledge (al-ʿilm al-ḍarūrī) according to what we have established. And God is the Grantor of success. All the mutakallimūn (theologians) of the People of Islam subscribed to this answer, and some of the verifying scholars of the community answered about this saying: Indeed, that which breaks the custom (nāqiḍ li’l-ʿāda) indicates the occurrence of the possible, not the occurrence of what is impossible (al-mumtaniʿ). Therefore, it is not evidence for the validity of the claim of divinity. And Zoroaster's claim is an impossible claim because of what it contains of saying about a Creator who is incapable and ignorant, from whose evil thought was born one who opposes him, rivals him in his kingdom, and contends with him in his authority, while he is unaware of the consequence of his thought, incapable of subduing his enemy and overcoming him, and he is, despite this, a locus of accidents, since his evil thought occurred in him. All of that is an impossible claim whose falsity is apparent from its corruption. And such does not require a proof? Do you not see that the claim of a claimant to divinity is not valid by such a thing because of the impossibility in it? He confirms that the occurrence of a miracle at the hands of a false prophet is not permitted, lest it lead to equating truth and falsehood, or to [implying] the inability of the Creator to establish evidence concerning the claims and to distinguish between the true and the false among them. And the equating or the inability to distinguish only arises if the claim itself is possible and not impossible. As for when it is impossible, it does not lead to that. Therefore, the occurrence of the custom-breaker at the hands of a claimant to divinity is possible and not impossible. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that Zoroaster performed miracles proving his divinity. The author provides two distinct arguments. First, he argues that the reports of Zoroaster's purported miracles are not mutawātir (mass-transmitted) and therefore do not yield certain knowledge. Such reports can be fabricated by kings and their followers for political purposes. In contrast, the miracles of true prophets are transmitted in a way that precludes falsehood and collusion, thus giving necessary knowledge. Second, the author presents an argument from the verifying scholars: a miracle (nāqiḍ li’l-ʿāda) only proves the occurrence of a possible event, not the truth of an impossible claim. Zoroaster's claim of a weak, ignorant, and competing deity is inherently impossible (mumtaniʿ). Even if such an event occurred, it would not validate his claim. The author elaborates that allowing a miracle for an impossible claim would either equate truth and falsehood or imply God's inability to distinguish, but this only applies when the claim itself is possible. Since Zoroaster's claim is impossible, no such confusion occurs, and the event remains possible without supporting the false claim.

Key Terms
التواتر
العلم الضروري
المعجزة
النقلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any report of a miraculous event is sufficient to prove a claimant's truth.
Correction: The report must be mass-transmitted (mutawātir) to yield certain knowledge; otherwise, it could be fabricated.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why do reports of Zoroaster's miracles not produce certain knowledge?
A) Because they contradict the Quran
B) Because they are not transmitted by tawatur
C) Because they are logically impossible
D) Because they are not mentioned in any scripture

Key Takeaway
The validity of a reported miracle depends on the reliability of its transmission; only mass-transmitted reports yield certain knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author says that kings and their followers generate false reports to subjugate their subjects. Where in your life do you passively accept reports without checking their reliability? Will you commit to verifying claims before letting them shape your worldview?
?
Prophets' miracles are transmitted without any possibility of falsehood. The Quran is such a miracle. Do you treat it as certain knowledge that demands your obedience, or as just another source? What would change if you truly acted as if it were absolutely certain?
?
Zoroaster's alleged miracles were performed before a limited audience. The author implies that limited audiences are suspect. In your own faith, are you relying on reports that only a few have witnessed? How can you ensure your beliefs are based on mass-transmitted certainty?

Why an Impossible Claim Cannot Be Supported by a Miracle
The author explains that a miracle only proves the possibility of an event, and since Zoroaster's claim is impossible, it cannot be supported.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a miracle (nāqiḍ li'l-ʿāda) can only prove a possible claim, and why Zoroaster's impossible claim cannot be validated even by an extraordinary event.

Core Idea
A miracle cannot prove an impossible claim, only a possible one.

The second refutation goes deeper: even if the event occurred, it cannot prove a claim that is inherently impossible. The author explains that a miracle only confirms the possibility of the event, not the truth of the claimant's doctrine. Zoroaster's doctrine regarding a weak and ignorant creator is impossible, so any supposed miracle is irrelevant. This lesson unpacks the logic and the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Focus on the definition of nāqiḍ li'l-ʿāda and its scope.
Note the term 'mumtaniʿ' (impossible) and how it is used.
2
Understand the principle
The author states that a custom-breaking event indicates only the occurrence of a possible thing, not an impossible one. Grasp why this limits what miracles can prove.
This is a key principle in kalam: miracles support possible claims.
3
Apply to Zoroaster's case
The passage explains why Zoroaster's claim is impossible (a weak, ignorant creator). Reflect on why such a claim cannot be validated by any event.
Also consider the argument about equating truth and falsehood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قلنا (١): لم يثبت شيء من ذلك بالتواتر بل (۲) المذكور أنه أدخل قوائم فرسه في بطنه في دار الملك بين يدي الملك وخواصه وكذا وضع طشت فيه نار على صدره فلم يضره ولم يكن عند ملأ من الناس. ومثل هذا الخبر لا يجب العلم بمخبره، لجواز التواطؤ على الكذب عليهم، بل الغالب من حال الملوك وأتباعهم، توليد أخبار لا صحة لها لما في ذلك من تمكين رعيتهم وتسوية أمور مملكتهم. فأما ما نقل من أعلام الرسل عليهم السلام فقد نقل على طريق لا احتمال فيه للكذب، ولا يتصور التواطؤ على النقلة ، وما هذا سبيله من الأخبار فهو موجب للعلم الضروري على ما قررنا والله الموفق. ذهب إلى هذا الجواب(۳) جميع متكلمي أهل الإسلام وأجاب بعض المحققين من علماء الأمة عن هذا فقال: إن الناقض للعادة يدل على ثبوت الممكن لا على ثبوت (٤) ما هو من الممتنع ()، ولهذا لا يكون دليلاً على صحة دعوى التأله، ودعوى زرادشت دعوى ممتنعة لما فيها من القول بصانع عاجز جاهل، تولد من فكرته الردية من (٦) يعاديه ويزاحمه في ملكه وينازعه في سلطانه وهو غير عالم بعاقبة فكره، عاجز عن قهر عدوه وغلبته، وهو مع هذا محل للحوادث، إذ حدثت فيه فكرته الرديئة ، وكل ذلك دعوى ممتنعة ظاهر عوارها بإفسادها، ومثل هذا لا بالدليل - ألا يرى أن دعوى المتأله لا تصح بمثل هذا لما فيها من الامتناع. يحققه أن قيام المعجزة على يدي المتنبئ إنما لا (۷) يجوز لئلا يؤدي إلى التسوية بين (۱) الحق والباطل أو إلى تعجيز الباري عن إقامة الدليل على ما من الدعاوي والتفرقة بين الحق منها والباطل، وإنما تثبت التسوية أو العجز عن التفرقة إذا كانت الدعوى في نفسها ممكنة غير ممتنعة، فأما عند امتناعها (۲) فلا يؤدي إلى ذلك، ولهذا كان قيام الناقض للعادة على يدي المتأله ممكنا غير ممتنع، والله الموفق.
We say: None of that has been established by tawātur (mass transmission). Rather, what is mentioned is that he inserted the legs of his horse into his belly in the royal court before the king and his retinue, and likewise he placed a basin containing fire on his chest and it did not harm him, and this was not before a multitude of people. Such a report does not necessitate certain knowledge of its content, because it is possible for them to conspire upon falsehood; indeed, the usual state of kings and their followers is to generate reports that have no truth, because of what is in that of subjugating their subjects and managing the affairs of their kingdom. As for what is transmitted from the signs of the messengers, peace be upon them, it is transmitted in a way that allows no possibility of falsehood, and collusion upon the transmitters is inconceivable. And what is of this nature among reports, it necessitates necessary knowledge (al-ʿilm al-ḍarūrī) according to what we have established. And God is the Grantor of success. All the mutakallimūn (theologians) of the People of Islam subscribed to this answer, and some of the verifying scholars of the community answered about this saying: Indeed, that which breaks the custom (nāqiḍ li’l-ʿāda) indicates the occurrence of the possible, not the occurrence of what is impossible (al-mumtaniʿ). Therefore, it is not evidence for the validity of the claim of divinity. And Zoroaster's claim is an impossible claim because of what it contains of saying about a Creator who is incapable and ignorant, from whose evil thought was born one who opposes him, rivals him in his kingdom, and contends with him in his authority, while he is unaware of the consequence of his thought, incapable of subduing his enemy and overcoming him, and he is, despite this, a locus of accidents, since his evil thought occurred in him. All of that is an impossible claim whose falsity is apparent from its corruption. And such does not require a proof? Do you not see that the claim of a claimant to divinity is not valid by such a thing because of the impossibility in it? He confirms that the occurrence of a miracle at the hands of a false prophet is not permitted, lest it lead to equating truth and falsehood, or to [implying] the inability of the Creator to establish evidence concerning the claims and to distinguish between the true and the false among them. And the equating or the inability to distinguish only arises if the claim itself is possible and not impossible. As for when it is impossible, it does not lead to that. Therefore, the occurrence of the custom-breaker at the hands of a claimant to divinity is possible and not impossible. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that Zoroaster performed miracles proving his divinity. The author provides two distinct arguments. First, he argues that the reports of Zoroaster's purported miracles are not mutawātir (mass-transmitted) and therefore do not yield certain knowledge. Such reports can be fabricated by kings and their followers for political purposes. In contrast, the miracles of true prophets are transmitted in a way that precludes falsehood and collusion, thus giving necessary knowledge. Second, the author presents an argument from the verifying scholars: a miracle (nāqiḍ li’l-ʿāda) only proves the occurrence of a possible event, not the truth of an impossible claim. Zoroaster's claim of a weak, ignorant, and competing deity is inherently impossible (mumtaniʿ). Even if such an event occurred, it would not validate his claim. The author elaborates that allowing a miracle for an impossible claim would either equate truth and falsehood or imply God's inability to distinguish, but this only applies when the claim itself is possible. Since Zoroaster's claim is impossible, no such confusion occurs, and the event remains possible without supporting the false claim.

Key Terms
الناقض للعادة
الممتنع
الممكن
المعجزة
التسوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If someone performs a miracle, it automatically proves their religious claim is true.
Correction: A miracle only indicates the possibility of the event; the claim itself must be inherently possible for the miracle to support it.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why cannot Zoroaster's claimed miracles prove his divinity?
A) Because the miracles are not well-documented
B) Because his claim is inherently impossible
C) Because miracles only occur for prophets
D) Because he did not perform any actual miracles

Key Takeaway
A miracle testifies to the possibility of an event, not the truth of an impossible doctrine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear of a miracle claim today (like a vision or healing), do you examine the content of the claim itself, or do you accept it as evidence because it is extraordinary? This lesson demands you to judge the claim's possibility first. How will you change your approach?
?
Zoroaster's claim was impossible because it attributed weakness and ignorance to the Creator. Is there any belief you hold about God that might inadvertently imply a deficiency? Let this lesson search your heart for any subtle anthropomorphism or limitation you might be ascribing to Him.
?
The author says a miracle for an impossible claim would equate truth and falsehood. Are you treating all claims of divine experiences as equally valid, even when they contradict tawheed? This is a matter of justice to the truth. Will you commit to distinguishing between possible and impossible claims before accepting any sign?

Miracles

Miracles Transcend Natural and Psychic Causes
Nasafi argues miracles transcend natural and psychic explanations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophetic miracles cannot be attributed to natural laws or psychic manipulation according to Imam Nasafi.

Core Idea
Miracles are neither natural nor psychic; they are divine acts beyond all created powers.

Before we can fully appreciate the proof of prophethood through miracles, we must first clear away two common misconceptions: that miracles might be merely rare natural phenomena or advanced forms of magic. In this passage, Imam Nasafi lays out the categorical distinction, using well-known examples from the Prophet's ﷺ life to show that miracles belong to a realm entirely their own.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice how Nasafi lists specific miracles and then rules out two possible explanations.
The examples are concrete: a roasted sheep revived, a she-camel speaking, a pillar moaning, water from fingers, the moon splitting.
2
Identify the two rejections
Nasafi first rejects natural causes (asrar al-taba'i'), then rejects psychic powers (quwa nafsaniyya). Underline the phrases that show each rejection.
For psychic powers, he splits them into sorcery/incantations and sleight of hand.
3
Reflect on the argument's structure
Nasafi does not prove here that miracles are impossible under natural or psychic causes; he appeals to the knowledge of experts in those fields. This is a preliminary argument before a deeper proof.
The passage ends by promising further clarification later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصول الطبيعية العارفين بما يجوز أن يترتب تحتها وما لا يجوز متيقنون أن إحياء الشاة المصليَّة وإنطاق الناقة وإلجاء الأسطوانة إلى الحنين، ونبع الماء من بين الأصابع، مما لا يجوز ترتبها تحت أسرار الطبائع، وكذا شق القمر وغيره على ما نبين إذا انتهينا إلى إقامة الدليل على ذلك إن شاء الله تعالى - ولا بالقوى النفسانية إذ الملتحق بالتدابير النفسانية إما أن يترتب تحت السحر والعزائم أو تحت اللطف والشعبذة، والعالمون بهذه الأمور يعرفون أن ما أتى به من المعجزات خارج عن هذه الوجوه، ونكشف عن ذلك أيضا بعد هذا - إن شاء الله تعالى.
Those who know natural principles and what can and cannot be subsumed under them are certain that reviving the roasted sheep, making the she-camel speak, causing the pillar to yearn, and water flowing from the fingers are not of the kind that can be subsumed under the secrets of natures; likewise the splitting of the moon and other things, as we will explain when we come to establish the proof for that, God willing. Nor are they [subsumable] under psychic powers, for what is attached to psychic manipulations is either subsumed under sorcery and incantations or under beguiling [lutf] and sleight of hand [shu'badha]; and those knowledgeable in these matters know that what was brought of miracles is beyond these ways, and we will reveal that also after this, God willing.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a general argument that the miracles of prophets cannot be attributed to natural causes (asrar al-taba'i') nor to psychic powers (quwa nafsaniyya). The author first states that those well-versed in the principles of nature know that certain miraculous events—like bringing a roasted sheep back to life, making a she-camel speak, causing a pillar to moan in longing, and water flowing from between the Prophet’s fingers—cannot be accounted for by the hidden properties of nature. Similarly, the splitting of the moon and other miracles are also beyond natural explanation. The author then rules out psychic powers, noting that anything achieved through psychological means falls under either sorcery (sihr) and incantations ('aza'im) or under beguiling and sleight of hand (shu'badha). Those who are experts in these arts recognize that the miracles brought by the Prophet are outside these categories. The author promises to elaborate further proofs for this later.

Key Terms
أسرار الطبائع
السحر
العزائم
اللطف
الشعبذة
المعجزات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are just advanced forms of magic or rare natural phenomena.
Correction: Nasafi explains that miracles are beyond the secrets of nature and beyond sorcery, incantations, or sleight of hand. They are categorically different.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why can miracles not be attributed to psychic powers?
A) Because miracles are always more impressive.
B) Because psychic powers fall under sorcery, incantations, or sleight of hand, and miracles are beyond these.
C) Because psychic powers do not exist.
D) Because miracles violate logical laws.

Key Takeaway
Prophetic miracles are entirely beyond natural causes and psychic powers, establishing them as divine signs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear or read about the miracles of the Prophet ﷺ, do you find yourself mentally explaining them away as exaggerated stories or natural coincidences? What does that reveal about your heart's certainty in the truth of prophethood?
?
If a miracle were to happen before your eyes today, would you immediately recognize it as a sign from Allah, or would you search for a natural or psychic explanation? How can you train yourself to see divine intervention in your daily life?

First Division: Prophet's Unlettered People and Knowledge of Unseen
Al-Nasafi details the first division: the Prophet's unlettered people and his knowledge of the unseen.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's background of being from an unlettered people, combined with his knowledge of the unseen, serves as a proof of prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet knew what he could not have learned from his environment.

Al-Nasafi begins by examining the Prophet's background in an unlettered desert community. He argues that the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen, despite the lack of any teachers or scriptures, could only come from divine revelation. In this lesson, we explore the first proof from the Prophet's state: his people and their ignorance, contrasted with his own knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Start by reading the Arabic text for the first division. Notice the multiple Quranic verses cited.
The passage uses several verses to reinforce the argument.
2
Identify the key claim
The central claim is that the Prophet knew news of the unseen without any human teacher. Identify how Al-Nasafi establishes this.
3
Understand the verses
Look at each Quranic verse cited and see how it supports the argument that the Prophet's knowledge is from Allah.
The verse from Al 'Imran 3:61 is particularly strong as it relates to the challenge of mubahala.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this is considered a miracle: the Prophet's complete lack of exposure to learning, yet he brings knowledge no one else had.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما هو راجع إلى حاله فمنقسم إلى أقسام أربعة: أحدها: ما هو راجع إلى قومه فإنه كان من قوم لا يعرفون الكتب ودراستها، وكانت بلدتهم في البراري لا يشهدها إلا الأعراب الأميون الذين كان الغالب عليهم الجهل، ثم هو لم يغب عنهم إلا مدة يسيرة في سفره إلى الشام مع العير، ولم يغب عنهم، ولم يقدم عليهم مكة أحد من أحبار أهل الكتاب والعلماء بشرائع الأمم المتقدمة يختصه ممن هو دونه ويعتكف على تعريفه ما في الكتب السالفة، ثم إنه علم أنباء الغيب الذي لم يكن يعلمها هو ولا أحد من قومه، وبلغ في ذلك الثقة به والطمأنينة إليه إلى أن قال عند مجادلتهم إياه: تَعَالَوْا نَدْعُ أَبْنَاءَنَا وَأَبْنَاءَكُمْ (آل عمران 61) وقال تعالى: تِلْكَ مِنْ أَنْبَاءِ الْغَيْبِ نُوحِيهَا إِلَيْكَ مَا كُنْتَ تَعْلَمُهَا أَنْتَ وَلَا قَوْمُكَ (هود 49) ولم ينسبه أحد منهم إلى تعلم قد تفرد به وأنفق عمره في تحصيله، وقال تعالى: أَمْ لَمْ يَعْرِفُوا رَسُولَهُمْ فَهُمْ لَهُ مُنْكَرُونَ (المؤمنون 69) وقال: وَمَا كُنْتَ تَتْلُو مِنْ قَبْلِهِ مِنْ كِتَابٍ وَلَا تَخُطُّهُ بِيَمِينِكَ إِذًا لَارْتَابَ الْمُبْطِلُونَ (العنكبوت 48) وقال: فَقَدْ لَبِثْتُ فِيكُمْ عُمُرًا مِنْ قَبْلِهِ أَفَلَا تَعْقِلُونَ (يونس 16). والثاني: أنه لم يكن قبل إظهار الدعوة متكلما، ولا خائضا في نظم الكلام وتأليفه، ولو كان شرع في شيء من ذلك لظهر لمعاشريه ولما خفى على أهل بطانته، وليس من طباع البشر التصدي لمثل ذلك الخطب الجليل والتعرض لمخالفة العالم فجأة بلا مقدمة ولا القدرة على الإتيان بكلام يعجز عنه الخلق بغتة من غير تدريج.
As for what relates to his state, it is divided into four sections: The first: what relates to his people, for he was from a people who did not know books and their study, and their town was in the deserts, which none but unlettered Bedouins, most of whom were ignorant, frequented. Moreover, he did not leave them except for a short time during his travel to Syria with the caravan, nor did he absent himself from them, nor did any of the rabbis of the People of the Book and scholars of the laws of previous nations come to Mecca specifically to him from among those inferior to him and devote themselves to teaching him what was in the former scriptures. Then he knew the news of the unseen, which neither he nor any of his people knew, and he reached in that confidence and tranquility to the extent that he said, while they were arguing with him, 'Come, let us call our sons and your sons' (Al 'Imran 3:61). And Allah said: 'These are of the news of the unseen which We reveal to you; you did not know them, neither you nor your people' (Hud 11:49). And none of them attributed him to learning that he had specialized in and spent his life acquiring. And Allah said: 'Or did they not recognize their Messenger, so they deny him?' (Al-Mu'minun 23:69). And He said: 'And you did not recite before it any scripture, nor did you write it with your right hand; then the falsifiers would have doubted' (Al-'Ankabut 29:48). And He said: 'I have remained among you a lifetime before it; do you not reason?' (Yunus 10:16). The second: that he was not, before declaring his call, a speaker [of eloquent speech], nor did he engage in the composition and arrangement of speech. Had he embarked on anything of that, it would have appeared to his contemporaries and would not have been hidden from his close associates. And it is not in human nature to undertake such a great matter and to expose oneself to opposing the world suddenly without preparation, nor to have the ability to produce speech that creation is incapable of, all at once without gradual progression.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage details the first two of four divisions of miracles related to the Prophet's state (ḥala). The first division concerns his people and environment: he came from an unlettered (ummī) tribe, living in a desert region with no exposure to scripture or scholars, yet he brought knowledge of the unseen and challenged others to malediction (mubāhala) with confidence. Al-Nasafi cites multiple Quranic verses (Al 'Imran 3:61, Hud 11:49, Al-Mu'minun 23:69, Al-'Ankabut 29:48, Yunus 10:16) to prove that his knowledge could only be from divine revelation. The second division argues that before prophethood, he never practiced eloquent speech or composed rhetorical works; his sudden ability to produce the inimitable Qur'an demonstrates divine intervention. Human nature cannot suddenly produce such sublime speech without gradual learning, so this too is a miracle.

Key Terms
أعراب أميون
أنباء الغيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's knowledge could have come from brief travel or from visiting scholars.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows he only traveled once to Syria briefly, and no scholars came to him; thus, his knowledge could only be from divine revelation.

Checkpoint
What evidence does al-Nasafi give that the Prophet did not learn from scholars?
A) He lived in a desert town with no scholars.
B) He traveled to Syria many times.
C) He was taught by rabbis in Mecca.
D) He read ancient scriptures.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's knowledge of the unseen, despite his unlettered environment, is a clear sign of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet knew the unseen despite his unlettered background. Do I truly believe that his knowledge came directly from Allah, or do I unconsciously reduce it to human factors? How does that affect my submission to his message?
?
If the Prophet’s environment offered no apparent means for his knowledge, what does that say about my own tendency to rely on external credentials and human learning for spiritual certainty? Am I willing to trust revelation over my own understanding?
?
The Prophet confidently challenged others to a prayer of curse (mubahala) because of his certainty. Is my faith in the truth of Islam accompanied by that same level of conviction? If not, what is holding me back from surrendering fully?
