Second Division: The Prophet's Sudden Eloquence as a Miracle
Al-Nasafi presents the second division: the Prophet's lack of prior rhetorical skill.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet's sudden ability to produce the Qur'an without prior rhetorical training is considered a miracle.

Core Idea
The Qur'an's eloquence came without prior preparation.

Al-Nasafi's second division focuses on the Prophet's lack of pre-prophethood engagement with eloquent speech. He argues that human nature cannot suddenly produce speech of such high quality without gradual learning. In this lesson, we explore this second proof from the Prophet's state.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the second division passage. Note the comparison between human nature and the sudden appearance of the Qur'an.
2
Identify the claim
The claim is that the Prophet was not a speaker or composer before prophethood. How does Al-Nasafi support this?
3
Understand the logical argument
Al-Nasafi argues that if the Prophet had practiced, it would have been known to his contemporaries. His sudden ability is against human nature.
4
Reflect on the miracle
This shows the Qur'an is not a human product; it is divine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما هو راجع إلى حاله فمنقسم إلى أقسام أربعة: أحدها: ما هو راجع إلى قومه فإنه كان من قوم لا يعرفون الكتب ودراستها، وكانت بلدتهم في البراري لا يشهدها إلا الأعراب الأميون الذين كان الغالب عليهم الجهل، ثم هو لم يغب عنهم إلا مدة يسيرة في سفره إلى الشام مع العير، ولم يغب عنهم، ولم يقدم عليهم مكة أحد من أحبار أهل الكتاب والعلماء بشرائع الأمم المتقدمة يختصه ممن هو دونه ويعتكف على تعريفه ما في الكتب السالفة، ثم إنه علم أنباء الغيب الذي لم يكن يعلمها هو ولا أحد من قومه، وبلغ في ذلك الثقة به والطمأنينة إليه إلى أن قال عند مجادلتهم إياه: تَعَالَوْا نَدْعُ أَبْنَاءَنَا وَأَبْنَاءَكُمْ (آل عمران 61) وقال تعالى: تِلْكَ مِنْ أَنْبَاءِ الْغَيْبِ نُوحِيهَا إِلَيْكَ مَا كُنْتَ تَعْلَمُهَا أَنْتَ وَلَا قَوْمُكَ (هود 49) ولم ينسبه أحد منهم إلى تعلم قد تفرد به وأنفق عمره في تحصيله، وقال تعالى: أَمْ لَمْ يَعْرِفُوا رَسُولَهُمْ فَهُمْ لَهُ مُنْكَرُونَ (المؤمنون 69) وقال: وَمَا كُنْتَ تَتْلُو مِنْ قَبْلِهِ مِنْ كِتَابٍ وَلَا تَخُطُّهُ بِيَمِينِكَ إِذًا لَارْتَابَ الْمُبْطِلُونَ (العنكبوت 48) وقال: فَقَدْ لَبِثْتُ فِيكُمْ عُمُرًا مِنْ قَبْلِهِ أَفَلَا تَعْقِلُونَ (يونس 16). والثاني: أنه لم يكن قبل إظهار الدعوة متكلما، ولا خائضا في نظم الكلام وتأليفه، ولو كان شرع في شيء من ذلك لظهر لمعاشريه ولما خفى على أهل بطانته، وليس من طباع البشر التصدي لمثل ذلك الخطب الجليل والتعرض لمخالفة العالم فجأة بلا مقدمة ولا القدرة على الإتيان بكلام يعجز عنه الخلق بغتة من غير تدريج.
As for what relates to his state, it is divided into four sections: The first: what relates to his people, for he was from a people who did not know books and their study, and their town was in the deserts, which none but unlettered Bedouins, most of whom were ignorant, frequented. Moreover, he did not leave them except for a short time during his travel to Syria with the caravan, nor did he absent himself from them, nor did any of the rabbis of the People of the Book and scholars of the laws of previous nations come to Mecca specifically to him from among those inferior to him and devote themselves to teaching him what was in the former scriptures. Then he knew the news of the unseen, which neither he nor any of his people knew, and he reached in that confidence and tranquility to the extent that he said, while they were arguing with him, 'Come, let us call our sons and your sons' (Al 'Imran 3:61). And Allah said: 'These are of the news of the unseen which We reveal to you; you did not know them, neither you nor your people' (Hud 11:49). And none of them attributed him to learning that he had specialized in and spent his life acquiring. And Allah said: 'Or did they not recognize their Messenger, so they deny him?' (Al-Mu'minun 23:69). And He said: 'And you did not recite before it any scripture, nor did you write it with your right hand; then the falsifiers would have doubted' (Al-'Ankabut 29:48). And He said: 'I have remained among you a lifetime before it; do you not reason?' (Yunus 10:16). The second: that he was not, before declaring his call, a speaker [of eloquent speech], nor did he engage in the composition and arrangement of speech. Had he embarked on anything of that, it would have appeared to his contemporaries and would not have been hidden from his close associates. And it is not in human nature to undertake such a great matter and to expose oneself to opposing the world suddenly without preparation, nor to have the ability to produce speech that creation is incapable of, all at once without gradual progression.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage details the first two of four divisions of miracles related to the Prophet's state (ḥala). The first division concerns his people and environment: he came from an unlettered (ummī) tribe, living in a desert region with no exposure to scripture or scholars, yet he brought knowledge of the unseen and challenged others to malediction (mubāhala) with confidence. Al-Nasafi cites multiple Quranic verses (Al 'Imran 3:61, Hud 11:49, Al-Mu'minun 23:69, Al-'Ankabut 29:48, Yunus 10:16) to prove that his knowledge could only be from divine revelation. The second division argues that before prophethood, he never practiced eloquent speech or composed rhetorical works; his sudden ability to produce the inimitable Qur'an demonstrates divine intervention. Human nature cannot suddenly produce such sublime speech without gradual learning, so this too is a miracle.

Key Terms
متكلما
نظم الكلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's eloquence was a natural talent that developed over time.
Correction: Al-Nasafi argues that he never engaged in such speech before, and human nature cannot produce such high-level speech without gradual learning.

Checkpoint
What does al-Nasafi say about human nature regarding sudden eloquence?
A) It is possible to produce great speech suddenly.
B) It is not possible without gradual progression.
C) It is possible with divine help.
D) It is common among poets.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's sudden eloquence is a miracle because it defies human nature's need for gradual learning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet had no prior eloquence, yet Allah gave him the Qur’an. In what area of your life are you waiting to be 'qualified' before obeying Allah, when He might simply give you what you need without your preparation?
?
If the Prophet's sudden eloquence is a miracle, then every good deed and ability you have is likewise a gift from Allah. Do you silently boast about your achievements, or do you genuinely attribute them to His grace in your heart?
?
The source says it is 'not in human nature' to suddenly change the world. Yet the Prophet did. Are you still making excuses for your own spiritual stagnation, or will you ask Allah for the same unearned transformation?

Miracles of the Prophet Through Answered Prayers
Author enumerates several miracles of the Prophet through answered prayers and declares them mutawatir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's answered prayers serve as mutawatir evidence for his prophethood, supported by several historically transmitted events.

Core Idea
The Prophet's answered prayers are mass-transmitted miracles proving his prophethood.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla presents a series of events where the Prophet's supplications were directly answered by Allah. These include prayers for rain, against enemies, and for companions. The author emphasizes that these reports are mutawatir, meaning they have been transmitted by so many chains that their truth is certain. Before reading the passage, consider: Why would the mass transmission of these miracles strengthen the case for prophethood?

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the miracles
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. As you read, list each miracle mentioned. Notice that the author begins with a reference to Yusuf (likely continuing from a previous discussion).
The passage uses numbered footnotes in the Arabic; these correspond to the translation.
2
Understand the claim of tawatur
The author states 'وذلك كله منقول بالتواتر' (all of that is transmitted via tawatur). Tawatur means multiple independent chains of transmission that preclude collusion. Ask yourself: How does this claim affect the reliability of these miracles?
Tawatur is a key concept in Islamic epistemology for establishing certainty.
3
Reflect on the diversity of miracles
Notice the range: from natural phenomena (rain, drought) to supernatural interventions (dog, blindness, sinking ground). This diversity strengthens the proof as they are not isolated incidents.
Each miracle addresses a different need: relief from hardship, protection, punishment, and blessing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يوسف (۱) فأمسك عنهم القطر حتى جف النبات والشجر وهلكت المواشي. وكان انكشاف الجدب عنهم أيضًا بدعائه فأتاهم الغيث وكثر حتى هدم بيوتهم فكلموه في ذلك فقال : "اللهم حوالينا ولا علينا، اللهم على الظراب والجبال وبطون الأودية(۲) وذلك كله منقول بالتواتر. ومن ذلك دعاؤه على كسرى حين مزق كتابه وبعث إليه بتراب فقال: "اللهم" مزق ملكه كل ممزق (۳). وقال لأصحابه: "مزق كتابي أما إنه ستمزق أمته، وبعث إلي بالتراب أما إنكم ستملكون أرضه"(4). فمزق الله ملكه، وشتت جمعه، وملكهم أرضه (٥) . ومن ذلك دعاؤه على (٦) عتبة بن أبى لهب : اللهم سلط عليه كلبًا من كلابك "(۱) فافترسه الأسد في بعض أسفاره، ومنها دعاؤه(1) لعبد الله بن عباس بالفقه والحكمة فحصل ما دعا ومنها ما أعمى الله تعالى رضي الله عنهما - • أبصار الظالمين له حين كان في الغار ومنها ما ساخ بقوائم فرس من اتبعه في الأرض بدعائه، وفي ذلك كثرة ، وفي هذا القدر كفاية.
Yusuf (1) – then He withheld from them the rain until vegetation and trees dried up and livestock perished. And the removal of the drought from them was also through his prayer, so He brought them abundant rain until it destroyed their houses, so they spoke to him about that, and he said: 'O Allah, around us and not upon us; O Allah, upon the hills, the mountains, and the valleys' (2) – and all of that is transmitted via tawatur. And among that is his prayer against Kisra when he tore up his letter and sent him some dust, saying: 'O Allah, tear his kingdom asunder' (3). And he said to his companions: 'He tore up my letter; indeed his nation will be torn asunder, and he sent me dust; indeed you will possess his land' (4). So Allah tore apart his kingdom, scattered his assembly, and made them inherit his land (5). And among that is his prayer against 'Utbah ibn Abi Lahab: 'O Allah, set upon him a dog from among Your dogs' (1) – so a lion devoured him on one of his travels. And among that is his prayer for 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas for understanding (fiqh) and wisdom, and what he prayed for was obtained. And among that is that Allah blinded the sight of the oppressors at the time when he was in the cave. And among that is that He sank the hooves of the horse of one of his followers into the earth by his prayer. There is abundance in that, and in this amount is sufficient.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage enumerates several miracles of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) that occurred through his supplications being answered. The author begins by noting a narrative involving 'Yusuf' (likely a continuation from the previous page) about drought relief: the Prophet prayed for rain to be diverted around rather than upon them, and it came abundantly. He then states that all these reports are transmitted by tawatur (mass transmission), indicating their reliability.

The next miracle is the Prophet's prayer against Kisra (the Persian emperor) after Kisra tore up his letter. The Prophet prayed for his kingdom to be torn apart, and it was; later the Muslims conquered Persia. Then the prayer against 'Utbah ibn Abi Lahab, that a dog would be set upon him; a lion killed him during a journey. Then the prayer for 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas for deep understanding of religion and wisdom, which was granted – Ibn 'Abbas became a great scholar. Then the blinding of the oppressors when the Prophet was in the cave during the Hijra, preventing his enemies from seeing him. Finally, the sinking of a horse's hooves into the earth for a follower who was being pursued.

The author concludes that these miracles are numerous, and the mentioned examples suffice as proof of prophethood.

Key Terms
تواتر
دعاء
كسرى
عتبة بن أبي لهب
عبد الله بن عباس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These miracle stories are legendary fabrications from later centuries.
Correction: The author asserts they are mutawatir, meaning they have been transmitted through so many independent chains that their historical certainty is beyond doubt, and they are recorded in authentic hadith collections.

Checkpoint
What method of transmission does the author claim for these miracles?
A) Ahad (single narration)
B) Tawatur (mass transmission)
C) Ijma' (consensus)
D) Qiyas (analogy)

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's miracles through answered prayers are mass-transmitted (mutawatir) and thus constitute undeniable proof of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet's prayers were answered in ways that changed history. If you truly believe he is the final messenger, why do you not turn to him with your deepest needs? What concrete step will you take this week to seek his intercession or follow his sunnah more closely?
?
The author says these miracles are so massively transmitted that they cannot be denied. Are you as certain of his prophethood as you are of the sun rising? What would change in your daily life if you truly lived with that level of certainty?
?
Ibn 'Abbas became a great scholar through the Prophet's prayer for him. What prevents you from seeking the Prophet's guidance in your own quest for knowledge? Will you commit to reading his biography or a hadith collection this month, asking Allah to bless you with understanding?

Prophetic Foreknowledge: Historical Examples
Author lists five examples of the Prophet's accurate predictions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand five specific incidents where the Prophet Muhammad accurately predicted future events, demonstrating that his knowledge came from divine revelation.

Core Idea
The Prophet's accurate predictions prove his prophethood.

To demonstrate that the Prophet Muhammad possessed knowledge of the unseen, the author presents several historical incidents. These events could not have been known through ordinary means, serving as clear evidence that he was inspired by God.

Guided Path
1
Read the five examples
Read through each incident carefully. Notice the specific details the Prophet revealed: the location of a lost camel, the activity of an enemy, a secret financial arrangement, and the private conversations of hypocrites.
The examples range from public to private matters.
2
Identify the common pattern
In each story, the Prophet announces something that no human could have known at that time, and it turns out exactly as he said. This consistency shows that his knowledge was not guesswork.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: if a person repeatedly makes accurate predictions about hidden or future events, what does that say about the source of his knowledge? This leads to the conclusion that he is a true prophet.
The author uses these examples as building blocks for a larger argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مِنْ ذَلِكَ حَدِيثُ لَيْلَةِ الْإِسْرَاءِ وَمَا أَخْبَرَ مِنْ أَخْبَارِ عِيرِ قُرَيْشٍ، وَكَانَ كَمَا. وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ أَنَّهُ ضَلَّتْ لَهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ نَاقَةٌ فَأَقْبَلَ يَسْأَلُ النَّاسَ عَنْهَا فَقَالَ الْمُنَافِقُونَ: هَذَا مُحَمَّدٌ يُخْبِرُكُمْ خَبَرَ السَّمَاءِ وَهُوَ لَا يَدْرِي أَيْنَ نَاقَتُهُ، فَصَعِدَ الْمِنْبَرَ وَحَمِدَ اللَّهَ وَأَثْنَى عَلَيْهِ، وَحَكَى قَوْلَهُمْ ثُمَّ قَالَ: إِنِّي لَا أَعْلَمُ إِلَّا مَا أَعْلَمَنِي رَبِّي وَقَدْ أَخْبَرَنِي أَنَّهَا فِي وَادِي كَذَا مُتَعَلِّقٌ زِمَامُهَا بِشَجَرَةٍ فَبَادَرَ النَّاسُ فَوَجَدُوهَا كَذَلِكَ. وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ قَوْلُهُ لِخَالِدِ بْنِ الْوَلِيدِ حِينَ بَعَثَهُ إِلَى أَكِيدَرِ دُومَةِ الْجَنْدَلِ: "أَمَا إِنَّكُمْ سَتَأْتُونَهُ فَتَجِدُونَهُ يَصِيدُ الْبَقَرَ" فَوَجَدُوهُ كَذَلِكَ. وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لِلْعَبَّاسِ حِينَ أَسَرَهُ: "اِفْدِ نَفْسَكَ وَابْنَيْ أَخِيكَ" يَعْنِي عَقِيلَ بْنَ أَبِي طَالِبٍ وَنَوْفَلَ بْنَ الْحَارِثَةِ- فَإِنَّكَ ذُو مَالٍ فَقَالَ: لَا مَالَ عِنْدِي. قَالَ: فَأَيْنَ الْمَالُ الَّذِي وَضَعْتَهُ بِمَكَّةَ عِنْدَ أُمِّ الْفَضْلِ وَلَيْسَ مَعَكُمَا أَحَدٌ، فَقُلْتَ: إِنْ أَصَبْتُ فِي سَفَرِي فَلِلْفَضْلِ كَذَا، وَلِعَبْدِ اللَّهِ كَذَا، وَلِفُلَانٍ كَذَا؟ فَقَالَ الْعَبَّاسُ: وَالَّذِي بَعَثَكَ بِالْحَقِّ نَبِيًّا مَا عَلِمَ بِهَذَا أَحَدٌ غَيْرِي، وَإِنَّكَ لَرَسُولُ اللَّهِ وَأَسْلَمَ هُوَ وَعَقِيلٌ. وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ مَا كَانَ يُخْبِرُ أَهْلَ النِّفَاقِ بِمَا كَانُوا يَقُولُونَ فِيمَا بَيْنَهُمْ وَيَبِيتُونَ مَا لَا يَرْضَى مِنَ الْقَوْلِ حَتَّى كَانُوا مِنْ شِدَّةِ تَعَنُّتِهِمْ يُحْذَرُونَ أَنْ يَنْزِلَ عَلَيْهِ سُورَةٌ تُنْبِئُهُمْ بِمَا فِي قُلُوبِهِمْ، وَأَمْثَالُ ذَلِكَ كَثِيرٌ، وَكِتَابُنَا هَذَا يَضِيقُ عَنْ ذِكْرِ عُشْرِ ذَلِكَ فَضْلًا عَنْ كُلِّهِ، وَاللَّهُ الْمُوَفِّقُ. ثُمَّ إِنَّ جَمِيعَ مَا أَخْبَرَ مِنَ الْأَخْبَارِ الْكَائِنَةِ فِي الْمُسْتَقْبَلِ خَرَجَ عَلَى مَا أَخْبَرَ مِنْ غَيْرِ تَمَكُّنِ كَذِبٍ أَوْ حَلِفٍ فِي شَيْءٍ مِنْ ذَلِكَ لَا كَمِثْلِ أَخْبَارِ الْكَهَنَةِ وَالْمُنَجِّمِينَ الَّذِينَ يَضِلُّ صِدْقُهُمْ فِي كَذِبِهِمْ وَحَقُّهُمْ فِي بَاطِلِهِمْ عَلَى أَنَّ حَالَتَهُ كَانَتْ تُخَالِفُ حَالَةَ الْكَهَنَةِ فِي طَهَارَتِهِ وَطِيِّبِهِ وَاشْتِغَالِهِ بِالطَّاعَاتِ وَالْعِبَادَاتِ. وَتَقَدُّرِ أُولَئِكَ وَتَنْجِسِهِمْ وَتَقَرُّبِهِمْ إِلَى الشَّيَاطِينِ وَالْأَرْوَاحِ الْخَبِيثَةِ، وَكَذَا كَانَتْ أَخْبَارُهُ صَادِرَةً عَنْهُ عَنْ طَرِيقِ الْغَيْبِ الَّذِي أَعْلَمَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى مِنْ غَيْرِ الِاشْتِغَالِ بِالنَّظَرِ فِي النُّجُومِ وَالتَّأَمُّلِ فِي الطَّالِعِ وَالِارْتِفَاعِ وَتَعَرُّفِ ذَلِكَ مِنْ قِبَلِ الرَّيْحِ وَالْإِسْطِرْلَابِ وَغَيْرِ ذَلِكَ مِمَّا يَفْعَلُهُ الْمُنَجِّمَةُ، فَكَانَ ذَلِكَ مِنْ بَابِ نَقْضِ الْعَادَةِ كَإِلَانَةِ الْحَدِيدِ وَاتِّخَاذِ الدُّرُوعِ بِلَا آلَاتٍ وَلَا اسْتِعْمَالِ النَّارِ.
Among that is the hadith of the Night Journey and what he informed of the news of the Quraysh caravan, and it was as [he said]. And among that is that a she-camel of his, peace be upon him, was lost, so he began asking people about it, so the hypocrites said: 'This Muhammad tells you the news of heaven while he does not know where his she-camel is.' So he ascended the pulpit, praised God and extolled Him, related their statement, then said: 'I do not know except what my Lord has taught me, and He has informed me that it is in such-and-such a valley, its halter entangled in a tree.' So the people hurried and found it thus. And among that is his statement to Khalid ibn al-Walid when he sent him to Ukaydir of Dumah al-Jandal: 'Indeed you will come to him and find him hunting cows.' So they found him thus. And among that is his statement, peace be upon him, to al-Abbas when he captured him: 'Ransom yourself and your brother's two sons'—meaning Aqeel ibn Abi Talib and Nawfal ibn al-Haritha—'for you are a man of wealth.' So he said: 'I have no wealth.' He said: 'Then where is the wealth that you placed in Mecca with Umm al-Fadl, with no one else with you, and you said: If I am killed on my journey, then for al-Fadl such-and-such, for Abdullah such-and-such, and for so-and-so such-and-such?' So al-Abbas said: 'By the One Who sent you with the truth as a prophet, no one but me knew this, and indeed you are the Messenger of God.' And he and Aqeel embraced Islam. And among that is what he used to inform the hypocrites of what they were saying among themselves and plotting at night of speech that is not pleasing, until they, due to the intensity of their obstinacy, feared that a surah would be revealed to him informing them of what was in their hearts. And examples of that are many, and this book of ours is too narrow to mention a tenth of that, let alone all of it, and God is the grantor of success. Then all the news of future events that he informed of turned out as he informed, without any possibility of falsehood or failure in any of that, unlike the news of soothsayers and astrologers, whose truth is lost among their falsehood and their right among their wrong—although his state differed from the state of soothsayers in his purity, goodness, and occupation with acts of obedience and worship, while those ones are unclean, defiled, and seek closeness to devils and evil spirits. And likewise, his reports were issued by him through the unseen which God, exalted, taught him, without engaging in examining the stars, contemplating the ascendant and elevation, or knowing that by means of the wind, astrolabe, or other things that astrologers do. So that was of the category of breaking the norm, like softening iron and making coats of mail without tools or use of fire.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a proof from miracles, specifically the miracle of prophetic foreknowledge (al-ikhbar bi al-ghayb). The author presents multiple historical incidents to demonstrate that the Prophet Muhammad accurately predicted future events without any ordinary means of knowledge, thereby establishing his prophethood. The passage proceeds as follows:

1. The first example is the Night Journey (al-isra'), where the Prophet informed about the Quraysh caravan, and it happened exactly as he said.
2. The second example: the Prophet's camel was lost. Hypocrites mocked him, saying he claims to know news from heaven yet cannot find his camel. The Prophet, after praising God, revealed that the camel was in a specific valley with its halter caught in a tree, and people found it exactly there.
3. The third example: when sending Khalid ibn al-Walid to Ukaydir, the Prophet predicted that they would find him hunting cows, which turned out to be true.
4. The fourth example: after capturing al-Abbas, the Prophet told him about the secret wealth he had entrusted to Umm al-Fadl, a matter known only to al-Abbas himself, leading to al-Abbas's conversion.
5. The fifth example: the Prophet would inform the hypocrites of their secret conversations and plots, so much so that they feared a surah would be revealed exposing their inner thoughts.

The author then concludes that such examples are abundant, and the book cannot cover even a tenth of them. He then makes a general statement: All of the Prophet's future predictions came true without any falsehood or failure, unlike the predictions of soothsayers (kahanah) and astrologers (munajjimun), whose predictions mix truth with falsehood. Moreover, the Prophet's method was completely different: he was pure and engaged in worship, whereas soothsayers seek closeness to devils and evil spirits. The Prophet's knowledge came directly from God through revelation, without any reliance on astrology, stars, astrolabes, or other tools. This ability to know the unseen is a breach of natural custom (naqd al-'adah), just like other miracles such as softening iron or making armor without fire.

Key Terms
إخبار بالغيب
معجزة
نقض العادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Prophet's predictions were just lucky guesses or based on intelligence reports.
Correction: The examples show that the Prophet knew specific details that no human could have known, such as the exact location of a lost camel or a secret financial arrangement made in private.

Checkpoint
What was the significance of the incident of the lost camel?
A) It showed the Prophet's concern for his property
B) It proved that the Prophet had no knowledge of the unseen
C) It demonstrated that God revealed the camel's location to the Prophet
D) It was a test of the hypocrites' faith

Key Takeaway
The five incidents collectively show that the Prophet possessed divinely given knowledge of the unseen, a clear sign of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The hypocrites mocked the Prophet for not knowing where his camel was, yet he later revealed its exact location. Do you ever find yourself quick to doubt or mock what you don't understand about the Prophet's knowledge? What would it look like for you to have more humility in accepting his prophethood?
?
Al-Abbas thought his secret was safe, but the Prophet revealed it. Are you harboring any secrets—thoughts, habits, or sins—that you assume are hidden from Allah? If you truly believed that Allah knows every secret, what would you change today?
?
The Prophet's foreknowledge was limited to what Allah taught him. Do you seek knowledge from Allah through revelation (Qur'an and Sunnah) as the ultimate source of truth, or do you rely more on your own guesses and opinions? Commit to reading one verse or hadith daily for a week to realign your sources of certainty.

Miracles

The Uniqueness of Prophetic Knowledge Against Soothsaying
Contrast between prophetic foreknowledge and soothsaying/astrology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen differs fundamentally from that of soothsayers and astrologers, and why it constitutes a miracle.

Core Idea
Prophetic knowledge is pure and divine; soothsaying is impure and demonic.

After presenting examples, the author contrasts the Prophet's method of obtaining knowledge with that of soothsayers and astrologers. He emphasizes that the Prophet's knowledge came directly from God without any worldly tools, and that his predictions were entirely truthful, unlike the mixed results of soothsayers.

Guided Path
1
Read the contrast passage
Read the second part of the source text where the author compares the Prophet's predictions to those of soothsayers and astrologers. Notice the specific differences mentioned.
The author lists several criteria for comparison.
2
Identify the key differences
The differences include: the Prophet's knowledge was always true, whereas soothsayers mix truth with falsehood; the Prophet was pure and engaged in worship, while soothsayers associate with devils; the Prophet's knowledge came without tools like astrology or astrolabes.
Highlight the phrase 'naqd al-'adah' (breach of custom).
3
Understand the concept of 'breach of custom'
The author concludes that the Prophet's knowledge is a miracle because it breaks the normal laws of knowledge acquisition, similar to miracles like softening iron or making armor without fire.
This connects to the broader category of miracles.

عَنْهَا فَقَالَ الْمُنَافِقُونَ: هَذَا مُحَمَّدٌ يُخْبِرُكُمْ خَبَرَ السَّمَاءِ وَهُوَ لَا يَدْرِي أَيْنَ نَاقَتُهُ، فَصَعِدَ الْمِنْبَرَ وَحَمِدَ اللَّهَ وَأَثْنَى عَلَيْهِ، وَحَكَى قَوْلَهُمْ ثُمَّ لِخَالِدِ بْنِ الْوَلِيدِ حِينَ بَعَثَهُ إِلَى أَكِيدَرِ دُومَةِ الْجَنْدَلِ: "أَمَا إِنَّكُمْ سَتَأْتُونَهُ فَتَجِدُونَهُ يَصِيدُ الْبَقَرَ" فَوَجَدُوهُ كَذَلِكَ. وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لِلْعَبَّاسِ حِينَ أَسَرَهُ: "اِفْدِ نَفْسَكَ وَابْنَيْ أَخِيكَ" يَعْنِي عَقِيلَ بْنَ أَبِي طَالِبٍ وَنَوْفَلَ بْنَ الْحَارِثَةِ- فَإِنَّكَ ذُو مَالٍ فَقَالَ: لَا مَالَ عِنْدِي. قَالَ: فَأَيْنَ الْمَالُ الَّذِي وَضَعْتَهُ بِمَكَّةَ عِنْدَ أُمِّ الْفَضْلِ وَلَيْسَ مَعَكُمَا أَحَدٌ، فَقُلْتَ: إِنْ أَصَبْتُ فِي سَفَرِي فَلِلْفَضْلِ كَذَا، وَلِعَبْدِ اللَّهِ كَذَا، وَلِفُلَانٍ كَذَا؟ فَقَالَ الْعَبَّاسُ: وَالَّذِي بَعَثَكَ بِالْحَقِّ نَبِيًّا مَا عَلِمَ بِهَذَا أَحَدٌ غَيْرِي، وَإِنَّكَ لَرَسُولُ اللَّهِ وَأَسْلَمَ هُوَ وَعَقِيلٌ. وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ مَا كَانَ يُخْبِرُ أَهْلَ النِّفَاقِ بِمَا كَانُوا يَقُولُونَ فِيمَا بَيْنَهُمْ وَيَبِيتُونَ مَا لَا يَرْضَى مِنَ الْقَوْلِ حَتَّى كَانُوا مِنْ شِدَّةِ تَعَنُّتِهِمْ يُحْذَرُونَ أَنْ يَنْزِلَ عَلَيْهِ سُورَةٌ تُنْبِئُهُمْ بِمَا فِي قُلُوبِهِمْ، وَأَمْثَالُ ذَلِكَ كَثِيرٌ، وَكِتَابُنَا هَذَا يَضِيقُ عَنْ ذِكْرِ عُشْرِ ذَلِكَ فَضْلًا عَنْ كُلِّهِ، وَاللَّهُ الْمُوَفِّقُ. ثُمَّ إِنَّ جَمِيعَ مَا أَخْبَرَ مِنَ الْأَخْبَارِ الْكَائِنَةِ فِي الْمُسْتَقْبَلِ خَرَجَ عَلَى مَا أَخْبَرَ مِنْ غَيْرِ تَمَكُّنِ كَذِبٍ أَوْ حَلِفٍ فِي شَيْءٍ مِنْ ذَلِكَ لَا كَمِثْلِ أَخْبَارِ الْكَهَنَةِ وَالْمُنَجِّمِينَ الَّذِينَ يَضِلُّ صِدْقُهُمْ فِي كَذِبِهِمْ وَحَقُّهُمْ فِي بَاطِلِهِمْ عَلَى أَنَّ حَالَتَهُ كَانَتْ تُخَالِفُ حَالَةَ الْكَهَنَةِ فِي طَهَارَتِهِ وَطِيِّبِهِ وَاشْتِغَالِهِ بِالطَّاعَاتِ وَالْعِبَادَاتِ. وَتَقَدُّرِ أُولَئِكَ وَتَنْجِسِهِمْ وَتَقَرُّبِهِمْ إِلَى الشَّيَاطِينِ وَالْأَرْوَاحِ الْخَبِيثَةِ، وَكَذَا كَانَتْ أَخْبَارُهُ صَادِرَةً عَنْهُ عَنْ طَرِيقِ الْغَيْبِ الَّذِي أَعْلَمَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى مِنْ غَيْرِ الِاشْتِغَالِ بِالنَّظَرِ فِي النُّجُومِ وَالتَّأَمُّلِ فِي الطَّالِعِ وَالِارْتِفَاعِ وَتَعَرُّفِ ذَلِكَ مِنْ قِبَلِ الرَّيْحِ وَالْإِسْطِرْلَابِ وَغَيْرِ ذَلِكَ مِمَّا يَفْعَلُهُ الْمُنَجِّمَةُ، فَكَانَ ذَلِكَ مِنْ بَابِ نَقْضِ الْعَادَةِ كَإِلَانَةِ الْحَدِيدِ وَاتِّخَاذِ الدُّرُوعِ بِلَا آلَاتٍ وَلَا اسْتِعْمَالِ النَّارِ.
Among that is the hadith of the Night Journey and what he informed of the news of the Quraysh caravan, and it was as [he said]. And among that is that a she-camel of his, peace be upon him, was lost, so he began asking people about it, so the hypocrites said: 'This Muhammad tells you the news of heaven while he does not know where his she-camel is.' So he ascended the pulpit, praised God and extolled Him, related their statement, then said: 'I do not know except what my Lord has taught me, and He has informed me that it is in such-and-such a valley, its halter entangled in a tree.' So the people hurried and found it thus. And among that is his statement to Khalid ibn al-Walid when he sent him to Ukaydir of Dumah al-Jandal: 'Indeed you will come to him and find him hunting cows.' So they found him thus. And among that is his statement, peace be upon him, to al-Abbas when he captured him: 'Ransom yourself and your brother's two sons'—meaning Aqeel ibn Abi Talib and Nawfal ibn al-Haritha—'for you are a man of wealth.' So he said: 'I have no wealth.' He said: 'Then where is the wealth that you placed in Mecca with Umm al-Fadl, with no one else with you, and you said: If I am killed on my journey, then for al-Fadl such-and-such, for Abdullah such-and-such, and for so-and-so such-and-such?' So al-Abbas said: 'By the One Who sent you with the truth as a prophet, no one but me knew this, and indeed you are the Messenger of God.' And he and Aqeel embraced Islam. And among that is what he used to inform the hypocrites of what they were saying among themselves and plotting at night of speech that is not pleasing, until they, due to the intensity of their obstinacy, feared that a surah would be revealed to him informing them of what was in their hearts. And examples of that are many, and this book of ours is too narrow to mention a tenth of that, let alone all of it, and God is the grantor of success. Then all the news of future events that he informed of turned out as he informed, without any possibility of falsehood or failure in any of that, unlike the news of soothsayers and astrologers, whose truth is lost among their falsehood and their right among their wrong—although his state differed from the state of soothsayers in his purity, goodness, and occupation with acts of obedience and worship, while those ones are unclean, defiled, and seek closeness to devils and evil spirits. And likewise, his reports were issued by him through the unseen which God, exalted, taught him, without engaging in examining the stars, contemplating the ascendant and elevation, or knowing that by means of the wind, astrolabe, or other things that astrologers do. So that was of the category of breaking the norm, like softening iron and making coats of mail without tools or use of fire.

Commentary
This passage is a proof from miracles, specifically the miracle of prophetic foreknowledge (al-ikhbar bi al-ghayb). The author presents multiple historical incidents to demonstrate that the Prophet Muhammad accurately predicted future events without any ordinary means of knowledge, thereby establishing his prophethood. The passage proceeds as follows:

1. The first example is the Night Journey (al-isra'), where the Prophet informed about the Quraysh caravan, and it happened exactly as he said.
2. The second example: the Prophet's camel was lost. Hypocrites mocked him, saying he claims to know news from heaven yet cannot find his camel. The Prophet, after praising God, revealed that the camel was in a specific valley with its halter caught in a tree, and people found it exactly there.
3. The third example: when sending Khalid ibn al-Walid to Ukaydir, the Prophet predicted that they would find him hunting cows, which turned out to be true.
4. The fourth example: after capturing al-Abbas, the Prophet told him about the secret wealth he had entrusted to Umm al-Fadl, a matter known only to al-Abbas himself, leading to al-Abbas's conversion.
5. The fifth example: the Prophet would inform the hypocrites of their secret conversations and plots, so much so that they feared a surah would be revealed exposing their inner thoughts.

The author then concludes that such examples are abundant, and the book cannot cover even a tenth of them. He then makes a general statement: All of the Prophet's future predictions came true without any falsehood or failure, unlike the predictions of soothsayers (kahanah) and astrologers (munajjimun), whose predictions mix truth with falsehood. Moreover, the Prophet's method was completely different: he was pure and engaged in worship, whereas soothsayers seek closeness to devils and evil spirits. The Prophet's knowledge came directly from God through revelation, without any reliance on astrology, stars, astrolabes, or other tools. This ability to know the unseen is a breach of natural custom (naqd al-'adah), just like other miracles such as softening iron or making armor without fire.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen is similar to soothsaying or astrology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Miracles

Posthumous Miracles of the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ)
The author enumerates three posthumous miracles as evidence of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that miracles can occur after a prophet's death and serve as ongoing evidence of his prophethood, illustrated by three historical examples.

Core Idea
Posthumous miracles prove the Prophet's truth even after his death.

The author presents a compelling argument: the Prophet's miracles did not cease with his death. By citing well-known events from Islamic history—the rain prayer through al-Abbas, the fresh bodies of Badr martyrs after fifty years, and the preserved body of Talha—he demonstrates that these breaches of natural custom continue to affirm his prophethood. As you read the passage, note how each example shares the theme of bodily preservation or divine intervention through the Prophet's blessing.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage in Arabic and translation.
Begin by reading the Arabic passage slowly, then the literal translation. Notice the author's style: he introduces examples with 'wa min dhalika' (and among that).
The passage ends mid-sentence, but the three examples are complete.
2
Identify the three posthumous miracles.
List each miracle: 1) Umar's rain prayer through al-Abbas, 2) The fresh bodies of Badr martyrs, 3) The story of Talha's body after 30 years. Notice what makes each a miracle.
3
Reflect on the common element: preservation from decay.
In the second and third examples, the bodies are found fresh and unchanged after decades. The first miracle shows extraordinary response to supplication. Ask: What do these events teach us about the Prophet's ongoing connection to his community?
The author uses these to show that miracles are not limited to the Prophet's lifetime.
4
Consider the significance as evidence of prophethood.
These events are 'mu'jizat' (miracles) because they break natural custom. They serve as proofs for the truth of Muhammad's prophethood, even for later generations who did not witness him alive.
This addresses the misconception that miracles only happen during a prophet's life.

وَأَمَّا مَا ظَهَرَ مِنْ مُعْجِزَاتِهِ وَأَعْلَامِهِ بَعْدَ وَفَاتِهِ فَكَاسْتِسْقَاءِ عُمَرَ فَإِنَّهُ اسْتَسْقَى بِالْعَبَّاسِ فَسُقُوا حَتَّى طَفِقَ النَّاسُ يَمْسَحُونَ أَرْكَانَ الْعَبَّاسِ وَيَقُولُونَ: هَنِيئًا لَكَ سَاقِي الْحَرَمَيْنِ، وَهَذَا مَشْهُورٌ تَفْتَخِرُ بِهِ بَنُو الْعَبَّاسِ. وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ إِخْرَاجُ شُهَدَاءِ بَدْرٍ رَطَابًا بَعْدَ خَمْسِينَ سَنَةً وَهُوَ أَمْرٌ مَشْهُورٌ بِالْمَدِينَةِ، وَكَذَا قِصَّةُ طَلْحَةَ حِينَ رَأَتْهُ ابْنَتُهُ عَائِشَةُ فِي الْمَنَامِ فَقَالَ لَهَا يَا بُنَيَّةُ حَوِّلِينِي مِنْ هَذَا الْمَكَانِ فَقَدْ أَضَرَّنِي النَّدَى، فَأَخْرَجَتْهُ بَعْدَ ثَلَاثِينَ سَنَةً وَحَوَّلَتْهُ وَهُوَ طَرِيٌّ لَمْ يَتَغَيَّرْ، وَتَوَلَّى إِخْرَاجَهُ عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ سَلَامَةَ الْكِنْدِيُّ. وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ أَنَّ أَبَا أَيُّوبَ الْأَنْصَارِيَّ حِينَ مَاتَ بِقُسْطَنْطِينِيَّةَ فَقُبِرَ عِنْدَ سُورِ الْمَدِينَةِ وَبُنِيَ عَلَيْهِ، فَكَانُوا إِذَا أَمْحَلُوا
As for what appeared of his miracles and signs after his death, such as the prayer for rain of Umar, for he sought rain through al-Abbas, and they were given rain until people began to rub the corners of al-Abbas and say: 'Congratulations to you, water-carrier of the two sanctuaries.' And this is well-known, and the Banu Abbas boast of it. And among that is the bringing out of the martyrs of Badr fresh after fifty years, and it is a well-known matter in Medina. And likewise the story of Talha when his daughter Aisha saw him in a dream, and he said to her: 'O my daughter, move me from this place, for the moisture has harmed me.' So she brought him out after thirty years and moved him, and he was moist and unchanged. And his exhumation was undertaken by Abd al-Rahman ibn Salamah al-Kindi. And among that is that Abu Ayyub al-Ansari when he died in Constantinople, he was buried at the wall of the city and a structure was built over him, and whenever they faced drought...
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a classification and listing of miracles that occurred after the Prophet's death (mu'jizat ba'd al-wafat). The author provides three examples:

1. The first example: During the caliphate of Umar, there was a drought. Umar prayed for rain through al-Abbas (the Prophet's uncle), and rain fell abundantly. People even touched al-Abbas's garment as a blessing, calling him 'water-carrier of the two sanctuaries.' This miracle is well-known and the Abbasid family prides itself on it.

2. The second example: The bodies of the martyrs of Badr were exhumed after fifty years and found fresh, as if they had just died. This was a well-known event in Medina.

3. The third example: The story of Talha ibn Ubayd Allah. His daughter Aisha saw him in a dream, asking to be moved from his grave because moisture was harming him. After thirty years, she exhumed him and found his body still moist and unchanged. The exhumation was carried out by Abd al-Rahman ibn Salamah al-Kindi.

The passage then begins a fourth example about Abu Ayyub al-Ansari, but it is cut off. The point is that these events are miracles because they involve the preservation of bodies from decay, which is a breach of natural custom, and they serve as ongoing evidence of the Prophet's prophethood even after his death.

Key Terms
معجزات بعد الوفاة
استسقاء
شهداء بدر
طلحة بن عبيد الله
أبو أيوب الأنصاري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles can only occur during a prophet's lifetime.
Correction: The Prophet's miracles continued after his death, as shown by these events, proving his prophethood remains evident.

Checkpoint
What common feature do the miracles of the Badr martyrs and Talha share?
A) They both involved rain
B) Their bodies were preserved from decay
C) They occurred during the Prophet's life
D) They were witnessed by Umar

Key Takeaway
Posthumous miracles, such as the preservation of bodies and answered supplication, continue to affirm the Prophet's prophethood and the ongoing blessing of his legacy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to witness the fresh body of a companion from 30 years ago, would that remove any lingering doubts you have about the truth of the Prophet? If not, what would?
?
The Banu Abbas boasted of the miracle through al-Abbas. Do you take pride in anything that could distract you from humility before Allah? How can you transform that pride into gratitude?
?
These miracles show that the Prophet's blessings continue after his death. In what specific area of your faith are you most in need of his intercession or blessing? What is one action you will take this week to seek that blessing?

The Prophet's State as a Miraculous Break in Custom
Contrasts the Prophet's state with soothsayers to prove his knowledge is a miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's purity and direct divine knowledge constitute a miracle (muʿjiza) that breaks normal custom (naqḍ al-ʿāda), distinguishing him from soothsayers and astrologers.

Core Idea
The Prophet's entire state—his purity and knowledge—is itself a miracle.

This passage presents a subtle but powerful argument for the Prophet's prophethood. While people often think of miracles as dramatic events, the author here points out that the Prophet's personal character and his knowledge of the unseen, coming without any worldly means, are equally miraculous. Let's see how he contrasts the Prophet with soothsayers and astrologers to prove this point.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author uses two main contrasts.
2
Identify the two contrasts
The passage contrasts the Prophet with soothsayers (purity vs impurity) and with astrologers (direct divine knowledge vs astrological tools). Find the phrases that describe each side.
3
Understand the conclusion
Both contrasts lead to the same conclusion: the Prophet's state breaks custom (naqḍ al-ʿāda). The author compares it to other miracles like softening iron.
4
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: If the Prophet's personal state and knowledge are miraculous, what does that mean for how we view his prophethood?
This helps internalise the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الذين يضل صدقهم في كذبهم وحقهم في باطلهم على أن حالته كانت تخالف حالة الكهنة في طهارته وطيبه واشتغاله بالطاعات والعبادات. وتقدر أولئك وتنجسهم وتقربهم إلى الشياطين والأرواح الخبيثة، وكذا كانت أخباره صادرة عنه عن طريق الغيب الذي أعلمه الله تعالى من غير الاشتغال بالنظر في النجوم والتأمل في الطالع والارتفاع وتعرف ذلك من قبل الريح والإسطرلاب وغير ذلك من خلاف ما يفعله المنجمة، فكان ذلك من باب نقض العادة كإلانة الحديد واتخاذ الدروع بلا آلات ولا استعمال النار.
Those whose truth is lost in their falsehood and their right in their wrong, that his state opposed the state of the soothsayers in his purity, his goodness, and his occupation with acts of obedience and worship. And those [soothsayers] are impure, defiled, and draw near to devils and evil spirits. Likewise, his reports came from him through the unseen which Allah taught him, without occupying himself with looking at the stars, reflecting on ascendants and heights, and knowing that by means of the wind and the astrolabe, and other than that contrary to what the astrologers do. So that was of the category of breaking the custom (naqḍ al-ʿāda), like softening iron and making coats of mail without tools and without using fire.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage presents an argument that the Prophet Muhammad's (peace be upon him) personal state and knowledge constitute a miracle (muʿjiza) that breaks normal custom (naqḍ al-ʿāda). The author begins by contrasting the Prophet with soothsayers (kuhhān): while soothsayers mix truth with falsehood and rely on impure spirits, the Prophet was pure, good, and devoted to worship. His knowledge of future events came directly from Allah without any recourse to astrological practices such as stargazing, reading ascendants, using the wind or astrolabe. This complete independence from earthly means is itself a miracle, comparable to the miraculous softening of iron and crafting of armor without tools or fire, which were among the Prophet's miracles. The argument underscores that the Prophet's entire way of life and mode of knowledge acquisition are supernaturally beyond human custom.

Key Terms
نقض العادة
كهانة
معجزة
إسطرلاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only extraordinary events like splitting the moon count as miracles.
Correction: The author argues that the Prophet's pure state and divine knowledge, even without dramatic events, are also miracles (naqḍ al-ʿāda).

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is the Prophet's state considered a break in custom (naqḍ al-ʿāda)?
A) Because he performed miracles like softening iron.
B) Because his knowledge came from Allah without using astrological or other worldly means.
C) Because he was born without a father.
D) Because he never made a mistake in his predictions.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's personal purity and his direct divine knowledge, without any worldly means, constitute a miracle (naqḍ al-ʿāda) that proves his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet's knowledge came directly from Allah without any worldly means like stars or astrolabes. In your own pursuit of knowledge—whether religious or worldly—how much do you rely on tools and human sources versus turning directly to Allah? What is one practical change you can make today to seek knowledge with greater reliance on Him?
?
Soothsayers mix truth with falsehood, but the Prophet's entire state was pure truth. Where in your life do you find yourself mixing truth with falsehood—perhaps in your intentions, words, or actions? What is one specific area where you can commit to complete honesty and purity, following the Prophet's example?
?
The author argues that the Prophet's purity itself was a miracle. If someone observed your daily state—your habits, priorities, and concerns—would they see a break from the worldly norm that points to something divine? What is the one habit or attachment you need to abandon so that your life becomes a sign of Allah?

Posthumous Miracles as Proof of Prophethood
Enumerates posthumous miracles of the Prophet and connects them to his prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that miracles continued after the Prophet's death as ongoing evidence of his prophethood, and that every saint's wonder (karama) is inherently linked to the Prophet's miracle.

Core Idea
The Prophet's miracles endure beyond his lifetime through the saints.

The author presents four remarkable events that occurred after the Prophet's death, each serving as a sign of his prophethood. These stories demonstrate that the Prophet's baraka continues to manifest in extraordinary ways, confirming the truth of his mission long after his departure from this world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Let the examples and their details sink in.
Notice the variety of miracles: rain, preservation of bodies, and drought relief.
2
Identify the four examples
List each posthumous miracle mentioned. Pay attention to the people involved and the time elapsed.
The first is about 'Umar and al-'Abbas; the second about the martyrs of Badr; the third about Talha; the fourth about Abu Ayyub.
3
Understand the concluding principle
Read the final sentence carefully. Understand how the author connects saints' karamas to the Prophet's miracle.
This is a key theological point in Maturidi thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما ظهر من معجزاته وأعلامه بعد وفاته فكاستسقاء عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه فإنه استسقى بالعباس رضي الله عنه فسقوا حتى طفق الناس يمسحون أركان العباس ويقولون: هنيئًا لك ساقي الحرمين، وهذا مشهور تفتخر به بنو العباس. ومن ذلك إخراج شهداء بدر رطابا بعد خمسين سنة وهو أمر مشهور بالمدينة، وكذا قصة طلحة حين رأته ابنته عائشة في المنام فقال لها يا بنية حوليني من هذا المكان فقد أضرني الندى، فأخرجته بعد ثلاثين سنة وحولته وهو طري لم يتغير، وتولى إخراجه عبد الرحمن بن سلامة الكندي. ومن ذلك أن أبا أيوب الأنصاري رضي الله عنه حين مات بقسطنطينية فقبر عند سور المدينة وبنى عليه، فكانوا إذا أمحلوا كشفوا عن قبره فمطروا، وكل كرامة ظهرت لولي ففيها معجزة النبي عليه السلام على ما نبين إن شاء الله.
As for what appeared of his miracles and signs after his death: such as the prayer for rain (istisqa') of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him—he prayed for rain through al-'Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, and they were given rain until the people began wiping the corners of al-'Abbas and saying, 'Congratulations to you, waterer of the two sanctuaries.' This is famous, and the Banu 'Abbas boast of it. And among that is the bringing out of the martyrs of Badr fresh after fifty years—a well-known matter in Medina. And likewise the story of Talha when his daughter 'A'isha saw him in a dream: he said to her, 'O my daughter, move me from this place, for the moisture has harmed me.' So she brought him out after thirty years and moved him, and he was fresh, unchanged. 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Salama al-Kindi undertook his exhumation. And among that is that Abu Ayyub al-Ansari, may Allah be pleased with him, when he died in Constantinople, was buried at the city wall and a structure was built over him. Whenever they suffered drought, they would uncover his grave and they would be given rain. And every miracle (karama) that appears from a saint (wali) thereby constitutes a miracle of the Prophet, peace be upon him, as we will explain—God willing.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage lists specific miracles (muʿjizat) and signs that appeared after the death of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), serving as ongoing evidence of his prophethood. The author gives four examples: (1) The istisqa' (rain prayer) of Caliph 'Umar ibn al-Khattab through al-'Abbas, the Prophet's uncle, resulting in immediate rain—this became a source of pride for the Abbasids. (2) The bodies of the martyrs of Badr were exhumed after fifty years and found fresh, as if newly buried—a well-known tradition in Medina. (3) The story of the companion Talha ibn 'Ubayd Allah: his daughter 'A'isha (not the Prophet's wife, but another) saw him in a dream complaining of moisture; when exhumed after thirty years, his body was still fresh and unchanged. The exhumation was performed by 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Salama al-Kindi. (4) The companion Abu Ayyub al-Ansari died in Constantinople (Istanbul); his grave near the city wall became a source of rain during drought. The author concludes by stating that every saintly wonder (karama) that appears from a righteous saint (wali) is, in fact, a miracle of the Prophet, because it stems from his baraka (blessing). This connection between the Prophet and later saints' wonders reinforces the authenticity of his mission.

Key Terms
معجزة
كرامة
استسقاء
ولي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles only happened during the Prophet's life.
Correction: Posthumous miracles also occur and are proofs of his prophethood.

Checkpoint
What is the relationship between a saint's karama and the Prophet's miracle, according to the author?
A) A saint's karama is independent and has no connection to the Prophet.
B) Every saint's karama is actually a miracle of the Prophet.
C) Only some saints' karamas are considered miracles of the Prophet.
D) Karamas are greater than the Prophet's miracles.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's miracles continue after his death through the wonders of saints, proving that his prophethood remains alive.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a difficulty, do you turn to the Prophet's intercession or rely only on your own means? This lesson shows that his blessings continue through saints—how can you consciously seek his baraka in your daily life starting today?

The bodies of the martyrs were preserved for decades as a sign of the Prophet's truth. What does this tell you about the real value of this world versus the hereafter? Are you living in a way that reflects that your body is temporary but your soul's state is eternal?
?
Saintly wonders are ultimately miracles of the Prophet. Do you see the righteous people around you as living signs of his prophethood? Have you truly honored them as such, or do you take their baraka for granted? Commit to one action that shows you recognize their connection to the Prophet.

The Comprehensive Virtues of Mecca
Lists the virtues of Mecca and its status as the first House.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various attributes that make Mecca a uniquely honored place in Islam, from its historical legacy to its status as the first House of worship.

Core Idea
Mecca's honor is rooted in its prophetic legacy and its role as the sanctuary of Allah.

The author begins by enumerating the many facets of Mecca's excellence, connecting it to the Prophets Ibrahim and Isma'il, and highlighting its central role for all nations. This passage establishes the foundation for understanding why Mecca is spiritually significant.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Mecca's virtues
Read the Arabic and translation carefully, noticing the list of attributes.
The author uses a series of descriptive phrases.
2
Identify the key elements
List the attributes mentioned: legacy of Ibrahim, origin of Isma'il, station of nations, pride of Arabs, navel of peninsula, honor of soil, resort of tribes, qibla, season of pilgrimage, security, refuge, sanctuary of Allah, mother of villages, first House.
These highlight both historical and spiritual significance.
3
Reflect on the status of the first House
Consider the significance of the Ka'ba being the first House established for mankind and how it demands humility from all, even tyrants.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما هو راجع إلى مكانه فقد كانت بلدته مأثره إبراهيم، ومنشأ إسماعيل ومنسك الأمم ومفخر العرب، وسرة جزيرتها، وشرف تربتها، ومثابة قبائلها، وقبلة جماعتها، وموسم إفتائها، ومأمن خائفها، وملاذ هاربها، وحرم الله في أرضه، وأم قرى عباده، وأول بيت وضع للناس يتجه إليها أهل البسطة في القوة لإظهار الخضوع والعبودية، وتخضع فيها أعناق الجبابرة لملابسة مر الطاعة، وقد عرفت عند الأجيال كلها بالآيات البينة والعلامات الظاهرة والعبر المتتابعة كالوحش الذي يأمن فيه حتى يجتمع مع السباع والكلاب ويذعر منها إذا خرجت منه، وكالطير التي تسقط على سطوح المسجد وزمزم والسقاية ولا تقرب سطح البيت، وكمقام إبراهيم عليه السلام في الحجر، ولو لم يكن لمكة آية إلا أمر الفيل وإتيان طير من البحر بحجارة من سجيل تحملها بأرجلها ومناقيرها حتى تهلك أمة من الأمم لكانت آية كافية في تعظيم شأنها وجلالة قدرها وكرامة أهلها عند الله تعالى، ثم مما لا يرتاب ذلك لم يكن ممن كان بها يومئذ من الناس لأجل أنفسهم إذ هم كانوا مشركين يعبدون ما ينحتون وجعلوا لله شركاء الجن وخلقهم وخرقوا له بنين وبنات بغير علم سبحانه وتعالى عما يصفون، وبعضهم كانوا قائلين بقدم الدهر ويضيفون الحوادث إليه وكانوا يقولون: وما يهلكنا إلا الدهر.
As for what pertains to his place: his town was the legacy of Ibrahim, the origin of Isma'il, the ritual station of nations, the pride of the Arabs, the navel of its peninsula, the honor of its soil, the resort of its tribes, the qibla of its community, the season of its pilgrimage, the security of its fearful, the refuge of its fugitive, the sanctuary of Allah in His earth, the mother of villages for His servants, the first House established for mankind. Those with physical strength turn to her to show humility and servitude, and the necks of tyrants are subdued in her by wearing the garment of obedience. She has been known among all generations by manifest signs, apparent markers, and consecutive lessons: like the wild animals that feel safe in it, so that they gather with predators and dogs, and become frightened when they leave it; and like the birds that alight on the roofs of the mosque, Zamzam, and the water dispensary, and do not approach the roof of the House; and like the Station of Ibrahim, peace be upon him, in the stone. Even if Mecca had no sign except the affair of the Elephant and the coming of birds from the sea with stones of baked clay (sijjil), carrying them with their legs and beaks until they destroyed a whole nation, it would be a sufficient sign for the greatness of its status, the majesty of its worth, and the honor of its people with Allah Almighty. Then, what is not doubted is that it was not for the sake of the people who were there at that time themselves, for they were polytheists worshipping what they carved, and they made for Allah partners—the jinn—while He created them, and they falsely attributed to Him sons and daughters without knowledge. Glory be to Him and High above what they describe! And some of them were saying the world is eternal, attributing events to it, and they would say: 'Nothing destroys us but time.'
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive description of the virtues and miraculous signs of Mecca, the birthplace of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). The author begins by listing the city's religious and historical merits: it is the legacy of the Prophet Ibrahim (Abraham), the origin of Isma'il (Ishmael), a place of pilgrimage for nations, the pride of the Arabs, the qibla (direction of prayer) for the community, and the first house of worship on earth (the Ka'ba). The city serves as a sanctuary (ḥaram) where even tyrants show humility. The author then enumerates specific ongoing signs (āyāt) and wonders: (1) wild animals are tame within the Haram, coexisting peacefully with predators and dogs, but become wild once outside. (2) Birds land on the roofs of the mosque, the well of Zamzam, and the water dispensary, but avoid the roof of the Ka'ba itself. (3) The Station of Ibrahim (Maqam Ibrahim) contains the footprint of the prophet. (4) The most famous historical sign is the Year of the Elephant (عام الفيل), when the Abyssinian army under Abraha was destroyed by birds carrying stones of baked clay (sijjil). The author argues that even if this were the only sign, it would suffice to prove Mecca's greatness. Finally, he notes that the Meccans themselves were not saved because of their own merits—they were polytheists who associated partners with Allah, denied resurrection, and attributed events to the eternal cycle of time (dahr). This contrast highlights that the signs are from Allah, not due to the people's righteousness.

Key Terms
مكة
حرم
إبراهيم
إسماعيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The first mosque built by angels
B) The first House established for mankind
C) The first city in history
D) The first sanctuary for animals

Key Takeaway
Mecca's unparalleled status comes from its prophetic heritage and its role as the first sanctuary for worship, commanding universal respect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage says tyrants' necks are subdued in Mecca by wearing the garment of obedience. Is there an area of your life where you are acting like a tyrant, refusing to humble yourself before Allah? What would it take for you to 'wear the garment of obedience' today?
?
Mecca is described as 'the security of its fearful, the refuge of its fugitive.' What fear or shame are you running from instead of seeking refuge in Allah's sanctuary? Will you turn to Him right now?

The Perpetual Miracles of Mecca's Sanctuary
Enumerates three miraculous signs in Mecca involving animals and the Station of Ibrahim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three ongoing miraculous signs in Mecca that demonstrate its sanctity: the behavior of wild animals, the birds avoiding the Ka'ba roof, and the Station of Ibrahim.

Core Idea
Mecca is distinguished by continuous miracles that prove its divine sanctity.

After establishing the historical and religious virtues of Mecca, the author now describes specific observable signs that continue to occur in the sanctuary. These signs are not mere legends but are witnessed by successive generations, affirming Mecca's unique status.

As for what pertains to his place: his town was the legacy of Ibrahim, the origin of Isma'il, the ritual station of nations, the pride of the Arabs, the navel of its peninsula, the honor of its soil, the resort of its tribes, the qibla of its community, the season of its pilgrimage, the security of its fearful, the refuge of its fugitive, the sanctuary of Allah in His earth, the mother of villages for His servants, the first House established for mankind. Those with physical strength turn to her to show humility and servitude, and the necks of tyrants are subdued in her by wearing the garment of obedience. She has been known among all generations by manifest signs, apparent markers, and consecutive lessons: like the wild animals that feel safe in it, so that they gather with predators and dogs, and become frightened when they leave it; and like the birds that alight on the roofs of the mosque, Zamzam, and the water dispensary, and do not approach the roof of the House; and like the Station of Ibrahim, peace be upon him, in the stone. Even if Mecca had no sign except the affair of the Elephant and the coming of birds from the sea with stones of baked clay (sijjil), carrying them with their legs and beaks until they destroyed a whole nation, it would be a sufficient sign for the greatness of its status, the majesty of its worth, and the honor of its people with Allah Almighty. Then, what is not doubted is that it was not for the sake of the people who were there at that time themselves, for they were polytheists worshipping what they carved, and they made for Allah partners—the jinn—while He created them, and they falsely attributed to Him sons and daughters without knowledge. Glory be to Him and High above what they describe! And some of them were saying the world is eternal, attributing events to it, and they would say: 'Nothing destroys us but time.'
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive description of the virtues and miraculous signs of Mecca, the birthplace of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). The author begins by listing the city's religious and historical merits: it is the legacy of the Prophet Ibrahim (Abraham), the origin of Isma'il (Ishmael), a place of pilgrimage for nations, the pride of the Arabs, the qibla (direction of prayer) for the community, and the first house of worship on earth (the Ka'ba). The city serves as a sanctuary (ḥaram) where even tyrants show humility. The author then enumerates specific ongoing signs (āyāt) and wonders: (1) wild animals are tame within the Haram, coexisting peacefully with predators and dogs, but become wild once outside. (2) Birds land on the roofs of the mosque, the well of Zamzam, and the water dispensary, but avoid the roof of the Ka'ba itself. (3) The Station of Ibrahim (Maqam Ibrahim) contains the footprint of the prophet. (4) The most famous historical sign is the Year of the Elephant (عام الفيل), when the Abyssinian army under Abraha was destroyed by birds carrying stones of baked clay (sijjil). The author argues that even if this were the only sign, it would suffice to prove Mecca's greatness. Finally, he notes that the Meccans themselves were not saved because of their own merits—they were polytheists who associated partners with Allah, denied resurrection, and attributed events to the eternal cycle of time (dahr). This contrast highlights that the signs are from Allah, not due to the people's righteousness.

Key Terms
آية
الوحش
الطير
مقام إبراهيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to wild animals inside the Haram according to the passage?
A) They become aggressive
B) They become tame and gather with predators
C) They disappear
D) They attack birds

Key Takeaway
The sanctuary of Mecca exhibits continuous supernatural signs that demonstrate its divine sanctity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The wild animals feel safe only within the bounds of the Haram. When you enter a masjid or engage in worship, does your soul find that same sense of peace, or do you carry your anxieties inside? What can you do to truly leave the world behind when you stand before Allah?
?
Birds instinctively avoid landing on the roof of the Ka'ba. Is there any part of your life where you show that level of reverence for what is sacred—or do you treat Allah's commands casually? Commit today to one specific act of reverence that you will practice consistently.
?
The Station of Ibrahim remains as a physical reminder of his devotion. What physical or visible reminders of faith have you placed in your home or daily life? If someone visited your space, would they see signs of your submission to Allah? Pledge to create one tangible sign of your faith this week.

Describes the miracle of the Elephant and contrasts it with the polytheism of the Meccans.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the miracle of the Elephant (Year of the Elephant) serves as a powerful sign of Mecca's sanctity, and how the Meccans' polytheism contrasts with Allah's favor.

Core Idea
The destruction of Abraha's army by birds is a sufficient miracle to prove Mecca's honor, despite the polytheism of its inhabitants.

The author now cites the most famous miracle associated with Mecca: the destruction of the Abyssinian army in the Year of the Elephant. He argues that even if this were the only sign, it would be enough. He then notes that these signs are not due to the righteousness of the Meccans, who were polytheists.

The Karāmāt of Saints and the Prophet's Miracle
Nasafi states the dependence of karamāt on the Prophet's mu'jizah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how every saintly miracle (karāmah) is intrinsically linked to the miracle (mu‘jizah) of the Prophet, and why this connection is fundamental in Ahl al-Sunnah theology.

Core Idea
Every saintly miracle is a reflection of the Prophet's miracle.

In this brief but profound statement, Imam al-Nasafi establishes a fundamental principle: the miracles of saints are not independent. They derive their reality from the miracle of the Prophet, underscoring the centrality of prophethood in all spiritual phenomena.

Guided Path
1
Read the statement
Read the Arabic sentence once. Then read the translation. Notice how Nasafi makes a direct claim: every karamah 'contains' the Prophet's miracle.
The word 'فيها' (contains) is key.
2
Identify the doctrinal point
Reflect on the implication: if every karamah depends on the Prophet's miracle, then prophethood is the source of all miraculous events in this community.
This guards against the misconception that saints have independent miraculous powers.
3
Connect to the lesson's core idea
Summarize in your own words: the karamah is a sign of the saint's closeness to Allah, but its reality is the Prophet's miracle manifesting through the saint.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل كرامة ظهرت لولي ففيها معجزة النبي عليه السلام على ما نبين - إن شاء الله. وأما ما هو راجع إلى مكانه فقد كانت بلدته مأثره إبراهيم، ومنشأ إسماعيل ومنسك الأمم ومفخر العرب، وسرة جزيرتها، وشرف تربتها، ومثابة قبائلها، وقبلة جماعتها، وموسم إفتائها، ومأمن خائفها، وملاذ هاربها، وحرم الله في أرضه، وأم قرى عباده، وأول بيت وضع للناس يتجه إليها أهل البسطة في القوة لإظهار الخضوع والعبودية، وتخضع فيها أعناق الجبابرة لملابسة مر الطاعة، وقد عرفت عند الأجيال كلها بالآيات البينة والعلامات الظاهرة والعبر المتتابعة كالوحش الذي يأمن فيه حتى يجتمع مع السباع والكلاب ويذعر منها إذا خرجت منه، وكالطير التي تسقط على سطوح المسجد وزمزم والسقاية ولا تقرب سطح البيت، وكمقام إبراهيم عليه السلام في الحجر، ولو لم يكن لمكة آية إلا أمر الفيل وإتيان طير من البحر بحجارة من سجيل تحملها بأرجلها ومناقيرها حتى تهلك أمة من الأمم لكانت آية كافية في تعظيم شأنها وجلالة قدرها وكرامة أهلها عند الله تعالى
And every miracle (karāmah) that appears from a saint (walī) contains a miracle (mu‘jizah) of the Prophet, peace be upon him, as we will explain – if Allah wills. As for what pertains to his place, his town was the birthplace of Ibrahim, the origin of Isma‘il, the place of pilgrimage for nations, the pride of the Arabs, the navel of its peninsula, the honor of its soil, the refuge of its tribes, the qiblah of its community, the season of its fatwas, the security of its fearful, the sanctuary of its fugitive, the sacred precinct of Allah on His earth, the mother of towns for His servants, the first house established for mankind; the people of strength turn towards it to manifest humility and servitude, and in it the necks of tyrants bow for the taste of obedience. It has been known throughout generations by clear signs, evident marks, and successive lessons, such as the wild beast that feels safe there so that it gathers with predators and dogs but flees from them when it leaves it, and the birds that land on the roofs of the mosque, Zamzam, and the water trough but do not approach the surface of the house, and the station (maqām) of Ibrahim, peace be upon him, in the stone. And were there no sign for Makkah except the matter of the elephant and the coming of birds from the sea with stones of baked clay (sijjīl) carrying them with their feet and beaks until they destroyed a nation of nations, that would be a sufficient sign to magnify its importance, the majesty of its rank, and the honor of its people in the sight of Allah the Exalted.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a combined statement and description. Nasafi first links the karamāt of awliyā’ to the mu‘jizah of the Prophet, indicating that every saintly miracle is actually a manifestation of the Prophet’s miracle, though he promises to explain this later. He then turns to the virtues of Makkah (the Prophet’s birthplace). He enumerates its honors: it is the place of Ibrahim’s legacy and Isma‘il’s origin, the spiritual focus of nations, the pride of Arabs, and the center of the peninsula. It is a place of refuge, safety, and worship. Nasafi then provides examples of miraculous signs that have been witnessed in Makkah: wild animals become tame, birds avoid the Ka‘bah roof, and the station of Ibrahim remains in the stone. He emphasizes that even the incident of the elephant (the year of the elephant) alone, where birds destroyed the invading army with clay stones, is sufficient to prove Makkah’s exalted status and the honor of its people before Allah.

Key Terms
كرامة
معجزة
ولي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the miracles of saints (karāmāt) are independent extraordinary acts, separate from the Prophet's miracle.
Correction: Nasafi explicitly states that every karamah contains the Prophet's miracle; they are derivative, not independent.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the relationship between a saint's miracle (karāmah) and the Prophet's miracle (mu‘jizah)?
A) They are independent
B) The saint's miracle is greater
C) The saint's miracle contains the Prophet's miracle
D) They are unrelated

Key Takeaway
Every saintly miracle is a manifestation of the Prophet's miracle, affirming the centrality of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every good deed or divine favor you experience is ultimately a reflection of the Prophet's mercy, how does this change how you view the blessings in your life? Will you consciously trace them back to the Messenger today?
?
Do you ever seek spiritual experiences that you think are your own achievements, forgetting they are only possible through the Prophet's light? What will you do to keep this connection alive?
?
The Prophet's miracle is the source of every saintly miracle. How does this truth make you more grateful to the Prophet, and what act of gratitude will you perform today?

The Exalted Virtues and Miraculous Signs of Makkah
Nasafi enumerates the virtues and miraculous signs of Makkah.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Makkah is distinguished by countless signs, from its sacred history to ongoing miracles.

After establishing the nature of saintly miracles, Nasafi turns to the virtues of Makkah, the Prophet's birthplace. He lists a series of honors and then provides specific miraculous events that confirm its sanctity, culminating in the famous Year of the Elephant.

intermediate

The Tawatur of the Elephant Incident and Pre-Islamic Poetry as Evidence
Nasafi argues for the tawatur of the elephant story and cites pre-Islamic poetry as proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses the concept of tawatur (mass transmission) and pre-Islamic poetry to establish the historicity of the elephant incident as a miraculous prelude to the prophethood of Muhammad.

Core Idea
The elephant story is historical fact, proven by mass transmission and independent poetic witness.

Nasafi anticipates doubt about the elephant incident and provides two powerful proofs: the principle of tawatur, which makes denial impossible without stubbornness, and the independent testimony of pre-Islamic Arab poets who referenced the event long before Islam. This lesson unpacks both arguments and shows how they reinforce the miraculous nature of the event as an irhas (prelude) for the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how Nasafi first explains the theological significance of the event (irhas) before addressing its historicity.
The poetry lines are fragmentary; focus on the overall argument.
2
Understand the irhas context
Nasafi clarifies that the Abyssinians were not destroyed because they were wrong, but as a prelude for Muhammad. This sets the stage for why the event is important.
3
Identify the tawatur claim
Find where Nasafi states that denial of the elephant incident is impossible because it is established by tawatur. Note what tawatur means: a transmission so widespread that collusion on a lie is inconceivable.
Tawatur is a key methodological concept in kalam.
4
Examine the poetic evidence
Read the two poem excerpts from Nufayl and Tufayl. Both were pre-Islamic poets. Identify how their lines reference the event (birds, stones, the elephant). Ask: why does Nasafi cite them?
These poems show that even before Islam, the event was known and remembered.
5
Reflect on the overall proof
Consider how the combination of tawatur (transmission continuity) and independent pre-Islamic testimony (early external witness) makes the elephant incident historically certain. This is a model for proving other prophetic miracles.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قصدهم من الحبشان كانوا من أهل الكتاب مؤمنين بموسى وعيسى عليهما السلام متمسكين بكتابيهما التوراة والإنجيل، فلا يظن إهلاكهم لنصرة من كانت حالته تلك بل كان ذلك إرهاصا لأمر نبيه المصطفى محمد عليه السلام إذ كان قرب زمانه ودنا أوان خروجه وظهور دعوته، فصان الله تعالى الآباء لاحترام من علم الله تعالى خروجه من أصلابهم من أنصار دعوة رسول الله عليه السلام وأتباع ملته، ومتبعي دينه وشريعته، وحفظ نبيه الذي كان في سابق علمه قضائه أن يكون قبلة لأمته ومنسكا ومثابة لأهل ملته، ثم إن إنكار أمر الفيل ومبرم غير ممكن لأهل الإلحاد لثبوت ذلك بالتواتر الذي لا يتمكن فيه توهم الكذب كثبوت سائر الأمور الماضية في الأزمنة الخالية التي ينسب جاحدها إلى العناد والمكابرة، وقد ذكر ذلك الشعراء في قصائدهم والخطباء في مواعظهم. فمن ذلك قول نفيل بن حبيب وهو جاهلي، وكانت الحبشة أخذته في طريقها إلى مكة ليدلها فاحتال الهرب منها : ألا ردى ركائبنـ ا ردينـ فإنك لو ترى ولن تراه حمدت الله إذا عاينت طيرنـ نعمناكم على الهجران عينا لدى جنب المخصب ما رأينا وحسب حجارة تلقـ علين وكلهم يسائل عن نفيل كأن عليَّ للحبشان دينـ وقال طفيل وهو جاهلي: ترعى مذانب وسمى أطماع لهـ بالجذع حيث عصى عصى أصحابه الفيل
And among those who attacked them from the Abyssinians were People of the Book, believers in Moses and Jesus, peace be upon them, holding fast to their books, the Torah and the Gospel. So do not think that they were destroyed for the help of one whose state was that; rather that was a prelude (irhās) to the affair of His chosen Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, when his time was near and the moment of his emergence and the appearance of his call had drawn near. Thus Allah the Exalted protected the fathers (i.e., ancestors) for the respect of one whose emergence from their loins Allah knew would be among the supporters of the call of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and the followers of his community, and the adherents of his religion and law. And He preserved His Prophet, whose decree in His prior knowledge was that he would be a qiblah for his community and a place of pilgrimage and a refuge for the people of his religion. Then, indeed, denial of the matter of the elephant and its calamity is not possible for the people of atheism (ilḥād) because it is established by tawātur (mass transmission) in which suspicion of falsehood is not possible, like the establishment of other past affairs in bygone times whose denier is attributed to stubbornness and obstinacy. And poets have mentioned it in their poems and preachers in their sermons. Among that is the saying of Nufayl ibn Habīb, who was a pre-Islamic (Jāhilī) poet, and the Abyssinians had taken him on their way to Makkah to guide them, so he contrived to escape from them: 'Oh, let my mounts return ... indeed, if you see, and you will not see, you will thank Allah when you see birds ... we have favored you over separation ... at the side of the fertile valley we have not seen ... and enough stones thrown upon us ... and all of them ask about Nufayl, as if I owe a debt to the Abyssinians.' And Ṭufayl, also a Jāhilī, said: 'They graze in rain-fed valleys, and his aspirations have swollen, and on the palm trunk where he disobeyed, the companions of the elephant disobeyed.'
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is an argument and evidence. Nasafi first explains that the Abyssinian attackers included Christians, so their destruction was not to defend them but as an Ẓ. (irhās) paving the way for Prophet Muhammad. He then asserts that the story of the elephant is established by tawātur (mass transmission), making its denial impossible without stubbornness. He then provides two pre-Islamic poems (from Nufayl ibn Habīb and Ṭufayl) that reference the event, showing that even before Islam, the story was known and used as evidence. The poetry fragments mention the birds and stones, confirming the supernatural nature of the event.

إرهاص
شعر
جاهلي
