Key Takeaway
The elephant incident is historically verified through mass transmission (tawatur) and corroborated by pre-Islamic poetry, making its denial a sign of obstinacy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How does the fact that even pre-Islamic poets testified to the elephant incident affect the level of certainty you should have in the truth of Islam? Where else in your faith might you be accepting things without this kind of verification, and what would change if you demanded the same standard?
?
If denial of the elephant incident is considered 'obstinacy' (mukabara), could there be any truths—whether about yourself, your relationship with Allah, or your purpose—that you are stubbornly avoiding? What would it take for you to submit to them today?
?
Allah carefully prepared the way for Prophet Muhammad by protecting ancestors and sending advanced signs. Do you trust that Allah is also preparing you for something greater, even in circumstances you don't understand? What step can you take right now to align yourself with His planning instead of resisting it?

The Perpetual Miracle of the Quran
Contrasts the perpetual Quranic miracle with time-bound other miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quran's inimitability is a perpetual miracle that differs from other signs.

Core Idea
The Quran's miracle is timeless and universal, unlike all other miracles.

The author begins by affirming that the Quran's inimitability is not a temporary phenomenon. Unlike other miracles that are limited to specific times and places, the Quran remains a living miracle until the Day of Resurrection. In this passage, he contrasts the Quran with other signs that require transmission, explaining why the Quran is a perpetual proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement
The author states 'The inimitability of the Quran remains forever.' Notice the strong assertion that the miracle is not temporary.
This sets the tone for the entire lesson.
2
Contrast with other miracles
The author explains that other miracles are bound to specific places and times, and later generations rely on reports. The Quran, however, is a sensory and rational sign spread across the earth.
Consider how this makes the Quran uniquely accessible.
3
Reflect on the implications
Think about why a perpetual miracle is necessary for a universal message. The Quran's continuous availability strengthens its proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إعجاز القرآن باق للأبد. وأما ما هو راجع إلى كتابه فهو من أعجب الآيات وأظهر الأعلام والدلالات إذ هو آية حسية عقلية باقية على الدهر مبثوثة فى الآفاق، وغيره من الآيات يختص بمكان ويوجد في زمان ثم يصير غير من شاهدها محجوجا ببلوغ الخبر على ألسنة من شاهدها وعاينها، والقرآن باق إلى يوم القيامة منتشر في أطراف الأرض ثم فيه وجوه من الدلالات. أحدها نظمه العجيب الذي باين ما سواه من الكلام فإنه في الجملة ينقسم إلى منثور ومنظوم، والقرآن ليس من جملة الكلام المنثور، ثم المنظوم من الكلام كان عند العرب منقسماً إلى أقسام أربعة نظم الشعر، ونظم الرجز، ونظم الخطبة، ونظم الرسالة، والقرآن باين كل وجوه النظم وليس في طباع البشر أن يجيء واحد فيأتي بنظم ينفرد به عن الأمم كافة، ثم هو بهذا النظم تحدى جميع البشر وغيرهم بالقصور عند وقوعهم بالعجز دونه، وبدأ في مدح ما أتى به وأعاد وبالغ تقريظه وزاد وإن تناسوه لم يتركهم، وإن تغافلوا عنه لم يعرض عنهم حتى هيجهم ليكون ذلك أبلغ في تبكيتهم وأغيظ الدهمائهم، وأدعى إلى الاعتزاز لمغالبته والابتدار لمباراته، وكان هذا دأبه معهم منذ مبعثه إلى مخترمه وذلك ثلاث
The inimitability of the Quran remains forever. As for what pertains to His Book, it is among the most amazing signs and the clearest marks and proofs, for it is a sensory and rational sign remaining perpetually, dispersed throughout the horizons. Other signs are specific to a place and exist in a time, then the one who did not witness them becomes obligated by the transmission of the report from the tongues of those who witnessed and saw them. The Quran remains until the Day of Resurrection, spread in the regions of the earth. Then in it are aspects of proofs. One of them is its wondrous composition which is distinct from all other speech. For it, in general, is divided into prose and poetry, and the Quran is not part of prose speech. Then poetry among the Arabs was divided into four types: the arrangement of poetry, the arrangement of rajaz, the arrangement of the sermon, and the arrangement of the epistle. The Quran is distinct from every type of arrangement, and it is not in the nature of humans that one should come and produce a composition that he alone distinguishes from all nations. Then, with this composition, he challenged all humans and others, with inability, when they fell short of it. And he began to praise what he brought and repeated and exaggerated its commendation and increased. And if they ignored it, he did not leave them, and if they were heedless of it, he did not turn away from them until he provoked them so that it would be more effective in silencing them and more angering for their commoners, and more conducive to pride for overcoming his challenge and rushing to compete with him. This was his practice with them from his mission until his death, and that is three...
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage defines the miracle of the Quran. It begins by stating that the Quran's inimitability is perpetual. Unlike other miracles that are limited to specific times and places, the Quran is both a sensory and rational miracle, spread across the world forever. The author then explains the specific aspect of this miracle: its unique composition. All speech is either prose or poetry. The Quran is neither. Arabic poetry has four types: regular poetry, rajaz (metered verse), sermons, and epistles. The Quran is distinct from all these. It is beyond human capacity to produce such a unique arrangement. The Prophet challenged all of humanity and they proved unable. He persistently urged them to compete, which made their defeat more decisive. The passage ends abruptly with 'and that is three...' likely referring to three periods or decades of his mission.

Key Terms
إعجاز
آية حسية عقلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran's inimitability is only about eloquence.
Correction: The author states it is both a sensory sign (heard) and a rational sign (intellectually compelling).

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Quran described as?
A) A sign only for a specific time and place
B) A sensory and rational sign remaining perpetually
C) A sign that disappears after the Prophet's death
D) A sign that only the Prophet's companions could witness

Key Takeaway
The Quran's inimitability is a perpetual sign that is both heard and intellectually compelling, unlike time-bound miracles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have the Quran in your hands, a perpetual miracle. Yet do you treat it as a living proof or just a script? When was the last time you were intellectually compelled by its message? What one change can you make today to engage with it as the rational sign it is?
?
Other believers rely on reports of past miracles. You have no excuse—the Quran is before you. Are you still indifferent? What would it take for you to truly feel its challenge (tahaddi) and respond with conviction?
?
The Quran remains until the Day of Resurrection, spread across the earth. Is it spread across your life? If not, what are you prioritizing over it? Write down one specific step to make the Quran central to your daily decisions.

The Unique Composition and the Challenge
Enumerates the types of Arabic speech and explains the Quran's distinct composition and the challenge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific inimitability of the Quran's composition and how the Prophet persistently challenged the Arabs.

Core Idea
The Quran's composition defies all categories of Arabic speech.

In this passage, the author turns to the specific aspect of the Quran's miracle: its wondrous composition. He explains that all human speech falls into prose or poetry, and poetry into four types. The Quran is distinct from all. He then describes how the Prophet challenged humanity and persistently urged them to produce something similar, making their inability a decisive proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the enumeration
The author lists five categories of speech: prose, and four types of poetry (regular, rajaz, sermon, epistle). Notice he says the Quran is not prose and not any of the poetic types.
This is a key element of the miracle.
2
Understand the challenge
The Prophet challenged all humans with this unique composition, and they were unable to match it. The author emphasizes the Prophet's persistent urging.
Why did the Prophet keep urging? To make their inability more evident.
3
Note the incomplete ending
The passage ends abruptly with 'and that is three...' likely referring to three decades of his mission. This is an incomplete thought.
The original text likely continues but is missing here.

The Quran as an Eternal Sensory-Rational Miracle
Nasafi introduces the Quran as an enduring sensory-rational miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi describes the Quran as a sensory-rational miracle that remains forever, unlike other miracles confined to specific times and places.

Core Idea
The Quran's miracle is permanent and accessible to reason and senses everywhere.

Nasafi begins by asserting the enduring nature of the Quran's inimitability. He contrasts it with other miracles that were witnessed only by specific people at specific times, requiring later generations to rely on reports. The Quran, however, is a self-sustaining miracle spread throughout the world, available for direct engagement until the end of time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
Read the opening line: 'The inimitability of the Quran remains forever.' This is the thesis. Notice how Nasafi immediately elevates the Quran above other miracles.
This sets the stage for the entire argument.
2
Contrast with other miracles
Look at how Nasafi describes other miracles: they are bound to a place and time, and later people only know them through transmitted reports. Underline the key Arabic phrases: 'يختص بمكان ويوجد في زمان'.
3
Recognize the nature of the Quran's miracle
Nasafi calls the Quran a 'sensory-rational miracle' (آية حسية عقلية). Think about what that means: it appeals to both the senses (audible, readable) and reason (its content and structure).
This dual nature makes it universally accessible.
4
Connect to the broader topic
Reflect on why this distinction matters for proving prophethood. The Quran's eternal presence means it continues to serve as a proof for all generations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إعجاز القرآن باق للأبد. وأما ما هو راجع إلى كتابه فهو من أعجب الآيات وأظهر الأعلام والدلالات إذ هو آية حسية عقلية باقية على الدهر مبثوثة في الآفاق، وغيره من الآيات يختص بمكان ويوجد في زمان ثم يصير غير من شاهدها محجوجا ببلوغ الخبر على ألسنة من شاهدها وعاينها، والقرآن باق إلى يوم القيامة منتشر في أطراف الأرض ثم فيه وجوه من الدلالات. أحدها نظمه العجيب الذي باين ما سواه من الكلام فإنه في الجملة ينقسم إلى منثور ومنظوم، والقرآن ليس من جملة الكلام المنثور، ثم المنظوم من الكلام كان عند العرب منقسماً إلى أقسام أربعة نظم الشعر، ونظم الرجز، ونظم الخطبة، ونظم الرسالة، والقرآن باين كل وجوه النظم وليس في طباع البشر أن يجيء واحد فيأتي بنظم ينفرد به عن الأمم كافة، ثم هو بهذا النظم تحدى جميع البشر وغيرهم بالقصور عند وقوعهم بالعجز دونه، وبدأ في مدح ما أتى به وأعاد وبالغ تقريظه وزاد وإن تناسوه لم يتركهم، وإن تغافلوا عنه لم يعرض عنهم حتى هيجهم ليكون ذلك أبلغ في تبكيتهم وأغيظ الدهمائهم، وأدعى إلى الاعتزاز لمغالبته والابتدار لمباراته، وكان هذا دأبه معهم منذ مبعثه إلى مخترمه وذلك ثلاث وعشرون سنة، فلم ينتدب أحد إلى مباراته ولم تصدر لمعارضته في مقدار سورة وآيات من كتابه ومنهم الفصحاء والبلغاء والفحول من الشعراء والمفوهون من الخطباء، إذ كان الزمان زمان فصاحة وبلاغة، ولم يكن عصر من الأعصار لدن آدم عليه السلام إلى زماننا هذا اجتمع فيه من فحول الشعراء الموسومين بأقصى غايات الفصاحة وأبعد نهايات البلاغة، كما لم يكن في زمان من مهرة السحرة مثل ما كان في زمان موسى عليه السلام، ولا من حذاق الأطباء مثل ما اتفق في زمان عيسى عليه السلام كل ذلك ليكون أظهر لعجز الخليفة عن معارضة ما جعل الله تعالى آية لرسله وأبين لقصورهم عن التصدي لمباراتهم فيما جعله الله تعالى علما على صدق دعوتهم، فدل عجز الفصحاء والشعراء الذين كانوا في زمانه مع ما مر من تقريعه إياهم وتبكيته لهم وتحريكهم على ذلك فإنه كان آية له معجزة من الله تعالى ليظهر به صدقه فيما ادعاه من إرسال الله تعالى إياه، ثم لا يظن بالعرب - وهم أثبت خليقة الله حقدًا وأكثرهم حمية وأنبذهم أنفة يفنى اثنان أعمارهم في التهاجي ويصيران على ما فيه من هتك الأستار، وإبداء الفواحش، ومثالب الأسلاف ومعايب الأجداد خوفًا من لحوق وصمة العجز عند التغالب وهجنة الانقطاع لدى التخاصم أنهم امتنعوا عن المعارضة مع القدرة، وتركوا ذلك عن اختيار ومكنة، وكيف يظن ذلك وهم قد بذلوا أموالهم النفيسة وخاطروا بمهجهم العزيزة، وركبوا المشاق العظيمة، وتحملوا المتاعب الشديدة من جر العساكر وتجريد البواتر، وحمل الرماح الخواطر والخوض في المهالك، وتقحم غمرات المعارك، ومبارزة الأقران ومناجزة الشجعان لإطفاء نوره وإبطال دعوته.
The inimitability of the Quran remains forever. As for what pertains to His Book, it is among the most wondrous signs and the clearest marks and indications, for it is a sensory-rational miracle enduring perpetually, spread throughout the horizons. Other miracles are specific to a place and exist in a time, then those who did not witness them are bound by the transmission of reports upon the tongues of those who witnessed and saw them. The Quran remains until the Day of Resurrection, spread in the extremities of the earth, and it contains aspects of indications. One of them is its wonderful composition that differs from all other speech, for speech in general is divided into prose and poetry, and the Quran is not from the category of prose. Then poetry among the Arabs was divided into four categories: the composition of poetry, the composition of rajaz, the composition of oratory, and the composition of epistles. The Quran differs from every kind of composition, and it is not in human nature that one person should come and produce a composition unique from all nations. Then by this composition it challenged all humans and others to incapability when they fell short of it, and it began praising what it brought, and repeated and exaggerated its commendation and increased, and if they neglected it, it did not leave them, and if they feigned ignorance of it, it did not turn away from them until it stirred them, so that would be more effective in shaming them and more angering to their masses, and more conducive to seeking pride in overcoming it and hastening to compete with it. And this was its constant practice with them from his mission to his death, which was twenty-three years. No one stepped forward to compete with it, nor did any attempt to oppose it in the measure of a surah or verses of its Book, despite the eloquent, the fluent, the master poets, and the eloquent orators among them, for the time was a time of eloquence and fluency. There was no age from the ages since Adam, peace be upon him, until our time, that gathered master poets characterized by the utmost limits of eloquence and the farthest reaches of fluency, just as there was no time with masters of sorcery like that which was in the time of Moses, peace be upon him, nor with skilled physicians like what occurred in the time of Jesus, peace be upon him. All of that was to make more apparent the incapacity of the creation to oppose what Allah made a sign for His messengers, and clearer for their inability to confront them in what Allah made a mark of the truth of their call. Thus the incapacity of the eloquent and the poets who were in his time, along with what has passed of his rebuking them and shaming them and provoking them to that, proved that it was a miracle from Allah to show his truthfulness in what he claimed of Allah sending him. Then let it not be thought of the Arabs—while they are the most firmly established of Allah's creation in rancor, the most full of zeal, and the most averse to shame, two of them spending their lives in lampooning each other and enduring what that involves of tearing down veils, revealing obscenities, and mentioning the defects of ancestors and faults of forefathers, out of fear of being branded with the stigma of incapacity in contests and the disgrace of defeat in disputes—that they refrained from opposition despite ability, and abandoned it out of choice and power. How could that be thought, while they expended their precious wealth, risked their dear lives, undertook great hardships, bore severe difficulties—dragging armies, unsheathing swords, carrying piercing spears, plunging into perils, charging into the thick of battle, dueling peers, and confronting champions—to extinguish his light and nullify his call?
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument for the miraculous inimitability (i'jaz) of the Quran as an enduring proof of the prophethood of Muhammad. Nasafi begins by stating that the Quran's inimitability remains forever. He distinguishes the Quran from other miracles: they are specific to a time and place, and later generations rely on reports, whereas the Quran is a 'sensory-rational' miracle (āya ḥissiyya 'aqliyya) spread throughout the earth and remaining until the Day of Resurrection. He then enumerates one of its aspects: its wonderful composition (naẓm). He explains that speech is either prose or poetry, and the Quran is not prose. Among the Arabs, poetry was divided into four categories: poetry, rajaz, oratory, and epistles. The Quran differs from all these forms of composition, and it is not within human nature for a single person to produce a composition unique from all nations. By this composition, the Quran challenged all humans, and the Prophet persisted in this challenge for twenty-three years, yet none of the eloquent Arabs—despite their high skill in poetry and oratory—attempted to produce anything like it, even a single surah. Nasafi draws a parallel with the miracles of earlier prophets: the time of Moses had master sorcerers, the time of Jesus had skilled physicians, and the time of Muhammad had master poets and orators. This heightens the evident incapacity. The inability of the Arabs to produce anything like the Quran, despite the Prophet's repeated provocations and their strong motivation to refute him (since they were proud and zealous), proves that the Quran is a miracle from Allah. Nasafi then refutes the possible objection that the Arabs refrained from opposition even though they were able. He argues that their character—their intense rancor, zeal, and aversion to shame—is such that they would endure extreme hardships (spending wealth, risking lives, waging wars) to avoid the stigma of incapacity. If they had been able, they would certainly have produced a rival text. Their failure is thus a decisive proof of the Quran's divine origin and the truth of Muhammad's prophethood.

Key Terms
إعجاز القرآن
آية حسية عقلية
غيره من الآيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that all miracles are equally accessible to later generations through reports, so the Quran does not have a special status.
Correction: Nasafi argues that the Quran is directly accessible and verifiable by all, not merely transmitted; it is a present miracle, whereas others are only known historically.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what makes the Quran's miracle different from other miracles?
A) It was witnessed by more people.
B) It is a sensory-rational miracle that remains forever, unlike time-bound miracles.
C) It was revealed in a language that no one could understand.
D) It contains prophecies about the future.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's inimitability is a permanent, self-evident miracle that serves as proof for all people in all times.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have heard the Quran recited many times. But have you ever personally felt the challenge of its inimitability? Today, the Quran is spread in the horizons—in your hands. What would it take for you to truly engage with it as a miracle that speaks directly to you, not just a text to recite? Commit to one specific ayah to ponder as a sign for your own life this week.
?
Nasafi says other miracles are bound to time and place, but the Quran is available to you always. If you treat the Quran as just another book, are you denying its perpetual miracle? What would change in your relationship with it if you believed it is a direct, eternal sign sent for you? Write down one change you will make today.
?
The passage contrasts reliance on testimonies of past miracles with direct access to the Quran. Are you relying on second-hand faith from scholars and parents, or have you personally confronted the Quran as a miracle? What step can you take to experience its inimitability directly?

Miracles
intermediate
6 min
The Unique Composition and Challenge of the Quran
Nasafi explains the Quran's unique composition and the challenge it posed to the Arabs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi argues that the Quran's extraordinary composition and the failed challenge to produce similar speech prove its divine origin.

Core Idea
The Quran's unique composition, defying all known forms of Arabic speech, proves it is beyond human capability.

Nasafi now delves into one specific aspect of the Quran's inimitability: its wonderful composition (naẓm). He explains how Arabic speech is divided into prose and poetry, and then poetry into four categories. The Quran does not fit any of these, yet it is eloquent and challenging. He then describes the prolonged challenge issued to the Arabs, who despite their mastery of language, could not produce anything like it.

Guided Path
1
Understand the classification of speech
Nasafi divides speech into prose (منثور) and poetry (منظوم). Then he lists four types of poetry: regular poetry, rajaz, oratory, and epistles. The Quran is not prose and differs from all these poetic forms.
This shows the Quran belongs to no known category.
2
Notice the uniqueness claim
He says the Quran 'differs from every kind of composition' and 'it is not in human nature that one person should produce a composition unique from all nations.' This highlights its supernatural origin.
3
Follow the challenge narrative
The Prophet persistently challenged the Arabs for 23 years, but no one stepped forward. Nasafi emphasizes the context: it was an age of eloquence, with master poets and orators. Yet they failed.
This failure is a key proof.
4
Compare with previous prophets
Nasafi parallels the situation with Moses (master sorcerers) and Jesus (skilled physicians). In each case, the miracle matched the expertise of the time, making the incapacity more evident.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إعجاز القرآن باق للأبد. وأما ما هو راجع إلى كتابه فهو من أعجب الآيات وأظهر الأعلام والدلالات إذ هو آية حسية عقلية باقية على الدهر مبثوثة في الآفاق، وغيره من الآيات يختص بمكان ويوجد في زمان ثم يصير غير من شاهدها محجوجا ببلوغ الخبر على ألسنة من شاهدها وعاينها، والقرآن باق إلى يوم القيامة منتشر في أطراف الأرض ثم فيه وجوه من الدلالات. أحدها نظمه العجيب الذي باين ما سواه من الكلام فإنه في الجملة ينقسم إلى منثور ومنظوم، والقرآن ليس من جملة الكلام المنثور، ثم المنظوم من الكلام كان عند العرب منقسماً إلى أقسام أربعة نظم الشعر، ونظم الرجز، ونظم الخطبة، ونظم الرسالة، والقرآن باين كل وجوه النظم وليس في طباع البشر أن يجيء واحد فيأتي بنظم ينفرد به عن الأمم كافة، ثم هو بهذا النظم تحدى جميع البشر وغيرهم بالقصور عند وقوعهم بالعجز دونه، وبدأ في مدح ما أتى به وأعاد وبالغ تقريظه وزاد وإن تناسوه لم يتركهم، وإن تغافلوا عنه لم يعرض عنهم حتى هيجهم ليكون ذلك أبلغ في تبكيتهم وأغيظ الدهمائهم، وأدعى إلى الاعتزاز لمغالبته والابتدار لمباراته، وكان هذا دأبه معهم منذ مبعثه إلى مخترمه وذلك ثلاث وعشرون سنة، فلم ينتدب أحد إلى مباراته ولم تصدر لمعارضته في مقدار سورة وآيات من كتابه ومنهم الفصحاء والبلغاء والفحول من الشعراء والمفوهون من الخطباء، إذ كان الزمان زمان فصاحة وبلاغة، ولم يكن عصر من الأعصار لدن آدم عليه السلام إلى زماننا هذا اجتمع فيه من فحول الشعراء الموسومين بأقصى غايات الفصاحة وأبعد نهايات البلاغة، كما لم يكن في زمان من مهرة السحرة مثل ما كان في زمان موسى عليه السلام، ولا من حذاق الأطباء مثل ما اتفق في زمان عيسى عليه السلام كل ذلك ليكون أظهر لعجز الخليفة عن معارضة ما جعل الله تعالى آية لرسله وأبين لقصورهم عن التصدي لمباراتهم فيما جعله الله تعالى علما على صدق دعوتهم، فدل عجز الفصحاء والشعراء الذين كانوا في زمانه مع ما مر من تقريعه إياهم وتبكيته لهم وتحريكهم على ذلك فإنه كان آية له معجزة من الله تعالى ليظهر به صدقه فيما ادعاه من إرسال الله تعالى إياه، ثم لا يظن بالعرب - وهم أثبت خليقة الله حقدًا وأكثرهم حمية وأنبذهم أنفة يفنى اثنان أعمارهم في التهاجي ويصيران على ما فيه من هتك الأستار، وإبداء الفواحش، ومثالب الأسلاف ومعايب الأجداد خوفًا من لحوق وصمة العجز عند التغالب وهجنة الانقطاع لدى التخاصم أنهم امتنعوا عن المعارضة مع القدرة، وتركوا ذلك عن اختيار ومكنة، وكيف يظن ذلك وهم قد بذلوا أموالهم النفيسة وخاطروا بمهجهم العزيزة، وركبوا المشاق العظيمة، وتحملوا المتاعب الشديدة من جر العساكر وتجريد البواتر، وحمل الرماح الخواطر والخوض في المهالك، وتقحم غمرات المعارك، ومبارزة الأقران ومناجزة الشجعان لإطفاء نوره وإبطال دعوته.

?

?

?

Refuting the Objection: Why the Arabs Did Not Respond
Nasafi refutes the objection that the Arabs could have opposed the Quran but chose not to.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's rebuttal of the claim that the Arabs refrained from challenging the Quran out of choice rather than inability.

Core Idea
The Arabs' fierce pride and enmity prove they would have opposed the Quran if they could have.

A possible objection arises: perhaps the Arabs did not try to produce a rival because they were not motivated or chose not to. Nasafi anticipates this and refutes it by highlighting the Arab character—their extreme rancor, zeal, and aversion to shame. They would rather endure war and death than be seen as incapable. Their failure to produce a rival, despite their intense desire to refute the Prophet, is the strongest proof of the Quran's miraculous nature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the anticipated objection
Nasafi addresses the idea that the Arabs refrained from opposition despite being able. Look for the phrase 'لا يظن بالعرب'.
This signals a refutation.
2
Analyze the Arab character described
Nasafi describes them as having the greatest rancor, zeal, and aversity to shame. He gives examples: they would spend years in lampooning each other, risking honor. Underline these traits.
3
Understand the counterfactual
If they had the ability, they would certainly have used it to extinguish the Prophet's light. Their actual sacrifices in war show their determination.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Conclude the argument
Thus, their inability to produce a rival is due to incapacity, not choice. This proves the Quran is a miracle.

Source Text

إعجاز القرآن باق للأبد. وأما ما هو راجع إلى كتابه فهو من أعجب الآيات وأظهر الأعلام والدلالات إذ هو آية حسية عقلية باقية على الدهر مبثوثة في الآفاق، وغيره من الآيات يختص بمكان ويوجد في زمان ثم يصير غير من شاهدها محجوجا ببلوغ الخبر على ألسنة من شاهدها وعاينها، والقرآن باق إلى يوم القيامة منتشر في أطراف الأرض ثم فيه وجوه من الدلالات. أحدها نظمه العجيب الذي باين ما سواه من الكلام فإنه في الجملة ينقسم إلى منثور ومنظوم، والقرآن ليس من جملة الكلام المنثور، ثم المنظوم من الكلام كان عند العرب منقسماً إلى أقسام أربعة نظم الشعر، ونظم الرجز، ونظم الخطبة، ونظم الرسالة، والقرآن باين كل وجوه النظم وليس في طباع البشر أن يجيء واحد فيأتي بنظم ينفرد به عن الأمم كافة، ثم هو بهذا النظم تحدى جميع البشر وغيرهم بالقصور عند وقوعهم بالعجز دونه، وبدأ في مدح ما أتى به وأعاد وبالغ تقريظه وزاد وإن تناسوه لم يتركهم، وإن تغافلوا عنه لم يعرض عنهم حتى هيجهم ليكون ذلك أبلغ في تبكيتهم وأغيظ الدهمائهم، وأدعى إلى الاعتزاز لمغالبته والابتدار لمباراته، وكان هذا دأبه معهم منذ مبعثه إلى مخترمه وذلك ثلاث وعشرون سنة، فلم ينتدب أحد إلى مباراته ولم تصدر لمعارضته في مقدار سورة وآيات من كتابه ومنهم الفصحاء والبلغاء والفحول من الشعراء والمفوهون من الخطباء، إذ كان الزمان زمان فصاحة وبلاغة، ولم يكن عصر من الأعصار لدن آدم عليه السلام إلى زماننا هذا اجتمع فيه من فحول الشعراء الموسومين بأقصى غايات الفصاحة وأبعد نهايات البلاغة، كما لم يكن في زمان من مهرة السحرة مثل ما كان في زمان موسى عليه السلام، ولا من حذاق الأطباء مثل ما اتفق في زمان عيسى عليه السلام كل ذلك ليكون أظهر لعجز الخليفة عن معارضة ما جعل الله تعالى آية لرسله وأبين لقصورهم عن التصدي لمباراتهم فيما جعله الله تعالى علما على صدق دعوتهم، فدل عجز الفصحاء والشعراء الذين كانوا في زمانه مع ما مر من تقريعه إياهم وتبكيته لهم وتحريكهم على ذلك فإنه كان آية له معجزة من الله تعالى ليظهر به صدقه فيما ادعاه من إرسال الله تعالى إياه، ثم لا يظن بالعرب - وهم أثبت خليقة الله حقدًا وأكثرهم حمية وأنبذهم أنفة يفنى اثنان أعمارهم في التهاجي ويصيران على ما فيه من هتك الأستار، وإبداء الفواحش، ومثالب الأسلاف ومعايب الأجداد خوفًا من لحوق وصمة العجز عند التغالب وهجنة الانقطاع لدى التخاصم أنهم امتنعوا عن المعارضة مع القدرة، وتركوا ذلك عن اختيار ومكنة، وكيف يظن ذلك وهم قد بذلوا أموالهم النفيسة وخاطروا بمهجهم العزيزة، وركبوا المشاق العظيمة، وتحملوا المتاعب الشديدة من جر العساكر وتجريد البواتر، وحمل الرماح الخواطر والخوض في المهالك، وتقحم غمرات المعارك، ومبارزة الأقران ومناجزة الشجعان لإطفاء نوره وإبطال دعوته.
The inimitability of the Quran remains forever. As for what pertains to His Book, it is among the most wondrous signs and the clearest marks and indications, for it is a sensory-rational miracle enduring perpetually, spread throughout the horizons. Other miracles are specific to a place and exist in a time, then those who did not witness them are bound by the transmission of reports upon the tongues of those who witnessed and saw them. The Quran remains until the Day of Resurrection, spread in the extremities of the earth, and it contains aspects of indications. One of them is its wonderful composition that differs from all other speech, for speech in general is divided into prose and poetry, and the Quran is not from the category of prose. Then poetry among the Arabs was divided into four categories: the composition of poetry, the composition of rajaz, the composition of oratory, and the composition of epistles. The Quran differs from every kind of composition, and it is not in human nature that one person should come and produce a composition unique from all nations. Then by this composition it challenged all humans and others to incapability when they fell short of it, and it began praising what it brought, and repeated and exaggerated its commendation and increased, and if they neglected it, it did not leave them, and if they feigned ignorance of it, it did not turn away from them until it stirred them, so that would be more effective in shaming them and more angering to their masses, and more conducive to seeking pride in overcoming it and hastening to compete with it. And this was its constant practice with them from his mission to his death, which was twenty-three years. No one stepped forward to compete with it, nor did any attempt to oppose it in the measure of a surah or verses of its Book, despite the eloquent, the fluent, the master poets, and the eloquent orators among them, for the time was a time of eloquence and fluency. There was no age from the ages since Adam, peace be upon him, until our time, that gathered master poets characterized by the utmost limits of eloquence and the farthest reaches of fluency, just as there was no time with masters of sorcery like that which was in the time of Moses, peace be upon him, nor with skilled physicians like what occurred in the time of Jesus, peace be upon him. All of that was to make more apparent the incapacity of the creation to oppose what Allah made a sign for His messengers, and clearer for their inability to confront them in what Allah made a mark of the truth of their call. Thus the incapacity of the eloquent and the poets who were in his time, along with what has passed of his rebuking them and shaming them and provoking them to that, proved that it was a miracle from Allah to show his truthfulness in what he claimed of Allah sending him. Then let it not be thought of the Arabs—while they are the most firmly established of Allah's creation in rancor, the most full of zeal, and the most averse to shame, two of them spending their lives in lampooning each other and enduring what that involves of tearing down veils, revealing obscenities, and mentioning the defects of ancestors and faults of forefathers, out of fear of being branded with the stigma of incapacity in contests and the disgrace of defeat in disputes—that they refrained from opposition despite ability, and abandoned it out of choice and power. How could that be thought, while they expended their precious wealth, risked their dear lives, undertook great hardships, bore severe difficulties—dragging armies, unsheathing swords, carrying piercing spears, plunging into perils, charging into the thick of battle, dueling peers, and confronting champions—to extinguish his light and nullify his call?
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument for the miraculous inimitability (i'jaz) of the Quran as an enduring proof of the prophethood of Muhammad. Nasafi begins by stating that the Quran's inimitability remains forever. He distinguishes the Quran from other miracles: they are specific to a time and place, and later generations rely on reports, whereas the Quran is a 'sensory-rational' miracle (āya ḥissiyya 'aqliyya) spread throughout the earth and remaining until the Day of Resurrection. He then enumerates one of its aspects: its wonderful composition (naẓm). He explains that speech is either prose or poetry, and the Quran is not prose. Among the Arabs, poetry was divided into four categories: poetry, rajaz, oratory, and epistles. The Quran differs from all these forms of composition, and it is not within human nature for a single person to produce a composition unique from all nations. By this composition, the Quran challenged all humans, and the Prophet persisted in this challenge for twenty-three years, yet none of the eloquent Arabs—despite their high skill in poetry and oratory—attempted to produce anything like it, even a single surah. Nasafi draws a parallel with the miracles of earlier prophets: the time of Moses had master sorcerers, the time of Jesus had skilled physicians, and the time of Muhammad had master poets and orators. This heightens the evident incapacity. The inability of the Arabs to produce anything like the Quran, despite the Prophet's repeated provocations and their strong motivation to refute him (since they were proud and zealous), proves that the Quran is a miracle from Allah. Nasafi then refutes the possible objection that the Arabs refrained from opposition even though they were able. He argues that their character—their intense rancor, zeal, and aversion to shame—is such that they would endure extreme hardships (spending wealth, risking lives, waging wars) to avoid the stigma of incapacity. If they had been able, they would certainly have produced a rival text. Their failure is thus a decisive proof of the Quran's divine origin and the truth of Muhammad's prophethood.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Arabs did not try to imitate the Quran because they respected it or were not interested.
Correction: Nasafi shows that their intense enmity and pride would have driven them to compete if they could.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what does the Arab practice of spending their lives in poetic lampooning demonstrate?
A) Their love for poetry
B) Their fear of being called incapable
C) Their respect for the Quran
D) Their lack of eloquence

Key Takeaway
The Arabs' fierce pride and relentless opposition show that their failure to produce a rival to the Quran was due to incapacity, not choice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you been more concerned about your reputation in the eyes of people than about pleasing Allah? How can you recalibrate your priorities to value Allah's approval above all else?
?
The Arabs spent their wealth and risked their lives to oppose the truth. What are you spending your wealth and life on today? Are you willing to spend as much in pursuit of truth as they spent in opposition?
?
Think of a time you avoided doing something right because you feared being seen as incapable or stupid. How does Nasafi's argument about Arab pride expose that fear in you? What step can you take this week to choose obedience over pride?

Miracles
intermediate
6 min
The Arabs' Inability to Challenge the Qur'an: A Proof of Divine Origin
Nasafi argues from the Arabs' failure to challenge the Qur'an to its divine origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses the historical fact of the Arabs' failure to challenge the Qur'an, despite their eloquence and hostility, as a rational proof of its inimitability and divine origin.

Core Idea
The Arabs' failure to challenge the Qur'an, despite every motive and ability, proves it is from Allah.

Nasafi presents a multi-layered argument for the inimitability (i'jaz) of the Qur'an. He begins by noting the historical context: for twenty years, the most eloquent Arabs could not produce a single surah like it. He then compares this to the miracles of Moses and Jesus, where contemporary experts were unable to match them. Finally, he refutes the objection that the Arabs might have refrained from challenging out of choice, demonstrating that their intense hostility and practical interests would have driven them to do so if they could. This passage lays out a cumulative proof that the Qur'an is a divine miracle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Nasafi uses a very detailed and repetitive style for emphasis.
2
Identify the three main parts
The passage has three clear sections: the historical fact of no challenge, the analogy with previous prophets, and the refutation of the idea that Arabs refrained by choice.
Each section builds on the previous one.
3
Examine Nasafi's description of the Arabs
Pay attention to how Nasafi describes the Arabs' eloquence, intellect, and hostility. Why does he emphasize these traits?
These traits are crucial for his argument that their failure was due to inability, not choice.
4
Understand the logical conclusion
Nasafi concludes that the Arabs were compelled by inability, not choice. Follow how he eliminates the possibility of voluntary refrainment.
This is the core of the proof of inimitability.
5
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how all the pieces fit together: historical fact, analogy, refutation of counterarguments. Why is this a strong proof?
This argument is a classic example of kalam reasoning.

وعشرون سنة، فلم ينتدب أحد إلى مباراته ولم تصدر لمعارضته في مقدار سورة وآيات من كتابه ومنهم الفصحاء والبلغاء والفحول من الشعراء والمفوهون من الخطباء، إذ كان الزمان زمان فصاحة وبلاغة، ولم يكن عصر من الأعصار لدن آدم عليه السلام إلى زماننا هذا اجتمع فيه من فحول الشعراء الموسومين بأقصى غايات الفصاحة وأبعد نهايات البلاغة، كما لم يكن في زمان من مهرة السحرة مثل ما كان في زمان موسى عليه السلام، ولا من حذاق الأطباء مثل ما اتفق في زمان عيسى عليه السلام كل ذلك ليكون أظهر لعجز الخليفة عن معارضة ما جعل الله تعالى آية لرسله وأبين لقصورهم عن التصدي لمباراتهم فيما جعله الله تعالى علما على صدق دعوتهم، فدل عجز الفصحاء والشعراء الذين كانوا في زمانه مع ما مر من تقريعه إياهم وتبكيته لهم وتحريكهم على ذلك فإنه كان آية له معجزة من الله تعالى ليظهر به صدقه فيما ادعاه من إرسال الله تعالى إياه، ثم لا يظن بالعرب - وهم أثبت خليقة الله حقدًا وأكثرهم حمية وأنبذهم أنفة يفنى اثنان أعمارهم في التهاجي ويصيران على ما فيه من هتك الأستار، وإبداء الفواحش، ومثالب الأسلاف ومعايب الأجداد خوفًا من لحوق وصمة العجز عند التغالب وهجنة الانقطاع لدى التخاصم أنهم امتنعوا عن المعارضة مع القدرة، وتركوا ذلك عن اختيار ومكنة، وكيف يظن ذلك وهم قد بذلوا أموالهم النفيسة وخاطروا بمهجهم العزيزة، وركبوا المشاق العظيمة، وتحملوا المتاعب الشديدة من جر العساكر وتجريد البواتر، وحمل الرماح الخواطر والخوض في المهالك، وتقحم غمرات المعارك، ومبارزة الأقران ومناجزة الشجعان لإطفاء نوره وإبطال دعوته، مع أنهم لو ظفروا به وبأتباعه وتمكنوا من إراقة دمه ودماء أشياعه لم يقدح ذلك في صدق نبوته ولم يظهر بذلك كذبه ولم تندفع حجته، ولو عارضوه في سورة واحدة فلحت حجتهم وظهرت نصرتهم، وثبت للداني والقاصي والغريب والبعيد كذبه وارتد قوله ونابذه أصحابه وباينه أنصاره وأعوانه، وكفى أعداءه مؤنة قتاله ومعرة حرابه وجداله، ولا شك أن العرب وإن كانوا أميين خالين عن صناعة الكلام وآداب الجدل والعلم بتوحيد الله ودلائله كانوا أوفر خليقة الله تعالى عقولاً وأكملهم أحلاما، ترى الرجل منهم وقد نشأ في البوادي والبراري لم يعن بتعلم علم ولا ارتاض بشيء من أصناف الحكم يتكلم بحكمة بليغة وطرف بديعة بلفظ محكم الصنعة رائع النظم بارع الوصف وقريش منهم المخصوصون برجاحة العقول والألباب، وكثرة النهي والأحلام، وغاية الدهاء والفكر والحيل اللطيفة في رفع ما ينوبهم من معضلات الأمور، والتخلص عما يقعون فيه من موبقات الفتن، ثم إن أقل خليقة لله تعالى عقلاً وأكثرهم غباوة وحمقا لا يعدل في مغالبة خصمه ومخاصمة عدوه عما سهل طريقه، وخفت مؤنته وانقطع به خصمه، واندفعت مادة معرته إلى ما تكثر مؤنته وتشتد صعوبته ويثقل تحمله ويتوعر طريقه، ومعرة الخصم بعد باقية وفرحته دائمة، فكيف يظن هذا بمن مر وصفه وسبق نعته؟! فإذا لا يشك عاقل أنهم امتنعوا عن ذلك عجزا منهم واضطرارًا لا اختيارًا وإيثاراً. يحققه أن حيرة لزوم الحجة وثبوت العجز دفعتهم إلى التكلم بالهذيان
And twenty years, so no one came forward to compete with him and no one produced a challenge to it to the extent of a sura or verses from his book, while they included the eloquent, the fluent, the great poets, and the articulate orators, since the time was a time of eloquence and fluency. And there was no era from the eras since Adam, peace be upon him, to our present time in which there gathered such great poets characterized by the utmost limits of eloquence and the farthest ends of fluency, just as there was not in any time master sorcerers like those in the time of Moses, peace be upon him, nor skilled physicians like those that occurred in the time of Jesus, peace be upon him; all that so that the inability of the creatures to oppose what God Almighty made a sign for His messengers would be more apparent, and their deficiency in confronting their competition in what God Almighty made a sign of the truth of their call would be clearer. So the inability of the eloquent and the poets who were in his time, along with the aforementioned reprimanding and rebuking and inciting them to that, indicated that it was a sign and a miracle from God Almighty to show the truth of his claim that God Almighty sent him. Then it should not be thought of the Arabs—and they are the most steadfast of God's creatures in rancor, the most zealous, the most disdainful, to the point that two of them spend their lives lampooning each other and persist in what involves tearing of veils, revealing obscenities, and criticizing ancestors and blaming forefathers for fear of the stigma of inability when competing and the disgrace of being defeated when disputing—that they refrained from challenging while having the ability, and left it out of choice and power. How could that be thought, while they had expended their precious wealth, risked their dear lives, undertaken great hardships, and endured severe difficulties—marching armies, drawing swords, carrying piercing spears, plunging into perils, surging into the thick of battles, dueling with peers, and fighting with the valiant—to extinguish his light and nullify his call? Yet if they had overpowered him and his followers and were able to shed his blood and the blood of his partisans, that would not have harmed the truth of his prophethood, nor would his falsehood have appeared thereby, nor would his proof have been repelled. And if they had challenged him in a single sura, their argument would have succeeded, their victory would have appeared, and for the near and far, the stranger and the distant, his falsehood would have been established, his word rejected, his companions would have deserted him, his supporters and helpers would have split from him, and he would have spared his enemies the burden of fighting him and the trouble of war and debate. And there is no doubt that the Arabs, even though they were illiterate, devoid of the art of speech, the etiquette of debate, and knowledge of the oneness of God and its proofs, were the most abundant of God's creatures in intellect and the most perfect in forbearance. You see a man among them, having grown up in the deserts and wilderness, not engaged in learning any science nor trained in any kind of wisdom, speaking with eloquent wisdom and novel subtleties, with speech solidly crafted, wondrously composed, and excellently described. And Quraysh among them were distinguished for soundness of intellects and minds, abundance of reason and forbearance, extreme cunning, thought, and subtle devices in resolving complex matters that befell them and escaping from deadly seditions they fell into. Then, the least of God's creatures in intellect and the most foolish and stupid would not turn away, in overcoming his opponent and disputing with his enemy, from what is easy in its path, light in its burden, and by which his opponent is overcome and the substance of his trouble is repelled, to what is heavy in its burden, severe in its difficulty, difficult to bear, and rugged in its path—while the trouble of the opponent remains and his joy is lasting. So how can this be thought of those whose description has passed and whose attribute has preceded? Thus, no intelligent person doubts that they refrained from that out of inability and necessity, not choice and preference. This is verified by the fact that perplexity at the binding proof and the confirmation of inability drove them to speak nonsense.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a detailed proof of the inimitability (i'jaz) of the Qur'an, arguing from the historical fact that the Arabs, despite their eloquence and intense hostility to the Prophet, were unable to produce anything like it. The author (Nasafi) begins by noting that for twenty years (the duration of the Prophet's mission) no one came forward to challenge the Qur'an, even though the Arabs were masters of eloquence. He then draws a parallel with the miracles of previous prophets: the era of Moses had master sorcerers, and the era of Jesus had skilled physicians, making the miracles more striking; similarly, the Arabs' eloquence made the Qur'anic challenge more compelling. He then argues against the possibility that the Arabs refrained from challenging out of choice. He emphasizes their intense rancor, zeal, and pride, as seen in their habit of lampooning each other, showing they were not averse to verbal contest. They risked their lives and wealth to oppose the Prophet, yet they could not produce a single sura to disprove him. Moreover, a single successful challenge would have been easier and more effective than warfare, and would have destroyed his mission. Therefore, their failure must be due to inability, not choice. He supports this by noting the Arabs' sharp intellects and Quraysh's cunning, which would have led them to the easier path of a literary challenge if it were possible. Hence, rational thinkers conclude that they were compelled by inability, and their resort to incoherent speech (al-hadhyan) confirms their desperation. The commentary should follow this sequence: statement of fact, comparison to previous miracles, refutation of the alternative explanation (choice), demonstration of motives and means, logical deduction of inability, and concluding verification.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Arabs did not challenge the Qur'an because they were uninterested or considered it merely poetry.
Correction: Nasafi shows they were intensely hostile and would have benefited from a successful challenge, so their failure must be due to inability, not lack of interest.

Checkpoint
Why does Nasafi argue that the Arabs' failure to challenge the Qur'an proves its inimitability?
A) Because the Arabs were illiterate and could not compose poetry.
B) Because the Arabs had strong motives to disprove the Prophet but were unable despite their eloquence.
C) Because the Prophet forbade them from trying.
D) Because the Qur'an is too long to imitate.

Key Takeaway
The Arabs' failure to produce a single surah, despite their eloquence and enmity, is a decisive proof that the Qur'an is the word of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Arabs, with all their eloquence and enmity, could not deny the Qur'an's divine origin, what excuses have you been making to avoid submitting to its commands? What 'challenge' have you avoided out of inability rather than choice?
?
The passage highlights the Arabs' desperation to silence the Prophet, yet they failed. In what areas of your life are you resisting the truth of the Qur'an, and what would it mean to finally accept that it is from Allah?
?
Consider the Arabs' intelligence and cunning—they knew the easier path would be to produce a sura, yet they couldn't. How does this challenge your own self-reliance? Are there areas where you think you can 'beat' the Qur'an's message on your own terms?

Miracles
beginner
5 min
The Arabs' Inability to Produce a Surah Proves the Quran's Miracle
The author argues that the Arabs' failure to produce a surah confirms the Quran's miraculous nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Arabs' inability to produce a surah like the Quran serves as a decisive proof of its miraculous nature, based on their intelligence and motives.

Core Idea
The Arabs' failure to produce a surah, despite their eloquence and motive, is the clearest proof of the Quran's miracle.

In this passage, the author presents a powerful argument for the Quran's inimitability. He notes that even if the Arabs had defeated the Prophet militarily, that would not disprove his prophethood. But if they had succeeded in producing a single surah like the Quran, it would have been definitive proof of his falsehood. Since they did not, despite their fierce opposition and literary skill, their failure confirms the Quran's divine origin.

Guided Path
1
Understand the hypothetical scenario
The author sets up a conditional: if the Arabs had produced a surah, it would have proven the Prophet false. This shows the stakes of the challenge.
Contrast this with military defeat, which would not have disproven his prophethood.
2
Recognize the Arabs' motives
The Arabs had strong motives to discredit the Prophet, including fighting and risking their lives. So their failure to produce a surah cannot be due to lack of desire.
3
Assess their intellectual capability
The author describes the Arabs, especially Quraysh, as highly intelligent and eloquent, demonstrating that they were capable of meeting a literary challenge if it were possible.
This counters any claim that they were too ignorant to produce a similar text.
4
Observe their choice of difficulty
Even a foolish person would choose the easier path of verbal challenge over war. The Arabs chose war, proving they were unable to produce a surah.
This argument from preference solidifies the conclusion of inability.
5
Conclude the miraculous nature
The author concludes that no rational person can doubt that the Arabs refrained from producing a surah out of inability, not choice. This confirms the Quran's miraculous inimitability.
The final line about speaking nonsense underscores their desperation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غمرات المعارك، ومبارزة الأقران ومناجزة الشجعان لإطفاء نوره وإبطال دعوته، مع أنهم لو ظفروا به وبأتباعه وتمكنوا من إراقة دمه ودماء أشياعه لم يقدح ذلك في صدق نبوته ولم يظهر بذلك كذبه ولم تندفع حجته، ولو عارضوه في سورة واحدة فلحت حجتهم وظهرت نصرتهم، وثبت للداني والقاصي والغريب والبعيد كذبه وارتد قوله ونابذه أصحابه وباينه أنصاره وأعوانه، وكفى أعداءه مؤنة قتاله ومعرة حرابه وجداله، ولا شك أن العرب وإن كانوا أميين خالين عن صناعة الكلام وآداب الجدل والعلم بتوحيد الله ودلائله كانوا أوفر خليقة الله تعالى عقولاً وأكملهم أحلاما، ترى الرجل منهم وقد نشأ في البوادي والبراري لم يعن بتعلم علم ولا ارتاض بشيء من أصناف الحكم يتكلم بحكمة بليغة وطرف بديعة بلفظ محكم الصنعة رائع النظم بارع الوصف وقريش منهم المخصوصون برجاحة العقول والألباب، وكثرة النهي والأحلام، وغاية الدهاء والفكر والحيل اللطيفة في رفع ما ينوبهم من معضلات الأمور، والتخلص عما يقعون فيه من موبقات الفتن، ثم إن أقل خليقة لله تعالى عقلاً وأكثرهم غباوة وحمقا لا يعدل في مغالبة خصمه ومخاصمة عدوه عما سهل طريقه، وخفت مؤنته وانقطع به خصمه، واندفعت مادة معرته إلى ما تكثر مؤنته وتشتد صعوبته ويثقل تحمله ويتوعر طريقه، ومعرة الخصم بعد باقية وفرحته دائمة، فكيف يظن هذا بمن مر وصفه وسبق نعته؟! فإذا لا يشك عاقل أنهم امتنعوا عن ذلك عجزا منهم واضطرارًا لا اختيارًا وإيثاراً. يحققه أن حيرة لزوم الحجة وثبوت العجز دفعتهم إلى التكلم بالهذيان
The waves of battles, and the facing of peers, and the wrestling of brave ones to extinguish his light and nullify his call, even if they had overcome him and his followers and were able to shed his blood and the blood of his partisans, that would not have impaired the truth of his prophethood, nor would his falsehood have appeared thereby, nor would his proof have been repelled. But if they had opposed him with a single surah, their proof would have been successful and their victory would have appeared, and for the near and far, the stranger and the distant, his falsehood would have been established, his word would have been rejected, his companions would have abandoned him, his supporters and helpers would have parted from him, and it would have sufficed his enemies the trouble of fighting him and the disgrace of his war and argument. There is no doubt that the Arabs, even though they were illiterate, devoid of the art of kalam and the etiquettes of debate and knowledge of God's oneness and its proofs, were the most intelligent of God's creation and the most perfect in forbearance. You see a man among them who grew up in the deserts and wildernesses, not occupied with learning any science nor trained in any kind of wisdom, speaking with eloquent wisdom and delightful subtleties in a statement firmly constructed, marvelous in composition, excellent in description. And Quraysh among them were especially distinguished by soundness of intellects and minds, abundance of forbearance and dreams, and utmost cunning, thought, and subtle tricks in lifting the difficult affairs that befell them, and in extricating themselves from the deadly afflictions they fell into. Then the least intelligent of God's creation and the most foolish and stupid among them does not turn in overcoming his opponent and disputing his enemy from what is easy in his path, light in its burden, and by which his opponent is cut off, and the matter of his disgrace is repelled, to what is more burdensome, severe, heavy, and rugged. And the disgrace of the opponent remains and his joy is permanent. So how can this be thought of those whose description and attributes have passed and preceded? Therefore, no rational person doubts that they refrained from that out of inability and compulsion, not choice and preference. This is confirmed by the fact that the bewilderment of being bound by the proof and the establishment of inability drove them to speak nonsense.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the miraculous nature of the Quran based on the Arabs' inability to produce a similar surah despite having strong motives and ability. The author begins by noting that even if the Arabs had killed the Prophet and his followers, that would not disprove his prophethood. However, if they had successfully produced a single surah like the Quran, that would have proven him false and caused his followers to abandon him. Therefore, the fact that they did not produce such a surah, despite their fierce opposition, is strong evidence. The author then describes the Arabs' intelligence and eloquence, especially the Quraysh, to show that they were capable of literary challenge. He argues that even a foolish person would choose the easier path to defeat an opponent, but the Arabs chose the harder path of warfare instead of the easier verbal challenge. This shows they were unable to meet the challenge. The passage concludes that their inability forced them to resort to incoherent speech, confirming the Quran's miracle.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the Prophet's military success is what proves his prophethood.
Correction: This passage clarifies that the Quran's inimitability is the primary proof, not military victory.

Checkpoint

C) The Arabs would have converted to Islam.

Key Takeaway
The Arabs' inability to produce a surah like the Quran, despite their eloquence and fierce opposition, is the decisive proof of the Quran's miraculous nature.

?
If this argument is sound—that the Quran's inimitability is decisive—then where does your hesitation in living by it come from? What will you do about that hesitation before you sleep tonight?

Refuting al-Warraq on Wars Occupying the Arabs
Author refutes al-Warraq's objection by presenting historical evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes al-Warraq's objection by citing the peaceful Meccan period and the limited nature of post-Hijra battles.

Core Idea
The Quranic challenge predates any warfare – the Arabs had 13 peaceful years to respond.

Al-Warraq, a former Qadari turned Dualist, argued that the Prophet's wars prevented the Arabs from producing a surah like the Quran. The author dismisses this as absurd and provides a detailed counterargument. Let's examine the refutation step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Warraq's claim
Al-Warraq claimed that the Arabs were too occupied by wars with the Prophet to attempt the challenge to produce a surah like the Quran.
The author calls this claim so ridiculous that even a madman would not say it.
2
Examine the Meccan period
The Prophet spent 13 years in Mecca peacefully challenging the Arabs without any warfare. He openly called them to monotheism and challenged them to produce a surah.
This period had no battles, so the excuse of occupation is invalid.
3
Consider the post-Hijra period
After Hijra, the battles were few and only involved specific tribes. Most Arabs never fought the Prophet. Yet they still did not produce a surah.
The author sarcastically asks why the Prophet was not occupied by wars while being alone, yet the Arabs with their many eloquent speakers were.
4
Conclude the refutation
The author concludes that al-Warraq's claim is clearly impossible and only clung to by stubborn opponents.
This highlights the Quran's miraculous nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعتراض للوراق والرد عليه وما زعم الوراق بعد انتقاله من مذاهب القدرية إلى مذاهب إخوانهم من الثنوية جريًا منه على قياد ما يفضي إليه المذهب أن حروبهم معه شغلتهم عن المعارضة كلام لو تفوه به مجنون لتعجب الناس من ذلك، فكيف إذا تكلم به عند المجادلة والمحاجة من يدعي العلم، ويخوض في الكلام، ولكن الغريق يتعلق بكل شيء فنقول له: إنه مكث بمكة ثلاث عشرة سنة يتحداهم بذلك، ويقرعهم آناء الليل والنهار، ويبكتهم في المحافل والمجامع، وكان انتشر أمره في جميع ديار العرب، وبلغ أقصى نهاية جزيرتها لما كان يعرض نفسه في أيام الموسم على قبائل العرب، ويدعوهم إلى عبادة الله، وينهاهم عما كانوا يدينون به من عبادة الأوثان، ويسفه أحلامهم وأحلام آبائهم الذين كانوا يتفاخرون بمفاخرهم ويتباهون بمناقبهم ومآثرهم، ويتحداهم بالقرآن ويأمرهم بإتيان سورة من مثله، ولم يكن طول تلك المدة بينهم حراب ولا طعان وضراب، فلم لم يعارضوا في تلك المدة وقد تفرغوا له ولم يشغلهم عن ذلك شاغل ولا منعهم عن ذلك مانع؟! ثم بعدما هاجر إلى المدينة فغزواته معدودة، ومن اشتغل بقتاله من القبائل معروف، وأكثر العرب ما قابلوه بالقتال ولا قاوموه في محال، فما بال أولئك لم يعارضوه في سورة ولم يقابلوه في آيات يسيرة؟!. ثم ما باله لم تشغله تلك الحروب وهو متوحد الذات، وقد شغل جميع العرب مع كثرة ما فيهم من الفصحاء والبلغاء؟! هذا والله المحال الظاهر الذي لا يتعلق به إلا كل مكابر معاند.
Objection of al-Warraq and the response to it. Al-Warraq claimed, after moving from the doctrines of the Qadariyya to the doctrines of their brothers among the Dualists, following the lead of what the doctrine leads to, that their wars with him occupied them from the challenge. This is speech which if uttered by a madman, people would marvel at it. So how about when it is spoken in debate and argument by one who claims knowledge and delves into kalam? But the drowning man clings to everything. So we say to him: He stayed in Mecca thirteen years challenging them with it, rebuking them night and day, and shaming them in assemblies and gatherings. His affair had spread throughout all the lands of the Arabs, reaching the farthest end of the peninsula, when he would present himself during the season to the Arab tribes, calling them to worship God, forbidding them from what they used to practice of idol worship, deeming their intellects and the intellects of their fathers foolish—those who boasted of their glories and prided themselves on their merits and exploits—and he challenged them with the Quran and commanded them to bring a surah like it. During that entire period there was no war, stabbing, or striking between them. So why did they not challenge him in that period while they were free for him, with nothing occupying them nor preventing them? Then after he migrated to Medina, his campaigns are countable, and the tribes that engaged in fighting him are known. Most of the Arabs did not meet him with war nor resist him in any arena. So what is the matter with those who did not challenge him with a surah nor confront him with a few verses? Then why was he not occupied by those wars while he was single in essence, yet he occupied all the Arabs despite the many eloquent speakers and rhetoricians among them? This, by God, is clear impossibility which only every stubborn opponent clings to.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of al-Warraq's objection. Al-Warraq claimed that the Arabs were too occupied by wars with the Prophet to attempt producing a surah like the Quran. The author dismisses this as absurd, saying even a madman would not say such a thing. He then provides a detailed response: the Prophet spent thirteen years in Mecca peacefully challenging the Arabs, without any warfare. He would confront them publicly, in the day and night, at seasonal fairs, calling them to monotheism and criticizing their idols. He explicitly challenged them to produce a single surah. They had ample time and opportunity, with no obstacles. After the Hijra, the number of battles was limited, and most Arabs never fought him. Those who did fight could have still attempted the literary challenge. The author highlights that the Prophet, being one person, was not occupied by wars, yet the Arabs with their many eloquent speakers were unable to meet the challenge. Therefore, al-Warraq's claim is clearly false.

Correction: The passage shows the challenge existed long before any warfare, and even after battles, most Arabs never fought and still failed to produce a surah.

?

?
The Arabs had eloquence but no sincerity. Where in your life do you rely on your own skills or reputation instead of submitting to the truth of Allah's revelation? What would true submission look like today?
?
You claim to believe in the Quran, but do you treat its challenge as binding on you? If the Arabs were held accountable for rejecting it, how will you respond to its call in your daily choices? What will you do from today to live as if the Quran is truly the Word of God?

Refuting Al-Nazzam's Denial of the Quran's Inimitability
The author begins to refute al-Nazzam's claim that the Quran is not inimitable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Nazzam's flawed argument against the Quran's inimitability and why it fails.

Core Idea
Al-Nazzam's claim proves the opposite: if anyone could match the Quran, why hasn't it been done?

Al-Nazzam, a Mu'tazilite theologian, argued that the Quran's composition is not miraculously inimitable, claiming even a dull-witted person could produce something similar. This lesson examines his claim and the beginning of the refutation, showing why his argument is self-defeating.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to understand al-Nazzam's claim and the author's initial response.
2
Identify al-Nazzam's key assertion
Notice that al-Nazzam claims the Quran is not inimitable in composition and that anyone, even a tongue-tied person, could produce something similar.
3
Analyze his proof
His proof is that whenever someone fails to produce it, that doesn't prove impossibility. The passage is cut off, so consider what the full argument might be.
The author likely responds that if it were possible, someone would have already done it.
4
Reflect on the self-defeating nature
Ask yourself: If al-Nazzam's claim were true, why hasn't he or anyone else produced a text like the Quran? This reveals the weakness of his argument.
The Quran's continued uniqueness is evidence of its miraculous nature.

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of al-Nazzam's claim that the Quran is not miraculously inimitable. Al-Nazzam asserted that even a dull, tongue-tied person could produce something like the Quran's composition and description. His argument was based on the idea that whenever someone fails to produce it, that does not prove impossibility. The passage is cut off, but the response likely argues that al-Nazzam's claim is self-defeating because if it were true, he or others would have already produced a similar text, but they have not. The Quran's unique eloquence and beauty remain unmatched, proving its miraculous nature.

Refutation of al-Warraq's Objection about Wars
Refutation of al-Warraq's objection that the Prophet's wars occupied opponents from challenging the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's thirteen years in Mecca without war disproves al-Warraq's claim that wars prevented the Quranic challenge.

Core Idea
The Quranic challenge was issued before any war—failure to meet it proves its inimitability.

Al-Warraq, a heretic who shifted from Qadariyya to Dualism, argued that the Prophet's wars occupied the Arabs from challenging the Qur'an. This lesson examines the refutation offered by Imam al-Nasafi, which highlights the thirteen-year Meccan period of open challenge without conflict.

Guided Path
1
Understand al-Warraq's Claim
Al-Warraq claimed that the Prophet's wars prevented the Arabs from producing a challenge to the Qur'an. Notice how the author dismisses this as absurd.
The author compares it to a madman's speech.
2
Examine the Meccan Argument
The Prophet stayed in Mecca for thirteen years challenging the Arabs without any war. They were free to respond but did not. This is the core refutation.
3
Consider the Medinan Continuation
After migration, most Arabs did not fight, and those who fought were few. Yet still no challenge was produced. The author also notes the Prophet’s singular occupation of all Arabs.
The argument concludes that only an obstinate person would cling to al-Warraq's claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما زعم الوراق - بعد انتقاله من مذاهب القدرية إلى مذاهب إخوانهم من الثنوية جريًا منه على قياد ما يفضي إليه -المذهب أن حروبهم معه شغلتهم عن المعارضة كلام لو تفوه به مجنون لتعجب الناس من ذلك، فكيف إذا تكلم به عند المجادلة والمحاجة من يدعي العلم، ويخوض في الكلام، ولكن الغريق يتعلق بكل شيء فنقول له: إنه مكث بمكة ثلاث عشرة سنة يتحداهم بذلك، ويقرعهم آناء الليل والنهار، ويبكتهم في المحافل والمجامع، وكان انتشر أمره في جميع ديار العرب، وبلغ أقصى نهاية جزيرتها لما كان يعرض نفسه في أيام الموسم على قبائل العرب، ويدعوهم إلى عبادة الله، وينهاهم عما كانوا يدينون به من عبادة الأوثان، ويسفه أحلامهم وأحلام آبائهم الذين كانوا يتفاخرون بمفاخرهم ويتباهون بمناقبهم ومآثرهم، ويتحداهم بالقرآن ويأمرهم بإتيان سورة من مثله، ولم يكن طول تلك المدة بينهم حراب ولا طعان وضراب، فلم لم يعارضوا في تلك المدة وقد تفرغوا له ولم يشغلهم عن ذلك شاغل ولا منعهم عن ذلك مانع ؟! ثم بعدما هاجر إلى المدينة فغزواته معدودة، ومن اشتغل بقتاله من القبائل معروف، وأكثر العرب ما قابلوه بالقتال ولا قاوموه في محال، فما بال أولئك لم يعارضوه في سورة ولم يقابلوه في آيات يسيرة؟!. ثم ما باله لم تشغله تلك الحروب وهو متوحد الذات، وقد شغل جميع العرب مع كثرة ما فيهم من الفصحاء والبلغاء ؟! هذا والله المحال الظاهر الذي لا يتعلق به إلا كل مكابر معاند.
And what al-Warraq claimed — after his transfer from the doctrines of the Qadariyya to the doctrines of their brothers the Dualists, proceeding on his part according to what his path leads to — that their wars with him occupied them from opposing [the Quran] is speech that if a madman uttered it, people would be astonished. How then [can it be spoken] at the time of argument and debate by one who claims knowledge and wades into discourse? But the drowning man clings to everything. So we say to him: He stayed in Mecca for thirteen years challenging them with that, rebuking them night and day, and shaming them in assemblies and gatherings. His affair spread throughout all the lands of the Arabs and reached the farthest extent of the peninsula, as he presented himself during the season to the tribes of the Arabs, calling them to worship of God, forbidding them from what they used to practice of worshiping idols, and deeming foolish their intellects and the intellects of their fathers who boasted of their exploits and took pride in their virtues and merits. He challenged them with the Qur'an and ordered them to bring a sura like it. During all that time there was no war, no spear-thrusting, no striking. So why did they not oppose during that period, when they had leisure for him, and no preoccupation occupied them nor any preventer prevented them?! Then after he emigrated to Medina, his military expeditions were countable, and those tribes that engaged in fighting him are known, and most Arabs did not meet him with fighting nor resist him in any place. So what is wrong with those [who fought] that they did not oppose him in a sura nor match him in a few verses?! Then what is wrong that those wars did not occupy him while he was singular in person, yet he occupied all the Arabs despite the many eloquent speakers and orators among them? This, by God, is the manifest impossibility that no one clings to except every obstinate opponent.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer refutation of a claim by al-Warraq, a heretic who moved from Qadariyya to Dualist views. He argued that the Prophet's wars occupied the Arabs so they could not produce a challenge to the Qur'an. The author says such speech would astonish people even from a madman, let alone from one who claims knowledge. The refutation proceeds: The Prophet stayed in Mecca for thirteen years challenging them without any war, yet they failed to produce a sura. He presented himself at the season, called them to God, forbade idolatry, and challenged them. They were free and not occupied by war, but they did not oppose. After Hijra, the battles were few and most Arabs did not fight him. So why did those who fought not produce a challenge? Moreover, the Prophet was one person yet occupied all the Arabs; the wars did not occupy him. So the claim is impossible and only an obstinate person would cling to it.

Correction: The passage shows the challenge was given continuously during the thirteen-year Meccan period, without any war.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet challenged the Arabs openly for 13 years, yet they made excuses. What excuse have you been using to avoid fully engaging with the Quran's message? Are you willing to drop it and respond sincerely?
?
Al-Warraq clung to a weak argument simply because he was drowning in denial. What weak argument have you been holding onto that prevents you from submitting to the truth of the Quran? Will you release it today?
?
The Prophet alone, with no army at first, occupied the minds of all the eloquent Arabs—yet you may be more concerned with what others think than with the truth of this Book. Will you let the Quran occupy your heart instead of the opinions of people?
