Miracles
beginner
5 min
The Four Types of Violations of Custom
Taxonomy of four violations of custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four categories of violations of custom (an-naqid li'l-'ada) and how they are distinguished based on the agent and purpose.

Core Idea
Not every supernatural act is a miracle; context and agent determine the category.

In this passage, the author completes the discussion of supernatural events by providing a clear taxonomy. Not all breaks in natural law are miracles; they can also be acts of divine assistance, charisma granted to saints, or even humiliation for sorcerers. Learning this classification helps us correctly interpret extraordinary events in light of Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation to get the full context. Note the four terms introduced at the end.
The passage builds up to the taxonomy through examples.
2
Identify the four types
Find the four categories listed: mu'jiza, karama, ma'una, ihanah. Understand the Arabic terms.
3
Understand the distinctions
The passage provides clues: ma'una is for a disliked person, karama for a saint, mu'jiza for a prophet, ihanah for a sorcerer. Reflect on how the agent defines the type.
4
Connect to the learning objective
Ask yourself: Why does this classification matter? How does it prevent misunderstanding supernatural events?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومكروه أقبل عليه، ويسمى ذلك معونة لا كرامة، وقد تظهر أيضا على يد المتأله وعلى يد الساحر عند انعدام دعوى النبوة، ولهذا ذكر محمد بن الحسن رواية عن أبي حنيفة - رحمهما الله - أن المؤخذ بمنزلة العنين وهو الذي أخذ بالسحر عن النساء ويكون ذلك إهانة لمن ظهر على يديه. وجاء من هذا أن الناقض للعادة على أنواع أربعة معجزة، وكرامة، ومعونة، وإهانة، والفرق بينها ما بينا.
And disliked [something] he accepted, and that is called assistance (ma'una) not charisma (karama), and it may also appear at the hand of the one who claims divinity (al-muta'allih) and at the hand of the sorcerer (as-sahir) when there is no claim of prophethood, and for this reason Muhammad ibn al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa - may Allah have mercy on them both - that the one affected by magic is like the impotent (al-'anin) and he is the one who was affected by magic from women, and that is a humiliation (ihana) for the one upon whose hands it appeared. And from this it follows that the violator of custom (an-naqid li'l-'ada) is of four types: miracle (mu'jiza), charisma (karama), assistance (ma'una), and humiliation (ihana), and the difference between them is as we have explained.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage defines and classifies supernatural events that break natural law. It begins by describing a situation where an act is considered 'ma'una' (assistance) rather than 'karama' (charisma), and states that such events can appear through a person who claims divinity or a sorcerer who does not claim prophethood. Then it cites a tradition from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan quoting Abu Hanifa that the one affected by magic is like an impotent man, and that magic appearing through him is a humiliation (ihana). From these examples, the author concludes that violations of custom are of four types: miracle (mu'jiza), charisma (karama), assistance (ma'una), and humiliation (ihana), and the distinction between them has already been explained. The passage thus provides a complete taxonomy of supernatural occurrences based on the status of the person through whom they appear and the purpose served.

Key Terms
الناقض للعادة
معجزة
كرامة
معونة
إهانة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All supernatural acts are miracles.
Correction: The passage shows that supernatural acts can be assistance, charisma, or humiliation, not just miracles; the agent determines the type.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the four types of violations of custom?
A) Mu'jiza, Karama, Ma'una, Ihanah
B) Mu'jiza, Karama, Ihanah only
C) Only Mu'jiza and Karama
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
Violations of custom are classified into four categories based on the agent: miracle for prophets, charisma for saints, assistance for believers, and humiliation for sorcerers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of the four types do you most hope your own unusual experiences belong to? Are you seeking humbly to be a recipient of divine assistance, or are you secretly wishing for a miracle to validate yourself? Commit to being content with whatever honor Allah grants, even if it is unseen assistance.
?
Have you ever been tempted to claim a supernatural event for yourself or someone else to gain status? The passage warns that such events can be a humiliation. Examine your heart: are you using spiritual experiences to feed your ego? Resolve to attribute all good to Allah and to remain silent about personal favors.
?
The passage says that even a sorcerer can bring about violations of custom, but it ends in humiliation. How does this reshape your understanding of power? Are you more concerned with the external sign or with the inner state of the one through whom it appears? Ask Allah to protect you from seeking power that leads to humiliation.
